## Upgrade suggestions

- **Fire `listing_price_invalid` from the create/edit item cost fields too** — `app/create.tsx` silently nulls an unparseable cost (`Number.isNaN` check) and the edit sheet does the same; routing those branches through `classifyInvalidPrice` with a `source` prop would show whether price-entry friction is marketplace-specific or app-wide.

- **Surface the invalid reason in the toast copy** — the classifier now knows WHY the price failed ("empty" vs "unparseable" vs "non_positive"), but the user still sees the generic `marketplacePriceInvalid`. Per-reason i18n messages ("Enter a price" / "Numbers only — use a dot for decimals" / "Price must be above zero") would convert the same signal the analytics captures into actionable UX.

- **Auto-recover comma decimals at submit time** — `sanitize()` already normalises commas while typing, but a pasted "12,50" can still reach `parseCurrencyValue` unsanitised (programmatic setState, platform paste quirks). Running the submit value through `sanitize()` before parsing would eliminate the very failure mode the new event is instrumented to measure — the event then verifies the fix empirically.

- **Add a `mode` prop to `listing_price_invalid`** — today the event only fires from sell-mode, but if trade listings ever gain an optional value field the reason taxonomy stays reusable; registering `mode` now (always "sell") keeps historical rows comparable once a second mode appears.

- **Property-test the classifier/parser lock-step in CI** — the structural pin catches gate-shape edits, but a tiny fuzz test (random numeric/garbage strings, assert `classifyInvalidPrice(x) === null` ⇔ `parseCurrencyValue(x) !== null`) would catch semantic drift too. Needs `parseCurrencyValue` promoted to a node-pure module first (it currently lives in the react-native component file — same extraction already suggested for `sanitize()`).

- **Add the categorical `relationship` prop to `chat_opened` too** — `listing_claimed` now carries both the boolean and the `sellerRelationship` bucket, but `chat_opened` still only sends `withFriend`. Mirroring the additive upgrade (`relationship: relationshipForAnalytics(...)`) would let Power BI compare "chats with people I follow" vs "stranger DMs" with the same slicer as the marketplace funnel.

- **Adopt `relationshipForAnalytics` in the profile screen's relationship UI switch** — `app/profile/[id].tsx` branches on the full 6-state `ProfileRelationship` for button labels, but several branches collapse to the same coarse treatment. Auditing whether the UI can consume the 3-way bucket for its non-handshake branches would shrink the switch and keep UX + analytics vocabulary aligned.

- **Fire `friend_request_accepted` with `targetRelationshipBefore`** — the queued friend-request-accepted task can now lean on the bucket helper: recording what the relationship was before acceptance ("following" vs "stranger") answers whether follows convert to friendships, closing the loop the 3-way bucket was built for.

- **Type `getRelationship`'s return usage through the helper module** — call sites destructure `getRelationship` from `useSocial()` and pass its result straight to the helpers; a `bucketRelationshipFor(userId, getRelationship)` convenience (or a `useAnalyticsRelationship(userId)` hook) would collapse the two-call chain at every site and keep future events one-liners.

- **Guard the bucket vocabulary in the Power BI docs** — `sellerRelationship`'s three values ("friend" / "following" / "stranger") are now part of the reporting contract, but the schema doc only lists prop KEYS. Extending `generate-powerbi-schema-doc.ts` to render enumerated value sets for categorical props (sourced from exported const tuples) would stop a silent rename from breaking saved report filters.

- **Fire `listing_dropped` on unmount-with-open-sheet too** — today the event only fires through `closeListingSheet()`; navigating back (hardware back on Android pops the route, not the modal on web) with the sheet open and a dirty draft is invisible. A `useEffect` cleanup that checks `listingSheetOpen && isListingDraftDirty(...)` at unmount would close the last abandon path, reusing the same helpers.

- **Add a `fieldsTouched` count prop to `listing_dropped`** — the dirty gate already knows WHICH fields deviate; returning `{ dirty, touchedCount }` from `isListingDraftDirty` (or a sibling `countListingDraftDeviations`) and registering a numeric `touchedCount` prop would let Power BI separate "typed one char and bailed" from "filled everything then abandoned" — different UX problems.

- **Persist the abandoned draft for one session** — a user who filled price + notes and accidentally tapped the backdrop loses everything. Keeping the last dropped draft in component state (or AsyncStorage keyed by item id) and pre-filling on the next `openListingSheet` would convert some of the drop-offs the new event is about to measure; the event then doubles as the success metric for the fix.

- **Route the currency reset through the user's preferred currency instead of hard-coded USD** — `openListingSheet` now (correctly) no longer persists USD, but it still resets the picker to USD rather than `getDefaultCurrencyForLanguage(language)` / the stored preference the edit sheet uses. Aligning the two sheets' defaults (and updating `LISTING_DRAFT_DEFAULTS` to take the resolved default as input) would remove a pointless re-pick for non-USD users — and the dirty gate would stop counting "changed currency back to their own" as filled-in intent.

- **Backdrop-dismiss confirmation for dirty drafts** — mirroring the `listing_dropped` gate: when `isListingDraftDirty(...)`, a backdrop tap could show a small "Discard listing draft?" confirm instead of silently closing (deliberate Cancel button stays one-tap). The helper is already pure/shared, so the confirm and the analytics event stay in lock-step by construction.

- **Widen the PII key rule with a deliberate boolean-prefix escape hatch** — `isPiiPropKey("hasDescription")` is true because the token "description" is denied, which blocks registering summary booleans like `hasDescription`/`hasNote` even though a boolean can't carry free text. A narrow, documented rule ("`has`-prefixed keys whose remaining tokens name a field are boolean summaries, allowed") plus a taxonomy test pinning that such props are only ever fed literal `true`/`false` would unblock the `item_added.hasDescription` funnel prop that `summarisePayload` already derives.

- **Adopt `summarisePayload` in the future `listing_created.hasPrice` derivation** — `app/item/[id].tsx` hand-rolls `hasPrice` from the parsed currency value. Extending the helper's input with `price?: number | null` (deriving `hasPrice: Number.isFinite(price) && price > 0`) would fold the last hand-rolled has-X boolean into the one tested derivation module.

- **Feed `summarisePayload` the whole `CollectableItem` at call sites** — the helper's structural input (`photos`/`coverPhoto`/`description`) is deliberately loose, so `summarisePayload(activeItem)` already type-checks. A future `item_updated` event could pass the item verbatim and pick the registered keys, keeping call sites one-liners; a small test pinning `CollectableItem` assignability to the input type would lock the ergonomics in.

- **Unify `isNonBlank` across `lib/analytics-helpers.ts` and other trim-checks** — the private `isNonBlank` duplicates trim-and-check logic that also appears in `lib/privacy-page.ts`, form validation (`title.trim()` gates), and the cover-photo checks. Promoting it to `lib/string-helpers.ts` with adoption tests would follow the `isWithinDuration` promotion pattern shipped 2026-07-11.

- **Add an `item_added.hasCost` funnel prop** — `app/create.tsx` already computes `parsedCost`; registering a `hasCost` boolean (non-PII: cost is a number the user typed, but the boolean only says whether one exists) would let Power BI slice "do users who track prices retain better" — the exact analysis the marketplace funnel needs, derivable via the same `summarisePayload` extension as `hasPrice`.

- **Promote `__resetSentryRateLimitForTests()` out of the now-redundant per-suite hooks** — with the global `beforeEach` in `__tests__/test-globals.ts` calling `__resetSentryForTests()` (which itself calls `rateLimiter.reset()`) before every test, the remaining `beforeEach(() => __resetSentryRateLimitForTests())` in `sentry-rate-limit.test.ts` and `sentry-test-error.test.ts` are dead weight. A follow-up could drop them (and the `__resetSentryRateLimitForTests` import where it becomes unused) so the rate-limit reset lives in exactly one place, mirroring the SDK-cache reset consolidation just shipped.

- **Add `__resetAnalyticsForTests` to the global bootstrap** — the docstring in `test-globals.ts` already lists analytics as the next module-cache reset to fold in. If `lib/analytics.ts` (or wherever `trackEvent`'s window/queue state lives) exposes a node-safe reset, wiring it into the same global `beforeEach` (static import if node-safe, `require.cache` peek if it drags in RN peers) would give the analytics suites the same zero-boilerplate isolation the Sentry suites now have.

- **Assert cross-file test isolation structurally in `lint:ci`** — a `scripts/check-test-isolation.ts` that greps `__tests__/sentry-*.test.ts` and fails if any file re-introduces a local `beforeEach(() => __resetSentryForTests())` would lock in the consolidation: today nothing stops a future PR from re-adding the per-suite hook and silently masking a broken global bootstrap. Same shape as the existing `check-inline-hex.ts` guard.

- **Document the `--import` tsconfig-path caveat in `test-globals.ts` (or a `docs/testing.md`)** — this task surfaced that modules loaded through Node's `--import` preload do NOT resolve tsconfig `@/*` aliases (they must use relative specifiers), unlike the test files themselves. A one-line note next to the `../lib/sentry` import would save the next engineer the debug cycle of a confusing `Cannot find module '@/lib/...'` from the bootstrap.

- **Make `test-globals.test.ts`'s functional leak-check generic** — the new "boot ready → next test starts fresh" pattern is a reusable proof that the global `beforeEach` fires cross-test. Extracting a tiny `assertGlobalResetFires(bootFn, isReadyFn)` helper would let the future analytics/realtime resets ship with the same one-liner regression guard instead of re-rolling the two-test dance each time.

- **Add a `npm run lint:fonts` guard mirroring `lint:hex`** — the new `__tests__/fonts-assets.test.ts` proves no unreferenced `.ttf` ships today, but a fresh font re-download re-adds the whole variable-weight family and only fails when the test suite runs. A dedicated `scripts/check-font-assets.ts` (same shape as `check-inline-hex.ts`) wired into `lint:ci` would fail fast in the lint stage and print exactly which orphan `.ttf` files to delete.

- **Flatten `assets/fonts/*/static/` into `assets/fonts/`** — the six kept weights still sit two folders deep (`Syne/static/…`, `DM_Sans/static/…`) because that's how the download unzipped. Moving them to a flat `assets/fonts/Syne-Bold.ttf` layout and updating the six `require()` paths in `app/_layout.tsx` removes the now-pointless `static/` nesting and makes the `require` block read cleaner; the `fonts-assets` test's expected-path list is the single place to update in lockstep.

- **Convert the kept `.ttf` faces to `.woff2` for the web bundle** — the app deploys to GitHub Pages, where `.woff2` is ~40% smaller than `.ttf` and universally supported. A build-time `scripts/convert-fonts.ts` (or a platform-split `useFonts` map that loads `.woff2` on web and `.ttf` on native) would shave the six embedded faces off the 4.24 MB web entry bundle without touching native builds.

- **Assert `navIconInactive` resolves to `#bbb0a6` in a theme test** — the design fixed the inactive nav-icon colour at `#bbb0a6`, but it now lives behind `theme.navIconInactive` in `components/use-app-theme`. A tiny structural test that reads the theme module and asserts the light-theme `navIconInactive` literal guards the design constant the same way the hex-lint guards the palette, so a future theme refactor can't silently drift the nav colour.

- **Preload the display font before the first hero paint** — `app/_layout.tsx` returns `null` until `useFonts` resolves, so on a cold web load the whole tree is blank rather than showing the skeleton. Rendering the `<Screen>`+`<Skeleton>` shell (with a system-font fallback) while fonts load, then swapping in `Syne`/`DM Sans` once ready, would remove the blank-flash and let the already-built skeleton states do their job during font fetch too.

- **Long-press the "Delivery confirmed" pill for the absolute date** — the new seller pill shows a relative date ("Delivery confirmed 2 days ago"). Mirroring the listing-detail `formatAbsoluteDate` tooltip pattern (long-press → `toast.info(formatAbsoluteDate(arrivedAt))`) would let a seller see the exact confirmation timestamp for dispute records, consistent with the item-cost tooltip already shipped.

- **Live-update the "Delivery confirmed {when}" label via `useNow()`** — the relative date is frozen at the last render of `app/marketplace.tsx`. Threading `useNow()` into `ListingCard` (or a `useTimestampWithTick` helper) would keep "Delivery confirmed 5 minutes ago" advancing without a manual refresh, the same upgrade already queued for the "Listed {when}" header.

- **Surface the delivery-confirmed signal on listing detail for the seller** — the My-sales card now shows "Delivery confirmed {when}", but `app/listing/[id].tsx` shows nothing equivalent to the seller of a sold listing. A matching banner under the sold pill (gated on `isSeller && arrivedAt != null`) would close the card/detail parity gap, reusing the same `relativeDateLabel(t("marketplaceDeliveryConfirmed"), …)` composition.

- **Extract a shared `DeliveryStatusPill` component** — the marketplace card now has three near-identical pill shapes (soldTo, delivery-confirmed, received badge) with copy-pasted `StyleSheet` blocks. A small `components/delivery-status-pill.tsx` taking `{ tone, label }` would de-duplicate the styling and give a single place to tune the warm-palette tokens.

- **Track `listing_received` analytics with `daysToArrival`** — `handleMarkReceived` flips state but emits no event, so the claim→delivery funnel and average delivery latency are invisible in PostHog/Power BI. Adding `trackEvent("listing_received", { daysToArrival })` to the typed union in `lib/analytics-events.ts` would let the BI dashboards measure confirmation rate now that both buyer and seller surfaces exist.

- **Mark-received undo affordance** — `markListingReceived` is idempotent and irreversible (the first `arrivedAt` stamp wins). A buyer who taps "Mark as received" by mistake has no recovery. Add a short-lived undo: surface an "Undo" action on the success toast (or a long-press on the "Received" badge) that clears `arrivedAt` within a grace window, backed by a `clearListingArrived(id)` context method gated on the same buyer/sold checks.

- **Optimistic-vs-server reconciliation for receipt** — the buyer UI flips to "Received" purely from local state today; once the `arrived_at` cloud-sync sub-task lands, a stale local stamp could disagree with the server. Add a tiny LWW merge (server `arrivedAt` wins, mirroring the BE-22c premium pattern) so a confirmation made on device A converges on device B without a full refresh.

- **Seller-facing "awaiting confirmation" pill** — the seller's My-sales card shows "Transferred" the moment a buyer claims, but nothing distinguishes *claimed-but-not-yet-arrived* from *delivery-confirmed*. A neutral "Awaiting confirmation" pill while `soldAt != null && arrivedAt == null` (then the "Delivery confirmed {when}" indicator from the next sub-task) would give sellers a clear two-stage delivery signal.

- **`relativeDateLabel`-based "Received {when}" on the purchase card** — the buyer's "Received" badge is a bare label. Threading the stamped `arrivedAt` through the existing `relativeDateLabel` helper ("Received 2 days ago") matches the seller-side "Delivery confirmed {when}" treatment and gives the buyer a sense of how long ago they confirmed, at no extra i18n cost beyond one `marketplaceReceivedAt` key.

- **Analytics event on receipt confirmation** — `listing_claimed` is tracked at buy time but there's no `listing_received` event, so the claim→delivery funnel is invisible in PostHog/Power BI. Emitting `trackEvent("listing_received", { daysToArrival })` from `handleMarkReceived` would let the BI dashboards measure average delivery latency and confirmation rate — a natural addition to the existing typed event union in `lib/analytics-events.ts`.

- **SEC-21 follow-up: a `.github/SECURITY.md` symlink/move so GitHub surfaces the policy tab** — GitHub only shows the "Security policy" community-health link when `SECURITY.md` is at the repo root, `docs/`, or `.github/`. Root works today; if the repo ever adopts a `.github/`-centric convention, keep one canonical copy and a CI check that the policy file is discoverable.

- **SEC-21 follow-up: a doc-link integrity test for SECURITY.md** — the runbook references concrete env-var names (`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED`, …) and helper files (`lib/runtime-config-gate.ts`, `assertCaller`). A test that cross-checks every `EXPO_PUBLIC_*`/Edge-secret name mentioned in SECURITY.md against the real `README-DEPLOY.md` table + `supabase/functions/` `Deno.env.get` calls would catch the doc drifting out of sync when a secret is renamed.

- **A scripted `npm run rotate-secrets` checklist** — the incident runbook is prose; turning the rotation steps into an interactive `tsx scripts/incident-rotate.ts` that prints each numbered step, the exact `supabase secrets set …` commands, and pauses for confirmation would cut mean-time-to-rotate during a real incident when nobody wants to parse Markdown under pressure.

- **Wire SECURITY.md into the issue/PR templates** — add a one-line "Found a security issue? See SECURITY.md — do not file a public issue" banner to the bug-report issue template and the PR template, so the private-reporting channel is discoverable at the moment someone is about to disclose publicly.

- **Automate the global-session-revocation step** — step 1 of the runbook (rotate the JWT secret to invalidate all tokens) is high-blast-radius and manual. A small Edge Function (service-role, admin-gated) that calls `auth.admin.signOut(userId, 'global')` for a target user — or all users — would give a surgical revocation option short of rotating the project JWT secret, and is testable with the existing `assertCaller` harness.

- **SEC-20 next: an ESLint `no-console` rule (allow `warn`/`error`) wired into `lint:ci`** — `lib/safe-log.ts` gives a clean `devLog.debug` channel, but nothing *prevents* a future `console.log(body)` from being reintroduced; the new structural test only guards `supabase-profiles.ts`. A repo-wide `no-console: ["error", { allow: ["warn", "error"] }]` ESLint rule (with a narrow override for `lib/safe-log.ts`/analytics/sentry) would make the gate enforced at author time, not just one file's test.

- **SEC-20 follow-up: route the analytics/sentry init-failure logs through `devLog` too** — `lib/analytics.ts` and `lib/sentry.ts` still `console.warn`/`console.info` raw `err` objects in production. An SDK init error is low-risk, but forwarding them through `devLog.debug` (or a new `devLog.warn`) keeps a single, redaction-aware logging surface and silences them in prod where the user can do nothing with them anyway.

- **SEC-20 follow-up: a global redacting `console` shim for production web** — for defence-in-depth against third-party libs (supabase-js, expo) logging payloads, install a thin `console.log`/`console.debug` override in the web entry that pipes through `redactForLog` when `!__DEV__`. Opt-in via an env flag so it never interferes with intentional diagnostics.

- **Add a `devLog.warn`/`devLog.error` pair so prod error logs are auto-redacted** — today only `debug` is gated; the always-on `console.error("[updateRemoteItem] FAILED", status)` and similar still bypass `redactForLog`. Extending the `DevLogger` interface with `warn`/`error` that *always* fire but redact their object args would let every cloud-write failure path log safely without each call site remembering to redact.

- **Property-based fuzz test for `redactForLog`** — the redactor walks arbitrary nested user payloads; a fast-check style generator that builds random objects mixing sensitive and safe keys and asserts (a) no sensitive *value* survives and (b) every safe value is preserved would harden it against edge cases (Symbol keys, getters, prototype-polluted objects) the 6 hand-written cases miss.

- **SEC-4 follow-up: one-shot warn when the runtime config is silently ignored** — after the SEC-4 gate, a QA engineer who set `collectables-supabase-runtime-config` in a production build now gets *silently* fed the build-time secrets with no hint why their override didn't take. A single `console.warn` (dev-only, never prod) inside `parseRuntimeConfig` when `readLocalStorage(RUNTIME_CONFIG_KEY)` is non-null but `isRuntimeConfigOverrideAllowed()` is false would make the gate's behaviour discoverable without leaking anything.

- **SEC-4 follow-up: surface `isRuntimeConfigOverrideAllowed` in the dev menu** — `app/_layout.tsx` already registers `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` as a DevMenu action. Add a sibling read-only DevMenu line that prints whether the override is currently honoured (dev vs QA-opt-in vs off) so QA can confirm the gate state on-device instead of reasoning about `__DEV__`.

- **SEC-4 follow-up: fold the new env into the runtime-config-parity scan** — the pending `__tests__/runtime-config-parity.test.ts` suggestion (scan `lib/*-config.ts` for env vars vs `README-DEPLOY.md`) should also cover `EXPO_PUBLIC_ALLOW_RUNTIME_SUPABASE_CONFIG` even though it lives in `lib/runtime-config-gate.ts`, not a `*-config.ts` file — widen the glob to `lib/*-gate.ts` so the parity guard catches it.

- **SEC-7 next: centralise the OAuth hash scrub into a `scrubAuthUrl()` helper** — SEC-7 (next task) will strip tokens from `window.location.hash` in `app/auth/callback.tsx`. Extract the scrub into a pure `lib/auth-url.ts` helper so it's node-testable and reusable if a second redirect entry point is ever added, rather than inlining `history.replaceState` in the screen.

- **Fold all SEC gate checks into a single `lib/security-gates.ts`** — SEC-4's `runtime-config-gate.ts` is the first of several env/dev gates the security roadmap will add (SEC-15 CSP toggle, SEC-20 prod-log strip). A small aggregator that re-exports each gate keeps the "what's allowed in prod vs dev" surface in one auditable file, mirroring the proposed `lib/runtime-config.ts` config aggregator. — adding UPDATE means every per-field edit (BE-9's moddatetime trigger fires on each save) now pokes `refreshTick` → a full delta pull. A trailing ~250ms debounce on the poke (one timer for collections+items) would collapse a rapid edit burst into one refresh; pairs naturally with the existing "coalesce rapid BE-18 pokes" suggestion now that UPDATE roughly triples the event rate.

- **Drop the wasted coerce on DELETE frames in the realtime sync handlers** — `subscribeToOwnCollections`/`subscribeToOwnItems` still run `coerceCollectionRow`/`coerceItemRow` on every event including DELETE, where the row is just `{ id }` and the poke consumer ignores the result entirely. Skipping the coerce when the frame is a DELETE (or, better, emitting a lightweight `{ id, kind }` instead of a full coerced domain object) trims per-event work on the hot path; the consumer only needs the poke.

- **Realtime DELETE smoke test on the supabase-test Docker CI** — the BE-19 `REPLICA IDENTITY FULL` + publication migration is only asserted by source-grep today. A pgTAP/integration test that deletes a row and asserts the postgres-changes DELETE payload carries the full pre-image (not just the PK) would catch a regression where someone resets replica identity back to default and silently breaks filtered DELETE delivery.

- **Symmetric `onRemoved` for collections/items shared via social** — BE-19 wired DELETE removal for marketplace listings; the social/subscribed-collections path (`subscribedCollections` in collections-context) still only learns of an unshared/deleted collection on the next `fetchCollectionById` refresh. Threading a DELETE→remove-by-id through the social realtime channel would close the symmetric gap for viewers of someone else's collection.

- **WAL-cost guardrail for `REPLICA IDENTITY FULL`** — full replica identity logs the entire old row on every UPDATE/DELETE, which is fine for the low-write user tables today but would bite if `items` ever takes bulk writes. A short doc note (or a `pg_stat`-based alert) recording the expected WAL overhead, plus a fallback plan (index-backed `REPLICA IDENTITY USING INDEX` on just the filter columns), would make the trade-off explicit before it scales.

- **BE-18 follow-up: replace the realtime "poke" with direct upsert for own collections/items** — the BE-18 wiring bumps `refreshTick` on every own-row INSERT, which re-runs the full `syncFromCloud` delta pull (two REST round-trips) for a single new row. Now that the wrapper already coerces the row to a typed `Collection`/`CollectableItem`, the context could upsert that payload straight into `localCollections`/`localItems` (mirroring how `marketplace-context` upserts the listing), saving the round-trip and rendering the cross-device add instantly. Keep the delta pull as the reconnect/catch-up path.

- **Add a status-aware reconnect catch-up for BE-18 subscriptions** — `subscribeShared` already exposes an `onStatusChange(connected)` arg (used by chat). Threading it into `subscribeToOwnCollections`/`subscribeToOwnItems`/`subscribeToFriendRequests` so a transition back to `connected` pokes `refreshTick` once would close the "events dropped while the socket was down" gap that INSERT-only realtime can't cover on its own.

- **Coalesce rapid BE-18 pokes with a short debounce** — a bulk import or a multi-item paste fires N INSERTs in quick succession, each currently bumping `refreshTick` → N delta pulls. A ~250ms trailing debounce on the poke (a `useRef` timer cleared on unmount) would collapse a burst into a single refresh without hurting the single-add latency case.

- **Expose a `getRegistryStats()` debug helper** — `realtime-channel-registry` tracks per-topic subscriber counts internally; a small read-only accessor (topic → handler count) wired behind a dev-only screen or `console` would make it observable that BE-18's per-user topics actually ref-count down to zero on sign-out, catching channel leaks before they ship.

- **pgTAP/integration coverage for the BE-18 realtime filters** — the wrapper's `owner_user_id=eq.${userId}` / `created_by_user_id=eq.${userId}` / friend-request direction filters are only asserted by source-grep today. A Docker pgTAP (or a fake-`RealtimeClient` integration) test that publishes a row for user A and asserts user B's channel does NOT receive it would lock in the RLS-aligned scoping that keeps one user's realtime stream private.

- **Route `activatePremium`/`cancelPremium` through the server (BE-22c follow-up)** — now that load-time `validate` is server-authoritative, a *locally* activated premium (the Activate button only mutates local `PremiumState`) is silently downgraded on the next authed load, because `mergePremiumState` lets the server's `isPremium=false` win. Wiring `activatePremium` to `cloudValidatePremium("activate")` (and a future `cancel` action) before/after the optimistic local flip closes that gap so an activation actually survives a reload.

- **Re-validate premium on app foreground / session refresh, not just initial load** — the BE-22c server pull fires once per `storageKey` mount; a long-lived session whose `current_period_end` lapses mid-use keeps gating paid features until the next cold start. A lightweight `AppState` "active" listener (or hooking the auth `TOKEN_REFRESHED` event) that re-runs `cloudValidatePremium("validate")` would expire a churned subscription promptly without a relaunch.

- **Surface a "couldn't verify premium" soft indicator when the server pull returns null** — `cloudValidatePremium` returning `null` (offline/transient) is intentionally invisible so a payer isn't downgraded, but it also means a *stale* cache is shown with no signal. A subtle "last verified …" timestamp on the settings premium card (set only on a successful validate) would let a user tell a genuinely-active entitlement from a never-server-confirmed local one.

- **De-dupe the premium load + server-pull into a single reducer transition** — the load effect now calls `setState` twice (cache, then merged server truth), so a fast server response can cause a brief `false→true` flicker for a payer whose cache was empty. Folding both into one `setState` (await the validate before the first commit when a token is already present, with a short timeout fallback to the cache) would remove the flicker without sacrificing the offline-keeps-cache guarantee.

- **Integration test for premium-context server-truth merge against a fake `cloudValidatePremium` (BE-35 seed)** — the BE-22c wiring is only structurally guarded; a render test (or a thin extraction of the merge step into a pure `applyServerValidation(prev, validation)` helper) that asserts a server `isPremium=false` downgrades a cached payer while a `null` preserves the cache would lock the LWW semantics that the regex test can't observe at runtime.

- **Idempotency / replay guard on `validate-premium` activate (BE-22b follow-up)** — `action:"activate"` is idempotent only against an *already-active* row; two near-simultaneous activates on a *lapsed* row both pass the `isActive` gate and both upsert, the last-writer's `activated_at` winning. Threading an `Idempotency-Key` header (or a conditional upsert that only resets `activated_at` when the row wasn't active) would make repeated taps on the "Activate premium" button deterministic.

- **A real IAP/receipt verification step before `validate-premium` activates** — today `action:"activate"` trusts any authenticated caller, so the server is authoritative about *storage* but not about *payment*. Wiring the function to verify an App Store / Play / Stripe receipt (passed in the body) before flipping `status='active'` closes the "any signed-in user can mint premium" gap that the BE-22a table was introduced to fix.

- **`pg_cron` nightly expiry sweep for lapsed subscriptions (pairs with BE-27)** — `validate-premium` only expires a row when the owner happens to call "validate"; a churned user who never opens the app keeps `status='active'` (with a past `current_period_end`) forever in the table. A nightly `UPDATE subscriptions SET status='expired' WHERE status='active' AND current_period_end < now()` keeps server-side analytics/entitlement queries honest without waiting for a client round-trip.

- **Emit a `premium_validated` / `premium_expired` analytics event from the function** — the Edge Function is the one place that knows the *server* truth about an entitlement transition (active→expired on lazy expiry, or a fresh activate). Forwarding that to the analytics sink (like `analytics-mirror`) would give a churn/renewal funnel that the client-side `premiumActivated` toast can't, since the client never sees the lazy server expiry.

- **Integration test exercising `cloudValidatePremium` against a fake `fetcher`/`tokenProvider` (BE-35 seed)** — `cloudValidatePremium` is currently only structurally guarded; a node test that mocks `fetcher` to return a `{ isPremium, activatedAt, expiresAt }` body and asserts the wrapper POSTs the right URL/body, coerces via `parseValidation`, and returns `null` on `!res.ok`/no-token would catch a regression the regex tests can't (e.g. a future refactor that drops the token guard). This is the BE-22 slice of the broader BE-35 "fake fetcher for every cloud wrapper" item.

- **Cap `cloudAcceptFriendRequest` retries on a hard server error (BE-21 follow-up)** — the wrapper treats `res.ok || res.status===409` as terminal, but a `500` (e.g. `function misconfigured`, or the function not yet deployed) returns `false` forever, so the `accept-request` mutation re-flushes on every remount until the function is fixed. A bounded retry/backoff (or surfacing a one-time "couldn't accept, try again later" toast after N failures) would stop a silently-undeployed function from pinning the queue.

- **Replace the `accept-friend-request` self-accept guard with a server-side dedup of the "accept your own outgoing request" case** — the function 400s when `fromUserId === toUserId`, but it doesn't catch the subtler "I already sent A→B, now I 'accept' B (who never requested me)" — `accept_friend_request` correctly raises `P0002` (no inbound), so the client should distinguish 409-no-inbound from a true accept and not optimistically flip the local relationship to `friend` in that case (today `addFriend` always inserts the local row first).

- **pgTAP test for `accept_friend_request` concurrency** — add a `supabase/tests/` case that opens two sessions, both accepting the same inbound request, and asserts exactly one reverse row exists + no error leaks; the `FOR UPDATE` lock is the whole point of BE-21 but only the structural SQL shape is currently guarded (the Docker-backed supabase-test CI can actually exercise the lock).

- **Emit a distinct `friend_accepted` analytics event on the accept path** — `addFriend` fires `friend_requested` for both a fresh request and an accept, so the funnel can't tell "sent" from "accepted". Now that `addFriend` already computes `isAccept`, branching the `trackEvent` name (and threading it through `analytics-shapes`) is a one-line behavioural win for retention analysis.

- **Realtime-propagate the reverse `friend_requests` INSERT to the sender** — when B accepts, A's client only learns it became "friends" on its next pull/remount because the realtime subscription filters INSERTs narrowly. Subscribing to `friend_requests` INSERTs where `to_user_id = me` (BE-19 UPDATE/DELETE work is adjacent) would flip A's relationship chip to "friend" live, matching the marketplace claim's realtime UX.

- **Make the `SyncStatusPill` tappable to force a flush (and show last-synced time)** — the BE-16 pill is read-only; a tap could bump the shared `refreshTick`/re-run the flush effects and, when the queue is empty, briefly show "Synced just now" before fading. Turns a passive indicator into an explicit "retry now" affordance for users on flaky connections who don't want to wait for the next remount.

- **Animate the pill in/out instead of a hard mount/unmount** — `SyncStatusPill` returns `null` the instant `total` hits 0, so a fast flush makes it flicker. A short `LayoutAnimation`/`Animated` fade (or a 1.5s "Synced" grace state) would make the transition feel intentional rather than glitchy, matching how mainstream apps surface sync state.

- **Surface a per-context breakdown on long-press** — the pill collapses collections + social + chat into one number. A long-press tooltip ("2 items, 1 friend request, 3 messages") reusing the same three `pendingSyncCount` values would help a power user understand *what* is stuck without opening devtools, and is a pure-render addition (no new context plumbing).

- **Add a `pendingSyncCount`-aware "don't quit yet" guard on web** — when `total > 0`, register a `beforeunload` handler warning the user that unsynced edits will be retried next launch but aren't in the cloud yet. The count already lives in context; this closes the data-loss-perception gap when someone closes the tab mid-flush.

- **Unit-test the chat `pendingSyncCount` memo against a real `pendingByChatId` snapshot** — the BE-16 structural test pins the wiring regex, but nothing asserts that two messages across two chats yield `2`. A small React-Testing-Library (or reducer-extraction) test mirroring the other context suites would lock the multi-group sum behaviourally, not just structurally.

- **Network-reconnect trigger for the social/collections flush effects** — both flush effects currently re-fire only on `ready`/`user` (and `refreshTick` for collections), so a queue parked while offline isn't retried until the next remount or manual refresh. Subscribing to an online/offline signal (NetInfo on native, `window.online` on web) and bumping a shared `refreshTick` would make reconnect re-deliver parked writes automatically, closing the main gap left by BE-13c/13d.

- **Unit-test the `SocialProvider` queue wiring, not just the pure module** — `__tests__/pending-social.test.ts` covers `lib/pending-social.ts` exhaustively, but nothing asserts the *context* enqueues on a failed `sendFriendRequest`, dequeues on success, or flushes on reconnect. A React-Testing-Library suite with mocked cloud fns (mirroring the existing context tests) would pin the integration the structural tests can't.

- **Generalise the social-graph "deleted profile IDs" into a real tombstone + soft-delete sweep (BE-15)** — `deletedProfileIds` is an ad-hoc client-only tombstone list; the BE-13 engine and a `deleted_at` column could turn it into a uniform LWW soft-delete applied across collections/items/profiles, so an admin delete propagates through the same queue instead of a bespoke filtered-out set.

- **Cap and age out persisted pending queues** — `pendingSocial`/`pendingCollections`/`pendingItems` grow unbounded while offline and are serialised to AsyncStorage on every change. A max-size guard (drop oldest, surface a toast) plus a per-entry `queuedAt` so a write that never succeeds is eventually abandoned would prevent a corrupt/permanently-rejected mutation from wedging the flush loop forever.

- **pgTAP cases asserting the BE-7 CHECKs actually reject bad values** — `20260619_integrity_checks.sql` adds the visibility/condition/no-self CHECKs, but no test inserts `visibility='draft'` / `condition='mint'` / a self-request and expects `23514` (check_violation). A `03_integrity_checks.sql` pgTAP (or cases in `01_core_tables_rls.sql`) would lock in the enforcement, mirroring how `02_fk_cascade.sql` proves the FK behaviour.

- **Promote `visibility` and `condition` to native PostgreSQL ENUM types** — the values are validated by string CHECKs in two places (base schema inline + the BE-7 backfill). A `CREATE TYPE collection_visibility AS ENUM (...)` / `item_condition AS ENUM (...)` would centralise the allowed set, give the REST API typed columns, and remove the risk of the CHECK list drifting from `lib/types.ts`. Pair with a `pg_enum`-vs-TS-union parity test.

- **Parity test: DB CHECK enums vs the TS literal unions** — `lib/types.ts` defines `visibility`/`condition` as TS unions and the migrations repeat the same literals in SQL. A test that extracts both and asserts they match would catch a future value added to one side but not the other (e.g. a new `condition: "poor"`), the same drift risk the SEC-ADMIN-1 column list calls out.

- **Generalise the BE-6/BE-7 "ensure constraint exists" guards into one helper migration** — both migrations hand-roll `DO $$ … IF NOT EXISTS (pg_constraint …) $$` blocks. A small reusable `pg_temp.ensure_check(table, name, expr)` / `ensure_unique(...)` (like BE-6's `ensure_cascade_fk`) would shrink future integrity migrations and keep the guard logic consistent.

- **Audit chat/marketplace tables for the same missing-constraint gap** — BE-6/BE-7 only normalised the four core tables. `chat_messages`, `chat_reads`, `marketplace_listings`, `marketplace_transfers` were also created from their own migrations; a one-pass review confirming their CHECKs/uniques/FKs are present on the live (hand-created) project — and a backfill migration if any are missing — would close the gap class entirely rather than table-by-table.

- **pgTAP assertion that every core FK actually carries `confdeltype = 'c'`** — BE-6's migration sets ON DELETE CASCADE, and `02_fk_cascade.sql` proves the *behaviour*, but nothing asserts the catalog metadata directly. A small pgTAP case querying `pg_constraint.confdeltype` for the six core FKs (expecting `'c'`) would catch a future migration that re-adds a FK with the wrong action even before a delete is attempted, mirroring the chat `chat_id_integrity` CHECK test.

- **Generalise the `ensure_cascade_fk` pg_temp helper into a reusable migration snippet** — chat/marketplace tables have their own FKs to `auth.users`/`collections` defined in their migrations; if any were hand-created without CASCADE they'd share BE-6's problem. Extracting the drop-then-readd helper into a documented snippet (or a shared `_helpers.sql` applied first) would let a single follow-up normalise `chat_messages`, `chat_reads`, `marketplace_listings`, and `marketplace_transfers` FKs the same way.

- **CI lint that flags a new `REFERENCES` in a migration without an explicit `ON DELETE` action** — the default `NO ACTION` is exactly the foot-gun BE-6 had to repair. A matcher (mirroring `check-migration-docs`) scanning `supabase/migrations/*.sql` for `REFERENCES … ` clauses lacking an `ON DELETE` would force every future FK to declare its delete behaviour at authoring time.

- **`delete-account` Edge Function integration test against the from-empty CI DB** — BE-25 verifies the cascade in pgTAP, but the actual Edge Function (which calls `auth.admin.deleteUser`) isn't exercised end-to-end. A test invoking the function with a service-role client against the `supabase db start` database would prove the function + FK cascade work together, not just the SQL layer.

- **Schema-drift guard comparing base-schema FKs to the live catalog** — BE-6 exists because the hand-created live tables drifted from the committed schema. A periodic (or CI) check dumping `pg_constraint` delete actions and diffing them against the canonical list in the base-schema migration would surface any future manual dashboard edit that re-introduces drift before it bites a delete path.

- **Lint that fails when any `id:` mint in `lib`/`app` is a non-uuid template literal** — BE-5 fixed items by hand, but the next entity (a new `addX`) could re-introduce a `${slug}-${Date.now()}` server key. A CI matcher (mirroring `check-migration-docs`) flagging `id:` assignments built from template literals on persisted entities — with an allowlist for client-only optimistic ids like the reaction `tmp-` placeholder — would stop the legacy-id class from recurring.

- **Proactively re-upsert ALL legacy-rewritten items, not just on hydrate** — `normalizeOwnItemIds` runs at sign-in hydrate, but an item created offline mid-session before this build won't pass through hydrate. A one-time storage sweep on app launch (migrate-then-persist, gated by a `collectables-item-uuid-migrated-v1` flag) would catch every cached legacy id exactly once and remove the per-hydrate scan cost.

- **Add a pgTAP / structural check that `items.id` rejects a non-uuid insert** — the migration declares `items.id uuid` but nothing asserts a `slug-123` POST is refused (22P02). A pgTAP case in `01_core_tables_rls.sql` (or a new `03_id_integrity.sql`) inserting a bad id and expecting the cast error would lock in BE-5's server-side guarantee, matching the chat `chat_id_integrity` CHECK test.

- **Generalise `normalizeOwnItemIds` into a shared `normalizeOwnEntityIds`** — collections, wishlist items, and future synced entities share the "rewrite my own legacy non-uuid ids" need. Promoting the helper to take an `ownerKey` accessor (so it works for `Collection.ownerUserId` too) and reusing it in the collections hydrate path would pre-empt the same bug class for any entity that predates its uuid fix.

- **Dedupe items by `(collectionId, title, createdAt)` when a legacy and a uuid row both exist** — if a pre-fix item was partially synced under one id and rewritten under a new uuid, a cross-device merge could surface both. A content-hash dedupe in `mergeItemsFromCloud` (keep the uuid-keyed row, drop the legacy-id duplicate) would clean up any straddled rows from the transition.

- **Promote the BE-23 self-check to module load so it fails at cold-start, not first-request** — `assertServiceRoleKey` currently runs inside the request handler, so a misconfigured secret only surfaces when the first call arrives. Hoisting it to top-level module scope (a thrown error there crashes the function boot) makes a swapped key fail the moment the function deploys/cold-starts, which is closer to the task's "fails loudly at deploy" intent and matches how Supabase surfaces boot errors in the dashboard.

- **Add a `lib/check-edge-fn-self-check.ts` lint asserting every `supabase/functions/*/index.ts` imports the claim guard** — the three current functions are wired by hand; a CI lint (mirroring `check-migration-docs`) that fails when a new Edge Function constructs an admin client with `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` without first calling `assertServiceRoleKey` would stop a future function shipping the foot-gun. Pair it with the structural test already in `service-role-claim.test.ts`.

- **Verify the JWT `iss`/`ref` claims match the project, not just `role`** — a service-role key from a *different* Supabase project still carries `role: service_role` and would pass today's check while pointing the admin client at the wrong DB. Decoding `ref` (project ref) and comparing it to the host in `SUPABASE_URL` would catch a cross-project key paste — a subtler misconfiguration than the anon/service swap.

- **Optionally signature-verify the service-role JWT against `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET`** — the current decode is claim-only (we own the secret, so tampering isn't the threat). But if `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` is also a function secret, an HMAC check would additionally catch a *truncated/corrupted* key that happens to still parse as JSON, turning a silent runtime failure into a named config error.

- **Surface a deploy-time smoke test in the functions CI** — add a workflow step (or a `supabase functions serve` + `curl` in the BE-31 Docker harness) that boots each function with a deliberately-wrong `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` (the anon key) and asserts it returns HTTP 500 `misconfigured`, proving the guard fails closed end-to-end rather than only in the structural source-scan test.

- **Land the BE-12b executable pgTAP (`supabase/tests/01_core_tables_rls.sql`) to back the BE-12a structural pins** — the verification test proves the policy *text* is shaped right, but only role-switched pgTAP in the BE-31 Docker harness proves a logged-in stranger actually gets zero rows from a private collection. Seed two synthetic `auth.users`, set `request.jwt.claims`, and assert cross-tenant SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE deny.

- **Generalise the "RLS-enabled-implies-policy-present" check across ALL migrations, not just the core four** — BE-12a hardcodes the four core tables. A repo-wide lint that pairs every `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` with either a `CREATE POLICY` on the same table or an allowlisted default-deny comment (like analytics) would catch a future table that enables RLS and forgets its policy, locking the app out.

- **Add a `USING (true)` / `WITH CHECK (true)` leak lint over `supabase/migrations/*`** — BE-12a only forbids bare-true SELECT policies on the core tables. A blanket check across every migration would flag any accidentally over-broad policy (e.g. a copy-pasted `USING (true)` on a write path) before it ships.

- **Unit-test the SECURITY DEFINER helpers in isolation via pgTAP** — `is_friend`/`is_visible_to`/`can_view_collection`/`is_admin` encode the entire visibility model; seeding friend_requests/collections and asserting their boolean output (no role switching needed) is a cheap, deterministic pgTAP layer that localises a logic bug to the helper rather than a policy.

- **Cross-check the MANUAL-TASKS leak-check SQL against the actual gated tables** — BE-12a asserts the leak check names collections/items/friend_requests, but if a future migration gates a fifth table the doc check won't notice it's missing from the leak-check block. Derive the expected table list from the `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` statements and assert each appears in the documented leak check.

- **Seed `profiles.is_admin = true` for the founder row and retire the client allowlist (BE-11b follow-up)** — now that `social-context` reads `selfProfile.isAdmin`, the `1337antoxa`/email literals in `lib/social-context.tsx` are only an offline fallback. A one-time `UPDATE profiles SET is_admin = true WHERE username = '1337antoxa'` migration (documented in MANUAL-TASKS.md) plus removing the hardcoded literal would stop shipping the admin identity in plaintext to every client.

- **Hydrate `selfProfile` from the cloud on sign-in so the server `is_admin` flag actually wins** — `social-context` derives admin from `profiles`, but if the self row is sourced from the seed/offline cache the new flag is never present and the gate silently falls back to the allowlist. A fetch of the authed user's own profile row (mirroring the bug-2c displayCurrency hydration in `collections-context`) would make the server flag authoritative in practice, not just in code.

- **Add a CI guard that no `*-shapes.ts` body builder writes a REVOKE-protected column** — `upsertProfileBody` correctly omits `is_admin`, but the invariant is only enforced by one structural test. A lint that cross-references columns with `REVOKE UPDATE(...)`/`REVOKE INSERT(...)` in `supabase/migrations/*` against the keys returned by every body builder would catch a future builder that re-adds a server-authoritative column.

- **Extend the schema-parity test (BE-3/BE-37) to assert read-only columns appear in `select`/`DbProfile` but never in a body builder** — parity today only checks columns *exist*; pairing it with the REVOKE list would prove the read path covers `is_admin`/future server columns while the write path excludes them.

- **Surface an admin badge/affordance gated on the synced `isAdmin` flag** — with `UserProfile.isAdmin` now threaded through, the profile/settings UI could show a small "admin" indicator and unlock the delete-profile control consistently, instead of the gate living only inside the `deleteProfile` callback. Keep it behind the same memo so offline fallback still works.

- **Generalise the BE-11a anon/leak RLS check into executable pgTAP (BE-12)** — `__tests__/core-tables-rls-migration.test.ts` only asserts the policy *text* exists; it can't prove a logged-in user actually can't read a stranger's private collection. A `supabase/tests/rls.sql` that `SET ROLE`s to two synthetic users and asserts cross-tenant SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE all deny would run inside the BE-31 scratch-DB harness and catch a policy that's present but wrong.

- **Add a CI lint that every RLS-enabled table has at least one policy (or a documented default-deny)** — `analytics_events` is intentionally policy-less (default-deny), but a future migration that runs `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` and forgets the `CREATE POLICY` would silently lock the app out of a table. A grep-style check pairing each `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` with either a policy or an allowlisted "default-deny" comment would catch that class of outage before merge.

- **Move the `1337antoxa`/email admin allowlist fully server-side once BE-11b lands** — BE-11a added `profiles.is_admin` + `is_admin()` but the client still hardcodes the allowlist in `lib/social-context.tsx`. After BE-11b reads the flag, a one-time seed/migration that sets `is_admin = true` for the founder row (and removing the literal from the bundle) closes the gap where the admin identity ships in plaintext to every client.

- **Add a `search_path`-injection guard test for SECURITY DEFINER functions** — BE-11a pins `SET search_path = public` on all four helpers and the test counts them, but a future definer function added without the pin is a privilege-escalation vector. A structural check that every `SECURITY DEFINER` in `supabase/migrations/*` is accompanied by a `SET search_path` would make the invariant repo-wide, not just for this migration.

- **Wire `is_visible_to`/`can_view_collection` into the app's cloud read path** — the helpers now enforce friend/shared visibility server-side, but the app still sources social collections from `seedSocialCollections` (per CLAUDE.md). A follow-up that fetches friends' collections via the REST API (now safely RLS-gated) would let real shared collections replace seed data without leaking private rows.

- **Have the migration-docs check (BE-32) also flag stale/orphaned MANUAL-TASKS.md sections** — today it only fails when a migration lacks a section. The reverse (a `## <timestamp>_*.sql` H2 whose file was renamed/deleted) leaves dead manual-apply SQL that drifts from reality. Restrict the reverse check to H2s matching the migration-filename pattern so prose sections (Edge Functions, the free-plan setup block) aren't touched.

- **Assert each migration's MANUAL-TASKS section actually contains the applied SQL, not just a heading** — BE-32 only checks a heading exists, so an empty `## 20260601_foo.sql` with no body would pass. A follow-up could require either a fenced ```sql block or a recognised "no manual step" sentinel under each migration heading.

- **Lint that every migration heading's documented SQL stays in sync with the file** — diff the `CREATE TABLE`/`ALTER` statements named in the MANUAL-TASKS section against the actual `.sql` so a migration edited after its doc was written can't silently diverge (e.g. a new column added to the file but never to the manual-apply block).

- **Surface the migration-docs and hex checks as a single `npm run lint:all` aggregate** — `lint:ci` chains tsc + hex + migration-docs + test, but there's no quick "just the static lints" entry point for local pre-commit. A `lint:all` that runs only the fast file-scanning checks would speed the inner loop.

- **Add a git pre-commit hook (husky or a committed `.githooks/`) running `lint:migration-docs` + `lint:hex`** — catching an undocumented migration at commit time is far cheaper than a red CI run minutes later; the checks are sub-second and filesystem-only.

- **Extend the BE-3 parity test to the row-reader shapes (`toUserProfile`/`toCollection`/`toItem` in `lib/supabase-profiles.ts`), not just the writer builders** — BE-3 derives expected columns from the URL/body builders, which covers writes + filters but not every column the app *reads back*. A column that's selected via `select=*` and consumed by a `toX` mapper (e.g. a future `profiles.is_admin`) wouldn't be in the builders, so a missing migration column would slip through. Parsing the `row.<col>` accesses in the `toX` functions and folding them into the parity set would close the read side.

- **Make BE-3 fail on *extra* migration columns too (bidirectional parity)** — the test asserts builder columns ⊆ migration columns, but not the reverse, so a column the migration declares that no builder/reader uses (dead schema) goes unnoticed. An allowlist of server-only columns (`id`, `created_at`, …) plus an assertion that every other migration column is referenced somewhere would catch schema that drifts ahead of the client.

- **Add a migration-ordering lint covering *all* cross-table references, generalising BE-1's ordering guard** — BE-1's test only checks the base schema sorts first. A stronger script would scan every `*.sql` for `REFERENCES public.<t>` / `FROM public.<t>` / `public.<t>` policy refs and assert the migration that `CREATE TABLE`s `<t>` sorts earlier — catching the next 20260424-style "relation does not exist" before it hits the Supabase Preview.

- **Move the Supabase Preview branch off the from-empty replay or document why it's expected** — the Preview check replays *all* migrations from empty on first PR creation, which is what surfaced the ordering bug (good) but also means any historical migration that assumed dashboard-created tables will keep failing until backfilled into a base schema. A short `docs/` note (or a `supabase/seed.sql` guard) recording that the base schema must precede every dashboard-era migration would save the next contributor the same debugging loop.

- **Add a `supabase db reset` smoke job to CI (BE-31 precursor)** — the parity + ordering tests are static-text assertions; they can't catch a genuine SQL syntax error or a type mismatch (e.g. `uuid[]` vs `text[]` on `shared_with_user_ids` if prod differs). A lightweight GitHub Actions job running `supabase db reset` against a throwaway local Postgres would execute the migrations for real and turn "applies cleanly from empty" into a fast pre-merge signal, independent of the paid Supabase Preview.

- **Generate the base-schema migration from the `*-shapes.ts` builders instead of hand-maintaining both** — BE-1's `20260423_base_schema.sql` and the REST URL/body builders in `lib/supabase-profiles-shapes.ts` encode the same column set twice; they can drift. A small `scripts/check-schema-parity.ts` (the BE-3 direction) — or better, a codegen step that emits the column list from the body builders — would make the migration provably in sync with what the client sends, killing a whole class of "column does not exist" prod errors.

- **Add `created_at`/`updated_at timestamptz` + a `moddatetime` trigger to all four base tables (BE-9)** — the base schema gives `profiles`/`collections`/`items`/`friend_requests` a `created_at`, but no `updated_at`. Without it, delta-sync (`updated_at=gt.<cursor>`) and last-write-wins conflict resolution are impossible, so every device keeps doing full-table pulls. Adding the column + the standard `moddatetime` trigger now (cheap, additive) unblocks BE-13/BE-14 later.

- **Promote the runtime `is_admin` flag out of the hardcoded allowlist into `profiles.is_admin`** — admin is currently decided client-side by matching `username === "1337antoxa"`/the email literal in `SocialProvider`. The base schema is the natural place to add a `profiles.is_admin boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false` column so the eventual RLS policies (BE-11) and the delete-profile path key off server state instead of a string the client could spoof.

- **Add a CI step that runs every `supabase/migrations/*.sql` against an ephemeral Postgres in order (BE-31)** — the new structural test only greps the SQL text; it never executes it, so a syntax error or a forward-reference (e.g. items → collections ordering) wouldn't be caught until prod `db push`. A `services: postgres` GitHub Actions job applying the migrations to a scratch DB would turn "the migration is valid Postgres and applies cleanly from empty" into a green/red signal.

- **Backfill `NOT NULL` defaults audit for legacy rows before the base schema's defaults are relied on (BE-10)** — the base tables declare `NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`/`'{}'` on text/array columns, but the live tables predate that and may hold NULLs the client tolerates via `?? ""`. A one-time `UPDATE … SET col = COALESCE(col, '')` documented in MANUAL-TASKS, run before any future `SET NOT NULL`, would let the server enforce the same invariants the client already assumes instead of trusting every read path's coalesce.

- **Collapse the four near-identical `ResolvedListing[]` useMemos in `app/marketplace.tsx` into a `useResolvedListings(source)` hook** — `resolved`/`purchases`/`sales`/`recentlySold` all map a `MarketplaceListing[]` to `{ listing, item, owner }` with the same `getItemById`/`getProfileById` body. A single hook (or a `resolveListings(list, getItem, getOwner)` pure helper) would dedupe ~30 LOC and give every section one resolution rule, as already flagged in an earlier marketplace suggestion — PR8d makes the duplication more visible now that each renders a themed grid.

- **Theme the marketplace `soldToPill` for dark mode** — PR8d themed the card surface + text but `soldToPill` keeps a fixed `AMBER_MUTED_3` bg with `HERO_DARK` text + `BORDER`. On a dark card the `HERO_DARK` label reads low-contrast against the amber pill. Mapping the pill to `theme.cardElevated` + `theme.text` (or a dedicated `theme.pill` slot) would keep the "bought from / sold to" provenance legible in both schemes.

- **Memoize the per-card themed style spread in `ListingCard`** — the redesign builds a fresh `{ ...styles.card, backgroundColor, ...SHADOW_SOFT }` object for every card in the grid (potentially dozens on a desktop 3-col layout). Lifting it to a `useMemo(() => ({...}), [theme])` inside `ListingGrid` and passing it down, or a memoized themed-stylesheet, would cut the allocations on large marketplaces.

- **Add a `theme.shadow` slot so `SHADOW_SOFT` renders correctly on dark cards** — same root issue called out for the home redesign: `SHADOW_SOFT` is tuned for the light page (`shadowColor: HERO_DARK`) and disappears on dark surfaces. A scheme-aware `theme.shadow` would give the marketplace/profile/people cards real elevation in dark mode from one read, instead of spreading the light-only constant everywhere.

- **Add a dark-mode contrast snapshot test for `app/marketplace.tsx`** — coverage is the structural regex that `theme.*` reads appear in source; it can't catch the `soldToPill` legibility gap above. A react-test-renderer mount with `useColorScheme` mocked to `"dark"` asserting the resolved card/text colors differ from the page would harden the redesign and surface the pill issue as a failing test.

- **Theme the `app/profile/[id].tsx` action/status pills + admin button for dark mode** — PR8c themed the body cards + text but left `primaryAction`/`secondaryAction`/`statusBadge`/`adminAction`/`saveBioButton` on fixed `HERO_DARK`/`CARD_BG_3`/`BORDER_2` tokens, so on a dark page the same blend-in issue as people.tsx applies. A shared button-theming pass across people + profile (both have the identical relationship-action cascade) would close both at once.

- **Convert the profile dark-hero rgba overlays (`settingsIcon`/`editAvatarButton`/`handleInput`/`handleAction`) into named tokens** — these surfaces hard-code `"rgba(255,244,229,0.12)"` / `"rgba(255,255,255,0.08)"` string literals that escape the `lint:hex` guard (it only catches `#rrggbb`). Promoting them to `HERO_OVERLAY_*` design tokens would bring them under the lint net and let the hero respond to a future "lighter hero in light mode" tweak from one place.

- **Extract the duplicated `MarketplaceHistoryRow` + wishlist-row card into a shared `<ProfileMediaRow thumb title subtitle meta>` component** — the profile screen now has two near-identical row renders (wishlist items + marketplace history) using the same `wishlistCard`/`wishlistThumb`/`wishlistInfo` styles + theme spreads. A single component would dedupe ~25 LOC and give both rows one source of truth for the themed card surface.

- **Add a dark-mode contrast snapshot test for `app/profile/[id].tsx`** — current coverage is the structural regex that `theme.*` reads appear in source; it can't catch the deferred-pill issue above. A react-test-renderer mount with `useColorScheme` mocked to `"dark"` asserting the resolved card/text colors differ from the page would harden the redesign and surface the button gap as a failing test.

- **Promote the relationship-action cascade (friend/request_sent/request_received/following/none) into a `<RelationshipActions profileId relationship/>` shared by people + profile** — the exact same five-branch ternary with the same `addFriend`/`removeFriend`/`followProfile`/`unfollowProfile` wiring is duplicated across `app/people.tsx` and `app/profile/[id].tsx`. One component (theme-aware) would remove ~50 LOC of duplication and unify the action labels + styling for both surfaces.

- **Theme the `app/people.tsx` action buttons (`primaryAction`/`secondaryAction`/`statusBadge`/pagination) for dark mode** — PR8b themed the card surfaces + text but left the action pills on fixed `HERO_DARK`/`CARD_BG_3` tokens, so on a dark page the primary "Add friend" pill blends into the background and the secondary's border vanishes. A follow-up that maps these to `AMBER_ACCENT` (primary) + `theme.cardElevated`/`theme.border` (secondary/ghost) would make the people screen fully scheme-correct, matching the same deferral flagged on PR8a's modals.

- **Add a shared `<ProfileCard profile relationship onAction>` component extracted from `renderProfileCard` in `app/people.tsx`** — the same avatar + name/username/bio + relationship-action cascade will be needed on the upcoming profile-search results and the "Friends" tab. Lifting it into `components/profile-card.tsx` (theme-aware via `useAppTheme`) would let both surfaces drop one component instead of re-rolling the 60-line render + its five-branch relationship ladder.

- **Memoize the per-theme spread objects in `app/people.tsx` into a `useMemo(() => ({ card: {...}, search: {...} }), [theme])`** — the redesign now allocates fresh `{ ...styles.card, backgroundColor, ...SHADOW_SOFT }` objects on every row render inside `renderProfileCard`, defeating StyleSheet caching for long people lists (PAGE_SIZE = 25). A memoized themed-style bundle would cut the per-render allocations, the same cleanup already proposed for `app/index.tsx`.

- **Add a dark-mode contrast snapshot test for `app/people.tsx`** — current coverage is a structural regex that the right `theme.*` reads appear in source; it can't catch the deferred-button issue above (a pill going invisible on the dark page). A react-test-renderer mount with `useColorScheme` mocked to `"dark"` asserting resolved background/text props differ from the page color would harden the redesign and surface the button gap as a failing test.

- **Convert the `{...styles.pageButton, ...(disabled ? styles.pageButtonDisabled : {})}` spreads in `app/people.tsx` pagination to a `StyleSheet`-array `[styles.pageButton, disabled && styles.pageButtonDisabled]`** — React Native natively flattens style arrays and skips falsy entries, which is cheaper and more idiomatic than building a new object literal per render. Pure cleanup with identical output; also reads cleaner than the `{...spread}` form.

- **Hoist the inline `{ ...styles.x, color: theme.y }` spreads on `app/index.tsx` into a `useMemo(() => StyleSheet.create({...}), [theme])`** — the home redesign (PR5) now sprinkles ~15 inline object spreads in the JSX, each allocating a fresh style object on every render and defeating `StyleSheet`'s registry caching. A memoized per-theme stylesheet (the React Native canonical pattern) would cut the allocations, keep colors co-located with layout, and read cleaner than the spread soup before PRs 6–8 repeat the same pattern on every screen.

- **Delete the dead styles left in `app/index.tsx` (`socialList`, `personCard`, `personName`, `personMeta`, `emptyCard`, `emptyCardText`, `phoneActionsRow`)** — these `StyleSheet` entries have zero `styles.<name>` references (verified by grep) and only survive because they still anchor `CARD_BG`/`BORDER`/`MUTED`/`TEXT_DARK` imports. Removing them and the now-orphaned token imports would shrink the file ~50 LOC; do it alongside a token-presence test rewrite so the design-tokens guard doesn't break.

- **Add a `theme.shadow` slot to `useAppTheme()` instead of spreading raw `SHADOW_SOFT` inline** — PR5 spreads `...SHADOW_SOFT` directly on three home banners/cards, but `SHADOW_SOFT` is tuned for the light page and reads as nothing in dark mode. Exposing `theme.shadow` (soft on light, hairline/none on dark) would let every redesigned screen get scheme-correct elevation from one read, and a node test could assert `DARK.shadow !== LIGHT.shadow`.

- **Snapshot-test the home screen under both color schemes** — the only home coverage is a regex/structural check that the right token names appear in the source; it can't catch a contrast regression (e.g. `theme.text` on `theme.card` going invisible). A lightweight react-test-renderer mount with `useColorScheme` mocked to `"light"` and `"dark"` would assert the resolved color props actually differ, hardening the redesign before PRs 6–8 fan it out.

- **Make `SHADOW_SOFT` opt-in per platform via `Platform.select`** — on web, RN's `shadow*` props map to `box-shadow` but `elevation` is dropped, while on Android only `elevation` paints; the current single object ships both, so web cards get a slightly different shadow than native. Splitting `SHADOW_SOFT` into a `Platform.select({ web, default })` shape would make the new home/banner elevation pixel-consistent across the deployed PWA and the native builds.

- **Add a `__tests__/design-tokens-frozen-map-parity.test.ts` that asserts every top-level numeric/string export in `lib/design-tokens.ts` is registered in the frozen `designTokens` object** — PR1 had to hand-add the five new geometry names to the map, an easy step to forget. A regex scan of `export const FOO = ...` lines vs. the `Object.freeze({...})` keys would fail-closed the next time someone appends a token but skips the map (which silently breaks `DesignToken` autocomplete + the tokens-preview route).

- **Promote `useAppTheme()` selection into a tiny `pickTheme(scheme)` pure helper** — today the LIGHT/DARK ternary lives inside the hook, so it can't be unit-tested without a React renderer (the current test is purely structural/regex). Extracting `export function pickTheme(scheme: ColorSchemeName): AppTheme` would let a node test assert `pickTheme("dark").isDark === true` and `pickTheme(null) === LIGHT` directly, hardening the mapping before PRs 4–8 consume it everywhere.

- **Add a `SHADOW_SOFT_DARK` companion token** — `SHADOW_SOFT` hard-codes `shadowColor: HERO_DARK`, which "disappears against the dark-mode page surface" by design, but on elevated dark cards a subtle lighter-tinted shadow (or a hairline top-border) reads better than no elevation at all. A paired token plus a `theme.isDark ? SHADOW_SOFT_DARK : SHADOW_SOFT` convention would keep depth perception in dark mode without inline values.

- **Wire `FONT_DISPLAY_EDITORIAL` into the `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` preview route** — the existing dev tokens screen renders color/spacing swatches; adding a "type specimen" row that renders a sample headline in each font constant (`FONT_DISPLAY`, `FONT_DISPLAY_BOLD`, `FONT_DISPLAY_EDITORIAL`) would let reviewers eyeball the new serif chain on each platform before the redesign PRs land, closing the "verify on deployed build" loop earlier.

- **Add a structural test that fails if any `app/**` or `components/**` file still imports `FONT_DISPLAY`/`FONT_DISPLAY_BOLD` after PR8 ships** — the visual-upgrade brief migrates display titles off Syne onto `FONT_DISPLAY_EDITORIAL` but keeps the old exports for the transition. A grep-based guard (skippable until PR8) would catch a half-migrated screen and make the "Syne TTFs are now unreferenced, safe to drop" decision a deterministic check rather than a manual audit.

- **Add a `marketplaceMySalesEmpty` placeholder when `mySales.length === 0` but `myListings.length > 0`** — today the section is hidden entirely. A "you've listed N items, none sold yet" hint between the active listings and the Recently-sold surface would set expectations for first-time sellers without polluting the empty state for brand-new users.

- **Extract `ResolvedListing[]` into a `useResolvedListings(listings)` hook** — the marketplace screen now has THREE near-identical useMemos (`resolved`, `purchases`, `sales`) that map `MarketplaceListing[]` to `{ listing, item, owner }` triples. Extracting the pattern into a `useResolvedListings` hook in `lib/marketplace-context.tsx` (or a sibling helpers module) would shrink the screen by ~30 LOC and unify the resolution rule for the upcoming wishlist / saved-searches surfaces.

- **Render sales count + total revenue at the top of the My-sales section** — once the section exists, the natural follow-up is a "5 sales · 1,247 USD lifetime" header chip. A 10-line `useMemo` over `mySales.reduce` plus a styled `<View>` would unlock the lightest possible analytics dashboard without leaving the marketplace tab.

- **Add a sort selector ("Newest", "Highest price") to the sales section** — the helper currently returns `soldAt` descending. Exposing a `salesForUser(listings, userId, sort)` overload with a typed `"recency" | "price"` argument plus a small `<Pressable>` toggle would let sellers spot their biggest sales without scrolling. Pure-helper change + UI affordance.

- **Add an empty-state pill under the My-sales section linking to "How to sell" docs** — when a user opens the marketplace tab without any listings, the sales section is hidden but discovery suffers. A persistent CTA card with a `Pressable` link to `/help/selling` (or an `EmptyState` variant) would give first-time users a clear path forward without conflicting with the existing `marketplaceEmpty` hint.

- **Wire `planTransferItem` into the seller-side sold-listing prompt** — the seller branch currently archives the local item but doesn't write its own "I sold X to @buyer" record. Mirror the buyer-side `logEntry` build in a `planSellerArchive(snapshot, source, ...)` planner so both sides of every sale go through the same audit-log shape. Two-line addition to the existing helper plus a paired test.

- **Add a `mergeAcquiredItem(existing, plan)` helper that merges field-by-field on re-claim** — today the duplicate branch returns the existing item untouched. A future user might want re-claims to *update* certain fields (e.g. refresh `cost` if the seller relisted at a different price). A merge helper plus an opt-in `{ mergeStrategy: "replace" | "keep" }` option on the planner would close the gap without breaking the current idempotent default.

- **Replay missed transfer-log entries on app cold-start** — the planner now writes the entry only when `transferItemToBuyer` is called live. If a buyer's device was offline when a claim went through (rare, but possible with realtime UPDATE races), the log misses the entry. A 5-line bootstrap in `MarketplaceProvider` that compares `loadTransferLog(userId)` with `listings.filter(l => l.buyerUserId === userId && l.soldAt)` and queues the diff into the planner would close the gap.

- **Add a `planTransferItem.dryRun(input)` variant** — exposing a pure-read helper that returns just `{ collectionId, itemId, isDuplicate }` (without building the full collection/item objects) would let UI code render "Already in your Acquired" badges on the listing detail screen without invoking the planner's full computation. Five-line wrapper plus a unit test.

- **Generate a typed `__tests__/helpers/transfer-item-fixtures.ts` set** — the new test file hand-rolls `makeSnapshot` and `baseInput`. Extracting these into shared fixtures would let the upcoming seller-side, dispute-flow, and refund tests reuse the same well-typed shapes without each suite duplicating the construction.

- **Promote `sellerProvenance` into a `sellerProvenanceLabel(profile, fallback)` helper in `lib/social-helpers.ts`** — the new `owner?.username ? @username : displayName ?? fallback` ladder is the same shape as `ownerName` (line 104), `buyerName` (line 109), and several other "render a profile reference" sites. Extracting a single helper would unify the rendering rule and let a future "user changes their @username" event re-render everywhere consistently. Five-line helper + paired unit test.

- **Persist `acquiredFromUserId` alongside `acquiredFrom`** — today the buyer's Acquired item records the seller as a string label, which goes stale if the seller renames themselves. Adding a `CollectableItem.acquiredFromUserId?: string` (mirror of `createdByUserId`) and writing `listing.ownerUserId` into it would let the UI dereference the live `displayName` at render time, falling back to the snapshot label only when the user no longer exists. Schema is additive, no migration needed.

- **Surface `acquiredFrom` as a pressable chip on the item detail screen** — once the seller's `@username` is stored, the natural follow-up is to make it tappable: `Pressable onPress={() => router.push(\`/profile/${acquiredFromUserId}\`)}`. Today `app/item/[id].tsx:483` renders `acquiredFrom` as static `<Text>`; a 5-line conditional render that wraps it in a `Link` when the `@`-prefix is present would close the buyer→seller navigation loop with no schema change.

- **Add a structural test asserting `confirmDialog` is awaited inside `handleClaimPress`** — today `__tests__/confirm-dialog.test.ts:65` covers the import-and-await pattern, but the new owner dep + sellerProvenance ladder is the kind of refactor that often loses a critical `await` by accident. A dedicated `assert.match(src, /const ok = await confirmDialog/)` guard alongside the existing tests would catch a stray sync slip on the next round of edits.

- **Add a `lib/profile-display.ts` test fixture set** — every test that exercises a profile-rendering rule (the new sellerProvenance, the existing buyerName, the ownerName in 3+ screens) currently constructs ad-hoc `{ id, username, displayName }` objects. A shared `MOCK_PROFILE_WITH_USERNAME`, `MOCK_PROFILE_NO_USERNAME`, `MOCK_PROFILE_MINIMAL` set in `__tests__/helpers/profile-fixtures.ts` would let future profile-related tests share the same edge-case coverage without each suite hand-rolling its own shapes.

- **Build a "Purchases" tab keyed off the new `marketplace-transfer-log`** — the buyer-side log now persists every claim (with seller, mode, price, currency, and source-listing id) but nothing renders it yet. A `app/marketplace/purchases.tsx` route that calls `loadTransferLog(user.id)` in a `useEffect` and renders one row per entry (photo + title + "Bought from @seller for {price} {currency}") would unlock the audit-history surface that sub-task #4 promised. Pure-UI add — the data layer already exists.

- **Mirror the buyer-side transfer log with a seller-side one** — today only the buyer's device records who got what; the seller has no equivalent local log surviving the upstream listing delete. A `sales` half of the same helper (writing under `marketplaceSalesLogKey(userId)` and triggered from the seller-side prompt's "Archive item" branch) would give the seller the same provenance the buyer just got, closing the audit-history loop on both sides.

- **Hydrate `MarketplaceTransferLogEntry.title` from the live item if it still exists** — the log captures the title *at claim time*. If the buyer renames the item afterwards, the log gets stale. A 5-line `useTransferLog()` hook that does `getItemById(entry.itemId)?.title ?? entry.title` at render time would prefer the live name and fall back to the snapshot only when the item is gone.

- **Add `clearTransferLogEntry(userId, id)` for the "Remove from history" UX** — once the Purchases tab lands, users will inevitably want to delete log entries (mistaken claims, refunds, etc.). The dedup-by-id shape already supports it cleanly: a `mergeTransferLogEntry`-shaped remove that filters by id and re-persists. Five lines plus a paired pure-helper test.

- **Migrate `MARKETPLACE_KEY` to a per-user scoped key** — `lib/storage-keys.ts` still exports `MARKETPLACE_KEY` as a global constant, while the new `marketplaceTransferLogKey(userId)` is per-user. A multi-account device today bleeds listings across users on `MARKETPLACE_KEY` reads. Wrap it in `marketplaceKey(userId)` and add a `migrateStorageKey(MARKETPLACE_KEY, marketplaceKey(userId))` shim in the marketplace context's bootstrap.

- **Add an "Archived items" subsection on `app/collection/[id].tsx`** — today archived items vanish from the collection list entirely (audit trail kept in storage only). A collapsible "Archived (N)" tail group with the existing `<ItemCard>` rendered at half opacity would let owners eyeball what they've moved out without forcing them to dig into stats.
