Pure UI; the data already flows through `useCollections().items.filter(i => i.collectionId === id && i.archivedAt)`.

- **Add an `unarchiveItem(itemId)` companion to `archiveItem`** — once items can be archived, the seller will inevitably want to undo. A 4-line `setLocalItems((current) => current.map(...{archivedAt: null}))` + `updateRemoteItem(itemId, {archivedAt: null})` would make the archive flow non-terminal and pair with the upcoming "Archived items" surface above.

- **Replay missed claim notifications on app cold-start** — the seller-side prompt only fires on realtime UPDATEs. If the seller was offline when the sale closed, the listing arrives sold via `cloudFetchListings()` and no prompt ever appears. Compare current sold listings to a persisted "last-seen sold listing ids" set (AsyncStorage key `marketplace-seen-sold-v1`) and queue notifications for the diff. Closes the cold-start gap.

- **Auto-archive instead of prompting when the seller has explicitly opted in** — power users selling dozens of items don't want a modal each time. Add a `settings.autoArchiveSoldItems` toggle (PremiumProvider already lives next door for the gating), and when true, skip the prompt and immediately call `archiveItem` + toast. Three-line setting + a one-line context branch.

- **Promote the prompt's three actions into a configurable `SoldListingPolicy` ("archive" | "delete" | "keep" | "ask")** — today the SoldListingPrompt forces an interactive decision per sale. Storing a per-user default (and letting "ask" remain the unspecified fallback) lets the same code path power both UX paths: ask-each-time and silent-on-sale. The PremiumProvider could enforce that only the "ask" branch is available to free accounts, with the silent variants gated behind premium.

- **Add a `SYSTEM_COLLECTION_SUFFIXES` enum + `parseSystemCollectionId(id)` helper alongside `userScopedCollectionId`** — today the helper builds an id but there's no inverse that parses `${userId}-${suffix}` back into its parts (useful for "is this a system collection?" checks at delete-collection or premium-gate sites). A 5-line `Record<"acquired-marketplace" | "wishlist" | "trash", string>` enum + a regex-based parser would close the parity gap and let the rest of the codebase replace string-literal comparisons with typed lookups.

- **Migrate other id-template patterns into the same `lib/collections-helpers.ts` file** — `chatCacheKey(userId)`, `socialCacheKey(userId)`, the `analytics-${userId}` key, and the `MARKETPLACE_KEY` are all `${userId}-${suffix}` shapes scattered across `lib/storage-keys.ts`. Folding them into a single `userScopedKey(userId, scope)` helper (or extending `userScopedCollectionId` into a generic `userScopedId`) would shave 5-10 LOC and unify the naming.

- **Add a structural test asserting `lib/collections-context.tsx` never re-introduces the `${ownerUserId}-${...}` template** — the new test only checks for one specific template; a broader assertion `assert.doesNotMatch(src, /\$\{(ownerUserId|userId)\}-/)` would catch any future regression at any callsite, not just the Acquired one.

- **Promote `ACQUIRED_COLLECTION_ID_SUFFIX` into `lib/collections-helpers.ts` so the suffix list and the id generator live together** — today the SUFFIX lives in `lib/collections-context.tsx` while the generator lives in the helpers module. Co-locating them in `collections-helpers.ts` removes the cross-module import that's only needed because the SUFFIX was orphaned in the context for historical reasons.

- **Add `userScopedCollectionId.parse(id)` returning `{ userId, suffix } | null`** — the inverse of the new helper would let cloud-merge code that today does `id.startsWith(userId)` use a typed predicate instead. The parser would return `null` for non-system collections, which is the natural "untouched user-created collection" signal.

- **Migrate `app/wishlist.tsx`'s inline `window.confirm` / `Alert.alert` fork to the new `confirmDialog` helper** — `app/wishlist.tsx:135-145` still has the exact duplicated pattern the new helper was extracted to replace. A 10-line swap (delete the Platform fork, replace with `const ok = await confirmDialog({...})`) would eliminate the second-largest remaining duplicate. Same opportunity exists in `app/settings.tsx` (delete-account confirm), `app/collection/[id].tsx` (delete-collection confirm), and `app/item/[id].tsx` (delete-item confirm) — each is independently mergeable as a per-screen sub-task.

- **Add a `confirmDestructive(...)` convenience wrapper around `confirmDialog`** — most destructive confirms share the same shape: title + body + the labels "Delete" / "Cancel" + `destructive: true`. A 3-line wrapper `confirmDestructive(title, body, t)` that defaults the labels to `t("delete")` / `t("cancel")` would shave 5-10 LOC off every delete-confirm callsite and unify the visual treatment.

- **Render the web variant of `confirmDialog` via a custom `<Modal>` instead of `window.confirm`** — today the web branch uses the browser's native confirm dialog, which doesn't match the app's design system (it's a raw alert with platform-default styling). Swapping to a portal-rendered Modal with the warm-brown palette and the existing `ToastProvider`'s look-and-feel would keep the visual brand consistent across platforms.

- **Add a structural test that pins `Platform.OS === "web"` references stay OUT of `app/listing/[id].tsx`'s claim flow** — the web fork is now centralised in `lib/confirm-dialog.ts`; a one-line `assert.equal((src.match(/Platform\.OS === "web"/g) ?? []).length, 1)` ensures only the absolute-date tooltip survives. Catches a future regression where someone re-introduces the inline web fork bypassing the helper.

- **Promote `confirmDialog` into a render-prop component `<Confirm.Provider>` + `useConfirm()` hook** — today the API is a top-level `Promise<boolean>`, which means every test that wants to mock it has to monkey-patch the module. A context-based variant would let tests render the screen with a fake confirm that resolves synchronously, opening the door to true integration tests of the claim flow (rather than the source-pinning tests we use today).

- **Promote `claimingListingId` from a single `string | null` to a `Set<string>` so concurrent buys across multiple tabs/devices don't fight over one slot** — today the context only tracks ONE in-flight claim because the slot is a single id. If a user opens listing A in one tab and listing B in another and clicks claim on both, the second click overwrites the first's spinner. A `Set<string>` plus an `isClaiming(id)` selector would scale naturally without complicating the consumer API.

- **Persist `claimingListingId` to AsyncStorage so a crash mid-PATCH can resume on next launch** — today the in-flight flag lives in memory only. A 5-line `useEffect` that writes the value to a `MARKETPLACE_CLAIMING_KEY` and rehydrates on mount would give us crash-recovery semantics for free, mirroring how `MARKETPLACE_KEY` already persists the listings list.

- **Add a `useClaimingListing(id)` hook in `lib/marketplace-context.tsx` that returns just the boolean** — the listing detail screen currently destructures both `claimingListingId` AND `setClaimingListingId` to derive a single bool, which is leaky. A dedicated hook would let consumers read only what they need and let the provider hide the implementation (Set<string> vs string|null vs persistent map).

- **Render a "Claim in progress" pill on the marketplace card grid for listings whose `claimingListingId` matches** — today the spinner is local to the detail screen; if a user navigates away during a slow PATCH the card on the grid still says "Buy now" until the realtime UPDATE arrives. A `claimingListingId === listing.id ? <ClaimingPill /> : null` next to the price label closes the gap with ~5 LOC.

- **Add a structural test that pins `setClaimingListingId(null)` inside a `finally` block** — today the test asserts both calls exist but not that the reset is wrapped in `finally`. A regex `assert.match(src, /finally\s*\{[\s\S]*?setClaimingListingId\(null\)/)` would catch a future refactor that moves the reset into the `try` branch and leaves a permanently stuck spinner on PATCH failure.

- **Add an undo CTA to the claim success toast** — today `toast.success(t("marketplaceClaimSuccess"))` is fire-and-forget; a richer toast variant with an "Undo" action that calls a future `cloudReopenListing(id)` would give buyers a 5-second grace window before the claim becomes permanent. Pairs with the existing toast API surface (`show(input)` already accepts arbitrary content).

- **Render a typed `<ClaimSuccessToast listing buyer>` component instead of plain text** — the current toast is a generic "Listing claimed" string; a typed component with an inline thumbnail of the claimed item (via `item.photos[0]`) would feel more like a real receipt. Same one-shot lifecycle as the existing toast queue, just richer content.

- **Move the toast/sendMessage/trackEvent chain into a `markListingClaimed(listing, user)` helper on `MarketplaceContext`** — the three side-effects (sold flip + toast + chat + analytics) currently live in `app/listing/[id].tsx`'s `performClaim`, which means a future "buy directly from the marketplace grid" entry point would have to re-implement all four. Centralising in the context lets the screen just call `markListingClaimed(listing)` and the side-effects fan out automatically.

- **Add a structural test pinning the `toast.success(...)` ↔ `t("marketplaceClaimSuccess")` coupling** — today the new test asserts the literal string `toast.success(t("marketplaceClaimSuccess"))`; a sibling test that asserts the i18n key is *referenced* somewhere in the file (regardless of the exact `toast.X(...)` wrapper) would catch a future refactor that swaps `toast.success` for `Alert.alert` while keeping the key.

- **Move `marketplaceClaimSuccess` rendering into a shared "success copy" helper that pluralises across sell/trade** — today both modes show "Listing claimed"; a `claimSuccessCopy(mode)` returning "Purchased!" for sell and "Trade accepted!" for trade would feel more bespoke without adding much complexity. Pair with two new i18n keys.

- **Pre-render the auto-message body as a chat preview in the confirm dialog** — today `app/listing/[id].tsx` fires the templated "Bought your listing for X" message *after* the user confirms, so the buyer never sees what gets sent. Adding the rendered template as a third line in the Alert / window.confirm body ("This will send: ...") gives the buyer agency over their own outbound message and matches how the seller will see it. Same translation key, zero new i18n surface.

- **Localise the auto-message body in the seller's language, not the buyer's** — the new `marketplaceClaimAutoMessageBuy` template uses `t()` which resolves to the *buyer's* current language, so a Russian-speaking buyer sends a Russian sentence to an English-speaking seller. The chat message body is server-stored as a raw string; a cleaner pattern would be to send a structured payload (`{ kind: "marketplace_claim", listingId, price, currency }`) and let the chat renderer pick the seller's language at display time. Today's plain-text approach is good enough for v1 but should be on the upgrade radar.

- **Add an analytics event `listing_claim_message_sent` distinct from `listing_claimed`** — the trackEvent in performClaim fires for the claim but not for the chat-side-effect. A separate event keyed on `chatMessageId` lets the analytics dashboard distinguish "claimed AND message sent" vs "claimed, message bounce" (e.g. when `canMessage` returns false despite the friendsOnly gate having let the buyer through) — useful diagnostics for the new flow.

- **Reuse `ensureChatWith(ownerUserId)` to short-circuit when the buyer can't message** — today `sendMessage` itself calls `canMessage` and returns null, but that null is swallowed by `void sendMessage(...)`. Guarding the call with `if (ensureChatWith(listing.ownerUserId))` would make the silent-skip semantics explicit and let the test pin the conditional structurally (today the test only asserts the call exists, not that it's gated).

- **Expose the new claim-message bodies as `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts` pure functions** — today the templated body lives inline in `performClaim`, which means the i18n parity test and any future "render claim preview" component each have to re-derive the same `listing.mode === "sell" ? buy : trade` branch. A `claimMessageBody(t, listing, sourceItem, fallbackTitle)` helper would centralise the predicate (and a paired unit test could pin the exact output for both modes without spinning up React).

- **Extract a single `<NonOwnerActions listing owner viewer/>` component from the `isSelf ? : friendsOnly ? : (...)` ternary cascade in `app/listing/[id].tsx`** — today the three branches (self-hint / friends-only EmptyState / claim+message column) are inlined directly in the screen render, which made the new "gate claim behind friendsOnly" test rely on substring index ordering instead of a typed prop boundary. A component split would let the test mount each branch in isolation and assert the *absence* of the claim button when `friendsOnly` is true, rather than asserting source-code order.

- **Promote `friendsOnly = !isSelf && !canMessage(ownerId)` into a `canTransactWith(viewer, owner)` helper in `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts`** — the predicate is now used in two places (the gate decision + the new structural test pinning it) and will soon be referenced from the seller-side "their listing was claimed" prompt once that lands. Centralising the rule means a future tweak (e.g. "block on muted users too") only edits one helper instead of every screen.

- **Add a runtime assertion in `cloudMarkSold` that the caller's `buyerUserId` matches the listing's existing `buyer_user_id` (if already set) — guard against double-claims** — today the PATCH happily overwrites a prior buyer because Supabase has no row-level "only-if-null" filter on the column. Threading a `if=buyer_user_id.is.null` URL filter (PostgREST supports it) plus failing closed when the row doesn't update would close the race where two viewers claim the same listing on identical wire timestamps.

- **Add a structural test that pins the relative order of `transferItemToBuyer` BEFORE `markListingSold`** — the existing test asserts both calls exist (`marketplace-listing-detail.test.ts:88-99`); a sibling assertion that the friends-only EmptyState short-circuits BEFORE either call is composed would catch a regression where someone accidentally moves the EmptyState below the actions column and the claim flow keeps running through.

- **Replace the substring-index assertion in the new "gates Buy/Trade behind friendsOnly" test with a regex that captures the surrounding ternary structure** — today the test relies on `friendsOnlyIdx < claimIdx` which would still pass if a future refactor renders the claim button further down the file but *outside* the friendsOnly branch. A regex like `: friendsOnly \? <EmptyState[\s\S]*?: \([\s\S]*?marketplaceBuyNow` would lock in the structural relationship instead of a positional ordering.

- **Delete the now-unused `buildMarkSoldPayload` duplicate from `lib/supabase-marketplace-shapes.ts`** — `markSoldPayload(soldAt, buyerUserId)` and `buildMarkSoldPayload(soldAt, buyerUserId)` return identical objects; only `markSoldPayload` is referenced anywhere in the codebase (`grep -rn buildMarkSoldPayload lib/ __tests__/` returns 0 hits outside the declaration). Removing the duplicate plus its `MarkSoldPayload` alias closes a foot-gun where a future contributor might import the wrong one and silently bypass the buyer_user_id round-trip that the new integration test pins.

- **Add a `__tests__/helpers/recording-fetcher.ts` extracting `makeRecordingFetcher` from `__tests__/supabase-marketplace.test.ts`** — the helper that records `{url, init}` for an injected `fetcher = fetch as FetchFn` is the canonical shape every cloud-wrapper test will need (cloudAddListing, cloudRemoveListing, cloudFetchListings, and the future buy/trade endpoints). Promoting it into a shared helper avoids each test file re-rolling the same 12 lines, and gives a single place to add common assertions like "Authorization header threaded" or "Content-Type defaults to application/json".

- **Pin a structural assertion that `lib/supabase-marketplace.ts:cloudMarkSold` returns `res.ok` rather than `res.status === 200`** — today the wrapper returns `res.ok` (which spans 200-299), but Supabase PATCH-with-`Prefer: return=representation` actually returns 200; a future refactor that tightens the check to `=== 200` would silently break a 204-returning path (e.g. if `Prefer` is dropped). A one-line structural test `assert.match(src, /return\s+res\.ok\s*;\s*\}\s*$/m)` keeps the contract loose-and-permissive.

- **Add a `cloudMarkSold buyer_user_id round-trip` smoke test under `__tests__/marketplace-context.test.ts` that drives the *full* context** — today the new integration test composes the pure helpers manually; a higher-level test that mocks `cloudMarkSold` and asserts the context's `markListingSold(id, buyerUserId)` actually invokes the cloud wrapper with the same `(id, soldAt, buyerUserId)` signature would catch a future regression in the context layer (e.g. someone passing `null` as a third arg by accident).

- **Add a unit test for the realtime UPDATE branch in `subscribeToListings` that asserts `buyer_user_id` survives the `rowToListing` mapping** — today the structural source pinning ensures the UPDATE listener is wired, but no test feeds a synthetic `{ buyer_user_id: "buyer-1", sold_at: "..." }` row through `rowToListing` to verify the realtime path emits a `MarketplaceListing` with the right `buyerUserId`. A 10-line test exercising `rowToListing({ ...baseRow, buyer_user_id: "x" })` would close the realtime ↔ wire-format gap.

- **Generalise the new `__tests__/dev-menu-wiring.test.ts` regex grammar into a `__tests__/helpers/source-asserts.ts`** — today the file rolls its own `match(/useEffect\(/)` / `match(/registerDevMenu\(/)` shorthand; a shared `assertCallSite(src, fn, { args?: Record<string, RegExp> })` helper would let the next structural test (e.g. analytics-mirror wiring, premium-context wiring) compose its assertions instead of re-rolling regex literals. Same DRY shape that `__tests__/helpers/sql-migration-asserts.ts` already takes (already pending in `.tasks.md`).

- **Pin a structural test that `app/_layout.tsx`'s registerDevMenu useEffect has `[]` deps** — today the file passes the deps array as `[]` (which is correct — the action map is stable), but a future refactor could accidentally inline `[clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig]` and re-run the registration on every parent render. A `match(/useEffect\(\s*\(\s*\)\s*=>\s*\{[^}]*registerDevMenu[^}]*\}\s*,\s*\[\s*\]\s*\)/s)` would close the gap.

- **Promote the new `types/globals.d.ts` into a typed ambient module for `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` env vars** — today every `lib/*-config.ts` module reads `process.env.EXPO_PUBLIC_X` and falls back to `undefined`. A `declare namespace NodeJS { interface ProcessEnv { EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL?: string; ...; } }` block in the same `globals.d.ts` would give every consumer IntelliSense on the documented env-var list and flag typos at compile time, without changing any runtime behaviour.

- **Declare `globalThis.__sentryStatus` / `globalThis.__sendSentryTestError` / `globalThis.__clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` ambient signatures in `types/globals.d.ts`** — these dev helpers are attached to `globalThis` at runtime in `app/_layout.tsx`, but their types are erased so a `globalThis.__sentryStatus()` call from the dev console (or a future structural test) sees `unknown` instead of the real function signature. A `declare const __sentryStatus: () => SentryStatusSnapshot;` block (gated under a `// dev-only`-flavoured comment) gives the typed surface without any runtime change.

- **Add a `__tests__/globals-d-ts-coverage.test.ts` that grep-walks every `(globalThis as` cast across `lib/`+`app/`+`components/`** — the new ambient declaration retired one cast in `lib/dev-menu.ts`; the same pattern is likely to creep back in for the next dev-globals helper. A 20-line structural test asserting the call-site count stays at zero would force every new global through the ambient declaration instead of an ad-hoc cast.

- **Add a copy-to-clipboard tap on each `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` swatch** — designers reviewing the palette currently have to manually retype the token name (e.g. `AMBER_ACCENT`) into their editor; a `Pressable` wrapper with `Clipboard.setStringAsync(token.name)` (web) / `navigator.clipboard.writeText` (RN web) plus a one-line "copied" toast via the existing `ToastProvider` would shave 2-3 seconds per swatch and feels right at home in a dev tool.

- **Render a `TYPOGRAPHY` section on `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` showing each `FONT_*` constant as a paragraph in its actual face** — today the route only covers colours + geometry, but the font ladder (`FONT_DISPLAY` / `FONT_BODY` / `FONT_BODY_BOLD` / etc.) is just as much a design token and equally invisible at a glance. A 30-line `<View>` with one `Text` per font + a "The quick brown fox…" sample would close the gap.

- **Add a `__tests__/dev-tokens-route-registered.test.ts` that asserts `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` is reachable via Expo Router's file-system routing** — today the route exists but nothing structurally tests that it default-exports a function with no required params (Expo Router silently ignores broken default exports). A quick `assert.equal(typeof (await import("../app/_dev/tokens")).default, "function")` would catch a future regression where someone wraps the export in a HOC that breaks the routing contract.

- **Surface the dev tokens preview as a settings-screen footer link gated on `__DEV__ || adminFlag`** — today the route is discoverable only by typing `/_dev/tokens` manually; a "Design tokens preview" row under the Diagnostics block (the same surface where `__sentryStatus` already lives) would let designers and reviewers reach the page in one tap during a real session instead of digging into the URL bar.

- **Add a deterministic CSS-snapshot test that hashes the swatches map** — the `groupColorTokens` helper inside `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` partitions the 100+ named tokens into prefix buckets; if someone reorders the COLOR_GROUPS or adds a token to a prefix that no group matches, the orphan bucket silently catches it but the visual ordering changes. A `__tests__/dev-tokens-classifier.test.ts` that asserts the hash of `[group.id, ...entries.map(name)]` matches a recorded snapshot would catch palette reshuffles before they hit a designer's eyes.

- **Adopt the new `ColorValue`/`BackgroundColorValue` types on every existing component that takes a color-flavoured prop** — today only `components/qr-code.tsx` was migrated. Sweep the codebase for `color?: string` / `background?: string` / `borderColor?: string` etc. on shared components (when new ones land) and route them through `ColorValue` so the autocomplete trick reaches every consumer. A grep-based structural test in `__tests__/color-value-adoption.test.ts` could enforce the convention going forward.

- **Use `ColorValue` as the type for `ItemTag.color` in `lib/types.ts`** — today it's plain `string`, which means a typo silently renders an empty fill. Switching to `ColorValue` keeps every existing call site compatible (literal hex still passes) while giving the tag-create UI in `app/create.tsx` autocomplete for the `TAG_*` palette entries.

- **Add an ESLint rule (or a `__tests__/no-string-color-prop.test.ts` regex sweep) banning `color?: string` declarations in `components/` once `ColorValue` is the canonical type** — keeps drift from happening when a contributor adds a new component without reaching for the type alias. Same shape as the existing `lint:hex` script that already catches inline literals.

- **Document `ColorValue` + `BackgroundColorValue` in the design-tokens preview route** — `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` currently shows swatches with the token *name* as a chip; adding a one-line code sample at the top (`import { type ColorValue } from "@/lib/design-tokens"`) would teach designers/engineers the new prop-typing convention without leaving the page they already visit when picking a colour.

- **Promote a `resolveColorValue(value: ColorValue | ColorTokenName): string` helper** — today consumers pass either a hex literal *or* a `ColorTokenName` (the *key*, e.g. `"HERO_DARK"`). A small `(value) => isColorTokenName(value) ? designTokens[value] : value` helper would let future components accept names AND values uniformly, giving the IntelliSense surface a second axis (the named tokens themselves) without breaking the hex-literal path.

- **Migrate `marketplaceListedAt` to use the new `relativeDateLabel` helper + a new `marketplaceListed` prefix-only translation** — today the prefix-only string is duplicated across six locales as a template (`"Listed ${when}"`). Switching to `relativeDateLabel(t("marketplaceListed"), formatRelativeDate(iso))` would delete five lines per language and reuse the same pattern that the helper was extracted to enable. Pure cleanup — the helper is already plumbed and tested.

- **Add `acquiredAgo` + `memberSince` prefix translations using `relativeDateLabel`** — the original task cited these as the two next call sites for the helper, but they're not yet wired. `app/item/[id].tsx` currently surfaces `acquiredDate` (an absolute date); appending an "Acquired 5 hours ago" subtitle via `relativeDateLabel(t("acquiredPrefix"), formatRelativeDate(item.acquiredAt))` would give the helper a real production consumer. `app/profile/[id].tsx` would follow the same pattern with `t("memberSincePrefix")`.

- **Guard against RTL language regressions in `relativeDateLabel`** — the current implementation always joins `prefix` + space + `when`. If/when an Arabic / Hebrew locale lands, the relative time clause would render LTR inside an RTL paragraph and read backwards. A `Intl.Locale(language).textInfo.direction === "rtl"` branch that swaps order (or wraps fragments with U+200F right-to-left marks) would close the gap before the i18n payload arrives. Pair with a unit test that asserts behaviour for a future `ar` / `he` `AppLanguage` member.

- **Surface a `useRelativeDateLabel(prefix: TranslationKey, iso: string)` hook in `lib/use-now.ts`** — the helper as shipped requires three coordinated calls (`t(prefix)`, `formatRelativeDate(iso)`, `relativeDateLabel(...)`). Wrapping them into a single hook that re-renders via the existing `useNow` clock cuts call-site noise to one line and ensures live-updating labels stay in sync without each consumer re-pulling `useNow` manually.

- **Test that `marketplaceListedAt` in every locale renders a `prefix + space + when` shape** — the helper's contract assumes that pattern, but it's not enforced by a test today. A `__tests__/marketplace-listed-at-shape.test.ts` that calls each locale's `marketplaceListedAt({ when: "X" })` and asserts the output matches `/^\S+(\s+\S.*)?\sX$/` would block a future locale that introduces a postfix or punctuation break.

- **Live-tick the chat preview timestamp via `useNow(60_000)`** — `formatChatPreviewTimestamp` swaps to `HH:mm` for the last hour, but the rendered string is a snapshot of `Date.now()` at the moment the chat list renders. If the user opens the chats screen and stays on it, a message that ticks past the 60-minute boundary will keep showing "23:47" forever (until `refreshFromCloud` happens to fire). Threading `useNow(60_000)` through the screen and adding a `now` arg to the helper would auto-flip the label to "1 hour ago" the moment the boundary is crossed, with zero extra plumbing on each call site.

- **Apply `formatChatPreviewTimestamp` in `app/chat/[id].tsx` per-message timestamps too** — the screen currently renders each individual chat bubble's timestamp via `formatRelativeDate`, but the same UX argument applies inline: a message sent 3 minutes ago reads more naturally as "14:32" than as "3 minutes ago". Reusing the new helper (already in the I18n context) is a one-line consumer change with no new helper code, and would close the gap between the chats *list* and the chat *thread*.

- **Add a user preference for 12h vs 24h chat preview clock** — `formatChatPreviewTimestamp` currently hard-codes `hour12: false` for consistency, but US-locale users may expect `2:47 PM`. A `lib/clock-format.ts` reader that pulls from a new `collectables-clock-format-v1` AsyncStorage slot (with `null` = follow-locale, `"12h"`/`"24h"` = override) and a Settings-screen toggle would respect either preference. The helper already takes a locale arg; widening to `{ locale, hourCycle }` keeps the change local.

- **Render an "absolute timestamp" tooltip on long-press for the chat preview** — pairs with the existing suggestion to expose an `accessibilityLabel` ISO date on the listing-detail "Listed X ago" `<Text>`. For chat previews specifically, a `Pressable` wrapper that surfaces `new Date(iso).toLocaleString(bcp47)` via the existing `ToastProvider` would give power users a way to see the full date+time of the last message without opening the thread. Same pattern, different surface.

- **Add a `__tests__/chat-preview-timestamp-locale.test.ts` that asserts every supported locale resolves to a 24h `HH:mm` form** — the new test already spot-checks "no AM/PM in en", but a locale-by-locale matrix (en/ru/de/pl/es/be → each must produce `/^\d{2}:\d{2}$/` for a recent ISO) would catch a future regression where someone flips `hour12` to `true` without updating the test contract. Mirrors how `__tests__/format-relative-date.test.ts` iterates the same locale tuple.

- **Reuse the long-press absolute-tooltip pattern on the chat preview timestamp** — `app/chats.tsx` now renders an `HH:mm` clock for fresh messages but loses the full date+time on long-press. Wrapping the `<Text style={styles.when}>` in the same `Pressable` + `onLongPress={() => toast.info(formatAbsoluteDate(preview.lastMessageAt))}` + `accessibilityLabel` shape would give the chats list the same power-user surface that listing detail just got. The two screens already share the helper.

- **Pull the long-press tooltip pattern into a shared `<AbsoluteDateTooltip>` component** — three call sites already need it (listing detail "Listed X ago", chat preview timestamps, price-history rows on listing detail). A 30-line component `<AbsoluteDateTooltip iso={...}><Text>...</Text></AbsoluteDateTooltip>` that encapsulates the `Pressable` + `onLongPress` + `accessibilityLabel` + web `title` triplet would keep each call site to a single component swap and avoid the per-screen ceremony every time.

- **Migrate price-history rows in `app/listing/[id].tsx` to the same tooltip pattern** — each `<Text style={styles.priceHistoryDate}>{formatRelativeDate(entry.recordedAt)}</Text>` row would benefit from the same absolute-date tooltip since users comparing prices over time often need to know the precise listing date. Two-line change once the shared component above lands.

- **Add an `accessibilityHint` to the new Pressable that announces "Long press for absolute date"** — today the Pressable only sets `accessibilityLabel` (the absolute date), but a screen-reader user won't discover the long-press affordance without a hint. RN's `accessibilityHint` is announced after the label with a slight pause, and is the canonical surface for "here's what activating this control will do". One-line addition.

- **Replace the medium/short style choices in `formatAbsoluteDate` with locale-driven hour-cycle awareness** — `toLocaleString(bcp47, { dateStyle: "medium", timeStyle: "short" })` defaults to 12h in `en-US` ("3:42 PM") and 24h elsewhere. If we want a consistent 24h surface across all locales (mirroring `formatChatPreviewTimestamp`), thread `hourCycle: "h23"` into the options. If we want to respect each locale, leave it. Either way, a unit test pinning the choice would lock in the contract.

- **Translate DevMenu labels through `t()` instead of inline English strings** — the `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` action now reads "Clear runtime Supabase config" in the native DevMenu, but engineers running the app in `ru`/`be` mode see English. Threading a translation key (e.g. `t("devMenuClearRuntimeSupabaseConfig")`) into the `label` field would localise the DevMenu entry to match the rest of the app. The `i18n-context` provider is already mounted above the `useEffect` that calls `registerDevMenu`.

- **Add an `accessibilityLabel` parallel to the DevMenu label** — today the label is a free-form string, but for screen-reader-friendly debugging (rare but real on accessibility-test rigs), an optional `accessibilityLabel` field on the `{ label, run }` shape would let `addDevMenuItems` consumers route the label to native accessibility surfaces. Defaults to `label` when unset; one-line addition.

- **Validate that a `{ label }` is not the empty string at registration time** — currently `registerDevMenu` will happily pass `addDevMenuItems({ "": fn })` if the consumer passes `label: ""`. A two-line guard that throws (in dev) or warns + falls back to the action key would catch the foot-gun before it renders an unclickable blank row in the DevMenu.

- **Expose a `describeAction` helper from `lib/dev-menu.ts` that returns the resolved `{ label, run }` pair** — today `resolveAction` is private; lifting it to a named export would let future test files (and the `__resetCollectablesStorage` sibling task pending below) assert that their action map descriptor matches the same shape without duplicating the type-narrowing logic.

- **Add a `__tests__/dev-menu-labels-no-duplicates.test.ts` that asserts no two actions share a label** — if a future contributor adds two `{ label: "Reset", run: ... }` entries to the same action map, the second silently overwrites the first because the DevMenu items map keys on label. A 10-line test that walks the action object and asserts label uniqueness would close that gap; same regex grammar as the existing `dev-menu-wiring.test.ts`.

- **Surface the `shouldCollapse` flag through `DevMenuAction`** — the real `expo-dev-menu` `ExpoDevMenuItem` accepts an optional `shouldCollapse: boolean` that auto-closes the menu after firing the callback. Today `adaptExpoDevMenu` hard-codes `shouldCollapse: undefined`, which uses the SDK default (don't collapse). A `{ label, run, shouldCollapse? }` widening on `DevMenuAction` would expose this for one-shot actions like "Reset onboarding" where staying in the menu after the click is awkward.

- **Add a `__tests__/expo-dev-menu-plugin-registered.test.ts` that scans the prebuild manifest** — today `__tests__/dev-menu-expo-adapter.test.ts` asserts `expo-dev-menu` is in `app.json`'s plugins array, but a deeper test could shell out to `npx expo prebuild --no-install --check` (in CI only) and assert the dev-menu native module's Podfile entry / Gradle import lands. The current structural check guards the JSON; a manifest check would guard that the plugin actually runs.

- **Auto-fire the DevMenu adapter on session start to verify wire-up** — the `adaptExpoDevMenu` adapter is exercised only when `loadDevMenuModule()` succeeds at runtime, but a smoke probe at app startup that calls `registerDevMenuItems([])` (no-op) and logs success/failure via the existing `addBreadcrumb` would give us a one-shot "the native bridge is live" signal in Sentry breadcrumbs. Useful for diagnosing why a contributor's local dev client doesn't show the menu entry.

- **Move the `globalThis.require("expo-dev-menu")` fallback to a dedicated `lib/native-require.ts` helper** — today `loadDevMenuModule` reaches into the React Native runtime require via `(globalThis as { require? }).require`. The same pattern will likely appear for other dev-only native modules (`expo-dev-launcher`, `expo-dev-client`, future Crash #4 reporter integrations). Centralising `nativeRequire(id: string)` keeps the `unknown` cast in one place and lets each consumer just ask for what they need.

- **Add `expo-dev-menu` to a `lib/runtime-config.ts` doctor health-check that surfaces "DevMenu native module: available / fallback"** — today the only way to know whether `loadDevMenuModule()` returned non-null is to call `registerDevMenu` and inspect the `RegisterDevMenuResult.devMenuRegistered` boolean. A user-facing diagnostics row on the (future) `app/_dev/diagnostics.tsx` screen that prints this status would let an engineer know at a glance whether they need to switch to a dev-client build.

- **Add a confirm-dialog gate before `clearAllCollectablesStorage` fires from the DevMenu** — today the `resetCollectablesStorage` action wipes every `collectables-*` key the moment it's tapped, with no "are you sure?" prompt. Even though it's dev-only, mis-taps in a long DevMenu list are easy. Wrap the `run` in the same `Platform.OS === "web" ? window.confirm : Alert.alert` pattern used in `app/listing/[id].tsx` `handleClaimPress` (or the future `lib/confirm-dialog.ts` helper) so a stray tap doesn't nuke an in-progress test session.

- **Surface a "Reset onboarding" sibling action that wipes only the language + diagnostics keys** — full storage reset is heavy; many dev cycles just need to re-trigger the language picker or the analytics opt-in prompt. A second labelled action (e.g. `resetOnboarding` with `label: "Reset onboarding flags"`) backed by `AsyncStorage.multiRemove([LANGUAGE_KEY, DIAGNOSTICS_KEY])` would give a lighter reset path. Same registration shape, one extra entry in the actions map.

- **Add a unit test that asserts the dev-menu actions map is sorted alphabetically by key** — today `app/_layout.tsx` lists `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` before `resetCollectablesStorage` by coincidence. As more actions land (the suggestion above adds two), maintaining a deterministic order prevents merge conflicts and makes the DevMenu list predictable. A 5-line regex scan of `_layout.tsx` that extracts the action keys and asserts `keys === [...keys].sort()` would lock it in.

- **Make `clearAllCollectablesStorage` return the wiped-key list** — today the helper returns `void`, so callers (Sentry breadcrumb, analytics dev event, DevMenu confirmation toast) can't log "wiped N keys". A `Promise<string[]>` return value lets the DevMenu `run` surface `console.info("[dev] wiped %d keys", keys.length)` (or a toast in the future), and tests can assert the exact set wiped without re-scanning AsyncStorage.

- **Add a `__tests__/dev-menu-action-keys-no-collisions.test.ts` that asserts no two actions share a global helper name after the `__` prefix is applied** — currently both `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` → `__clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` and `resetCollectablesStorage` → `__resetCollectablesStorage` are safe, but a future contributor adding `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig: () => ...` again (e.g. in a different `useEffect`) would silently overwrite the global. A 15-line test that reads `app/_layout.tsx`, extracts the action keys, and asserts uniqueness keeps the globalThis namespace clean.

- **Use `normalizeListing` inside `cloudFetchListings` / `cloudFetchListingById` so every cloud hydration path runs through the same defensive default** — today the helper is applied only inside `MarketplaceProvider`'s effect, but `app/listing/[id].tsx` calls `fetchListingById` which delegates to `cloudFetchListingById` and returns the raw row. Threading `normalizeListing` through the cloud wrappers (one `.map` per fetch) means deep-link routes that bypass the provider's hydration still see a coalesced `buyerUserId`.

- **Add a `normalizeListings(raws)` array helper that runs the per-row coalesce + drops obviously malformed entries** — pairs with the pending `coerceListing` validator suggestion above. Where `normalizeListing` only fixes the `buyerUserId` default, `normalizeListings` would walk the array, run `normalizeListing` on valid rows, and quietly skip entries missing `id` / `mode` / `ownerUserId`. Single entry point for every JSON-hydration path.

- **Re-export `normalizeListing` from a public `lib/marketplace-public.ts` barrel** — today consumers must reach into `@/lib/marketplace-helpers` for pure helpers and `@/lib/marketplace-context` for the React surface. A single barrel that re-exports both keeps import lines short in screens (`import { useMarketplace, normalizeListing, listingsForUser } from "@/lib/marketplace-public";`) and lets the helpers move between files without breaking call sites.

- **Add a `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts` JSDoc `@example` block on `normalizeListing` showing the push-notification deep-link case** — explanatory comments aside, an `@example` snippet (`const listing = normalizeListing(JSON.parse(pushPayload.listing))`) makes the intended consumer surface obvious in IntelliSense. Mirrors the existing `priceHistoryForTitle` doc shape.

- **Add a structural test asserting `normalizeListing` is the ONLY place that does the `buyerUserId ?? null` coalesce** — a `__tests__/marketplace-no-duplicate-coalesce.test.ts` that greps `lib/marketplace-*.ts(x)` for `buyerUserId\s*\?\?\s*null` and asserts exactly one match keeps future contributors honest. Today the original call site in `MarketplaceContext` was removed; this test would catch a regression where someone re-introduces the inline coalesce.

- **Promote a `lib/supabase-test-harness.ts` that stubs `react-native` + `@react-native-async-storage/async-storage` via `Module._resolveFilename`/`_load` so live tests can actually import `lib/supabase-marketplace.ts`** — today the cloud wrapper layer (`cloudFetchListings`, `cloudAddListing`, `cloudMarkSold`) is tested only structurally because importing the file pulls in react-native peers that `node:test` can't resolve. A small harness loaded via `--import` (mirrors `__tests__/test-globals.ts`) that returns no-op stubs for those modules would unlock real fetcher-injection tests for every cloud wrapper, not just the structural shell of `cloudMarkSold`.

- **Add a `__tests__/supabase-marketplace-fetcher-injection.test.ts` that asserts every cloud wrapper threads its `{ fetcher, tokenProvider }` arg into the actual call** — today `cloudMarkSold`'s structural test pins the destructure, but `cloudFetchListings`/`cloudAddListing`/`cloudRemoveListing`/`cloudFetchListingById` rely on visual inspection. A 20-line scan across each function body asserting `fetcher(` appears inside (not just `fetch(`) prevents a regression where a future refactor accidentally bypasses the injected fetch.

- **Make `cloudMarkSold` return the parsed row instead of `boolean`** — today it returns `res.ok`, throwing away the `Prefer=return=representation` body that PostgREST sends back. A `MarketplaceListing | null` return value would let `MarketplaceProvider` immediately reconcile its in-memory state with the canonical row (including server-set `updated_at` and any future `transferred_at` column) without a follow-up `cloudFetchListingById` round trip.

- **Add an analytics event `marketplace_listing_marked_sold` fired by the wrapper, with `{ has_buyer: boolean, mode }`** — useful for understanding how often listings are claimed by a friend vs. self-sold-marker (no buyer). Same shape as the existing `marketplace_listing_created` event; one line in `cloudMarkSold` after the `res.ok` check.

- **Extract the `markSoldPayload(soldAt, buyerUserId) → JSON.stringify → PATCH` boilerplate into a `cloudPatchListing(id, patch)` helper** — once a second column gets PATCHed (e.g. `transferred_at`, `archived_at`), this helper would avoid copy-pasting the same URL builder + header builder + body serialiser. The current `cloudMarkSold` would become a 3-line wrapper that calls `cloudPatchListing(id, markSoldPayload(...))`.

- **Promote the "Transferred" pill into a shared `<ListingTransferredBadge />` component** — today `app/listing/[id].tsx` and `app/marketplace.tsx` each declare their own `transferredBadge` + `transferredBadgeText` styles. A 30-line component in `components/listing-transferred-badge.tsx` that reads the i18n key and renders the pill with theme tokens would let the future "My listings" / "Sales" / profile-history surfaces drop the same badge in one line, with a single source of truth for the colour and corner radius.

- **Add an `accessibilityLabel` and `accessibilityRole="text"` on the transferred pill** — the badge is rendered as a `<Text>` inside a styled `<View>`, but screen readers don't naturally pronounce the visual association ("this listing went to a buyer"). A more descriptive label (`t("marketplaceTransferredBadgeA11y", { name: buyerName })`) would announce "Transferred to {buyer}" instead of just "transferred". Pair with the existing chip-naming pattern in `app/profile/[id].tsx`.

- **Surface a `transferredAt` timestamp under the pill on listing detail** — today the sold banner shows the buyer name + the new badge but loses the *when*. Threading the existing `soldAt` ISO through `formatRelativeDate` ("Transferred 2h ago") gives collectors immediate temporal context without opening the chat thread. Already wired in the price-history rows on the same screen — a 3-line addition.

- **Filter the transferred-badge i18n keys through the existing `relativeDateLabel` helper for "Transferred X ago"** — once the timestamp lands, the same prefix-translation pattern that powers `marketplaceListedAt` / "Acquired X ago" can produce a unified "Transferred 3h ago" line per locale. Avoids adding a per-language "transferred ago" key for each suffix variant.

- **Add the transferred-pill render to `app/profile/[id].tsx`'s future "Trades & Transfers" section** — already proposed in the broader sub-task list, but worth a fresh suggestion now that the badge component is locked in. The section would render `purchasesForUser(...) + listingsAcquiredByUser(...)` and reuse the badge to mark each entry as a "completed transfer" vs. an in-flight listing.

- **Reduce `purchasesForUser` to a thin wrapper that calls `listingsAcquiredByUser` and re-sorts by `soldAt`** — today the two helpers duplicate the `buyerUserId === userId && soldAt != null` filter. Centralising the predicate in `listingsAcquiredByUser` and having `purchasesForUser` just `.sort((a, b) => (a.soldAt < b.soldAt ? 1 : -1))` the result keeps the contract (different sort = different surface) without two copies of the same gate. Saves a future regression where one filter gets a new clause and the other doesn't.

- **Add a `listingsSoldByUser(listings, userId)` mirror for the seller side** — `listingsForUser` returns *all* listings owned by the user (active + sold), but a "Sales" tab specifically wants `ownerUserId === userId && soldAt != null`. A 5-line helper mirroring `listingsAcquiredByUser` (createdAt-desc sort, same shape) gives the sales surface a single import point.

- **Generalise into a `filterAndSortListings(listings, predicate, sort?)` higher-order helper** — every "filter+slice+sort" trio in `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts` repeats the same scaffold. A 10-line helper that takes a predicate and an optional sort comparator (defaulting to createdAt-desc) would let `purchasesForUser`, `listingsAcquiredByUser`, `listingsForUser`, and the future `listingsSoldByUser` collapse to 1-line wrappers.

- **Add a JSDoc `@example` on `listingsAcquiredByUser` showing the profile-screen integration** — analogous to the suggestion on `normalizeListing`. An `@example` snippet like `<View>{listingsAcquiredByUser(listings, user.id).map(l => <ListingCard listing={l} />)}</View>` makes the canonical consumer pattern visible in IntelliSense without forcing developers to scan call sites.

- **Add a `__tests__/marketplace-helpers-sort-parity.test.ts` that asserts every "listings for X" helper sorts the same shape** — today `listingsForUser`, `listingsAcquiredByUser` use createdAt-desc; `purchasesForUser` uses soldAt-desc. A structural test enumerating the helpers and pinning their sort key prevents a future "drift" where one helper switches to `updatedAt` and breaks the implicit contract.

- **Run `coerceListings` on the cloud-fetched payload too** — today `cloudFetchListings()` returns rows already mapped through `rowToListing`, but PostgREST schema drift (e.g. a column rename) could still produce malformed objects. Threading `coerceListings(rows)` through both the cloud and cache hydration paths makes `MarketplaceProvider` resilient to *every* upstream — not just AsyncStorage.

- **Add a one-line `console.warn("[marketplace] dropped %d corrupt listings", dropped)` when `coerceListings` filters out entries** — today a corrupt cache silently drops rows; an engineer investigating "where did my listing go" has no signal. Comparing `JSON.parse(raw).length` to the coerced length and warning when they differ would surface the issue without forcing a Sentry round-trip. Dev-only; gated on `__DEV__`.

- **Emit a Sentry breadcrumb (and optionally an analytics event) when `coerceListing` rejects a row in production** — the dev-only warn above is good for local debugging; in prod, threading the row id (or a hash of it) into `addBreadcrumb({ category: "marketplace", message: "dropped corrupt listing", data: { id: r.id } })` gives us telemetry on real cache corruption rates. Single import, single line.

- **Add a `coerceListing` JSDoc note covering the future Zod migration** — once a runtime-schema lib lands (Zod, Valibot, etc.), this hand-rolled validator becomes a 5-line `MarketplaceListingSchema.safeParse(raw).success ? data : null`. Tagging the current implementation `@deprecated once @/lib/schemas/marketplace lands` keeps the migration path obvious.

- **Add a `MarketplaceListing` JSON Schema doc generated from the `coerceListing` predicate list** — a single doc file (`docs/marketplace-listing.schema.md`) listing every field, its type, and whether nullability is allowed would make the contract auditable for backend engineers without forcing them to read TS. A `tsx` script that extracts the predicates from `coerceListing` source and prints the schema markdown closes the loop.

- **Cap the recently-sold carousel at a horizontal scroll on mobile** — today `recentlySoldListings(listings)` returns up to 12 cards and renders them in the same `<View style={styles.grid}>` flex-wrap layout as the active grid. On a single-column phone layout, that's 12 stacked cards taking up considerable scroll height. Wrapping the section in a `<ScrollView horizontal>` (mobile only, gated on `!isDesktop && !isTablet`) keeps the surface compact while still showing every entry.

- **Replace the inline `marketplaceSoldTo(name)` reuse with a dedicated `marketplaceSoldToPill(handle)` translation** — `marketplaceSoldTo` was originally written for the full sold-banner text ("Sold to @buyer"); reusing it on the card pill works but couples the two surfaces. A new key with a shorter variant ("→ @buyer") would let the card stay compact without forcing the banner text to shrink.

- **Expose `recentlySoldListings` on the `MarketplaceContext` value as `recentSales: MarketplaceListing[]`** — today the marketplace screen calls the helper directly. Hoisting it into the context (as a memoised slice) lets profile screens, listing detail "Recent comparable sales" sections, and the future analytics summary all consume the same precomputed list with the same default limit.

- **Add a `recentlySoldListings(listings, options: { since?: Date, limit?: number })` overload** — once the carousel becomes a "Recently sold this month" surface, the helper needs a time-window argument. Adding `since` (defaulting to `null` = no filter) keeps the current contract while letting new surfaces narrow the window without re-implementing the sort.

- **Cross-reference the "Recently sold" surface with the price-history panel on listing detail** — `priceHistoryForTitle` already walks the full listings list to find comparable titles for a given reference listing. The carousel could surface "tap an item to see how its price compares" by linking each card to the seller's listing detail with a `?priceHistoryTab=true` deep-link. Closes the loop between pricing context and the per-listing view.

- **Expose `mySales: MarketplaceListing[]` on `MarketplaceContext`** — today the profile screen calls `salesForUser(listings, activeProfile.id)` inline via `useMemo`. The mirror of `myPurchases` already lives on the context; hoisting `mySales` keeps the symmetry and lets future surfaces (analytics summary, "Sales this month" widget on the marketplace page, push-notification badges) consume the same precomputed slice without re-running the filter.

- **Add an aggregated "Net trading" line on the profile marketplace history** — sum the `askingPrice` of `mySales` minus the `askingPrice` of `myPurchases` (grouped by currency to avoid FX silently being wrong) and render it as a small footer. Gives collectors a one-glance audit of their marketplace activity without exporting data. Reuses the existing `format-cost` helper for currency-aware formatting.

- **Render a totals header for each sub-section ("Purchases (3) · $214 total")** — the new history rows show one listing per row, but the section is more useful if it answers "how many" and "for how much" at a glance. A 5-line `useMemo` over `myPurchases` / `mySales` summed by currency closes the gap; falls back to a count-only label when listings are pure trades without an asking price.

- **Filter the profile marketplace history by mode (trade vs sell) via a chip toggle** — the current shape interleaves trades and sales chronologically, which is correct but loses the "I want to see all my trades" use case. Adding two chips (`All` / `Trade` / `Sell`) above the list, gated on a local `useState`, would mirror the filter pattern already on the collection screen and reuse the existing `marketplaceModeSell` / `marketplaceModeTrade` i18n keys.

- **Surface the profile marketplace history on friend profiles too (read-only)** — today the section is gated on `isSelf`, but a friend's public sale history is just as useful for collectors evaluating who to trade with. A `isSelf || isFriend` gate plus an alternate empty-state copy ("No marketplace activity to show") would unlock the section without leaking private data (the data already flows from the shared `useMarketplace().listings` channel, which is RLS-gated server-side).

- **Wire DELETE postgres-changes into `subscribeToListings`** — the realtime channel now propagates INSERT + UPDATE, but if a seller deletes a still-active listing on device A, device B keeps showing it until the next `cloudFetchListings` refresh. Adding a third `.on(...)` registration that emits a tombstone (e.g. via a separate `onRemoved` callback or by emitting a row with `__deleted: true`) plus a `removeListingById` branch in the context callback closes the symmetric gap.

- **Persist the realtime-suppression window per listing id** — when a buyer claims a listing on device A, the optimistic local `setListings(... upsertListing ...)` write fires immediately, then the cloud PATCH lands and the realtime UPDATE arrives a moment later. The upsert handles the second write idempotently today, but if the local write fails (offline, RLS denial) the realtime UPDATE will still flip the row. Tracking an in-flight `pendingClaimIds: Set<string>` and reconciling against it would let the UI distinguish "claim succeeded server-side" from "claim landed somewhere else".

- **Hoist the cross-device "your listing was claimed" notification into the realtime callback** — now that the seller's device receives the UPDATE for their own listing's `sold_at` transition, the marketplace context could fire a `toast.success("Your listing was bought by @buyer")` when `row.ownerUserId === user.id && incoming.soldAt !== null && previous.soldAt === null`. Closes the feedback loop without polling or requiring the seller to refresh.

- **Add a `subscribeToMyListings(userId, handler)` overload that PG-filters server-side** — today every connected client receives every UPDATE in the `marketplace_listings` table, then filters client-side. For a "your listings only" use case (the seller-notification idea above) the server could pre-filter via `filter: \`owner_user_id=eq.${userId}\`` to cut wire chatter once the feature lands. Backwards-compatible — keeps the existing global stream for the marketplace browse page.

- **Run a Supabase migration that explicitly enables `REPLICA IDENTITY FULL` on `marketplace_listings`** — postgres-changes only emits `payload.old` correctly when the table has `REPLICA IDENTITY FULL` set; under the default REPLICA IDENTITY DEFAULT, `payload.old` only carries the primary key. The current code only reads `payload.new`, but if the seller-notification idea above (or any future diff-style consumer) needs the previous row state, the migration is the right time to set it. Document the SQL in `MANUAL-TASKS.md` per CLAUDE.md.

- **Add the cloud wrapper that INSERTs into `marketplace_transfers` on a successful claim** — the table is now defined and RLS-locked, but nothing writes to it yet. A `cloudRecordTransfer(listing)` helper in `lib/supabase-marketplace.ts` keyed off the existing `cloudMarkSold` call site would close the loop; the buyer's device fires both PATCH (mark sold) and POST (insert transfer) under the same auth session.

- **Add a `lib/supabase-marketplace-transfers-shapes.ts` pure module** mirroring `supabase-marketplace-shapes.ts` — URL builders, row→transfer mappers, and a `listingToTransferPayload(listing)` helper. Keeps the cloud wrapper thin and gives the future integration tests a synchronous typed surface to assert against without touching `@/lib/supabase`.

- **Render a "Purchases & Sales (audit)" toggle on the profile marketplace history section** — today the section reads from `useMarketplace().listings`, which is gone the moment a seller deletes their listing. Once we start writing to `marketplace_transfers`, that table becomes the canonical audit source and the section can fall back to it for "deleted listing" rows (with a "(listing removed)" badge in lieu of the photo). Closes the visible gap the migration just papered over server-side.

- **Add a `__tests__/marketplace-transfers-payload.test.ts` suite** that asserts the eventual `listingToTransferPayload` helper round-trips every field of a sold `MarketplaceListing` (id → listing_id, item_id, owner_user_id, buyer_user_id, mode, asking_price, currency) and bounds `transferred_at` to a parseable ISO 8601 timestamp. Locks the schema contract before the Edge Function / cloud wrapper has a chance to drift.

- **Promote the migration-structural-test pattern into a shared `__tests__/helpers/sql-migration-asserts.ts`** — the new `marketplace-transfers-migration.test.ts` re-uses the same `assertColumns / assertRlsEnabled / assertNoPolicies` shapes already implied by `analytics-events-migration.test.ts` and `chat-messages-migration.test.ts`. Hoisting them into a helper would drop the next migration test from ~140 to ~30 lines and force consistent terminology across the suite.

- **Render a real avatar thumbnail in the "From @seller" / "Sold to @buyer" pills** — the new `fromSeller` pill on My-purchases cards (and the existing sold-to pill) only shows a text handle. The `UserProfile` already carries an `avatarUrl`; wrapping the pill in a small `<Image>` + handle row would match the "avatar chip" framing of the original task and give a stronger visual identity to the counterparty.

- **Make the counterparty pill a deep link to the profile** — both the "From @seller" and "Sold to @buyer" pills are currently inert `<Text>` inside the card's outer `Link` to `/listing/[id]`. Nesting a `Link href={/profile/${owner.publicId}}` (with `onPress` stopPropagation) would let a buyer tap straight through to the seller's profile from the purchases grid, mirroring how `app/people.tsx` rows navigate.

- **Extract the duplicated pill markup into a `<CounterpartyPill prefix handle />` component** — the `soldToPill` View/Text pair is now rendered in three places in `app/marketplace.tsx` (sold-to on sales, sold-to on recently-sold, from-seller on purchases) with identical styles and only the i18n key differing. A 10-line shared component keyed by `kind: "from" | "soldTo"` removes the copy-paste and the risk of style drift.

- **Add a unit-testable `counterpartyHandle(profile)` helper in `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts`** — the `@${profile.username ?? profile.publicId ?? profile.id}` coalesce now appears twice in `ListingCard` (buyer + seller). Promoting it to a pure helper gives the fallback chain a single home and a paired test asserting the username→publicId→id precedence, instead of relying on inline duplication.

- **Surface the "From @seller" provenance on the item-detail screen too** — the buyer's Acquired item already records `acquiredFrom` (seller @username) per the recent provenance task; rendering the same "From @seller" pill on `app/item/[id].tsx` for acquired items would keep the provenance treatment consistent between the marketplace purchases grid and the item's own detail view.

- **Add a matching `since?: Date` to `salesForUser` and `listingsAcquiredByUser`** — `purchasesForUser` now supports a date cap, but the sibling sold/acquired selectors don't. A profile "this month" toggle would want symmetric filtering across all three; extracting a shared `withinSince(soldAt, sinceMs)` predicate keeps the parse-and-compare logic in one tested place.

- **Expose `purchasesForUser(listings, id, since)` through `useMarketplace()` as a `purchasesSince(date)` selector** — today the context only memoises the full `myPurchases`. A thin `useCallback` wrapper would let a profile screen request "purchases this month" without importing the pure helper directly, mirroring how other context selectors hide the helper layer.

- **Guard against a `since` in the future** — passing a `since` later than `Date.now()` silently returns an empty list. A dev-only `__DEV__` warning (or clamping `since` to now) would surface a caller bug where a timezone/parsing mistake produces a future bound, instead of rendering a confusing empty "purchases this month".

- **Add a `lib/time-helpers.ts:startOfMonth(now?)` helper** — the obvious first caller of the new `since` arg is "purchases this month", which needs the first instant of the current month in the user's locale. Centralising `startOfMonth` / `startOfWeek` there (paired with unit tests for month/year boundaries) avoids each screen rolling its own `new Date(y, m, 1)` arithmetic.

- **Document the `soldAt`-vs-`createdAt` semantics of the `since` cap in the profile history doc** — `purchasesForUser` filters and now caps on `soldAt` (sale-close time), while `listingsAcquiredByUser` sorts on `createdAt` (listing-appearance time). A short note in the marketplace-history section prevents a future "why does my 'this month' count differ between the two surfaces?" confusion.

- **Memoise `<ListingGrid>` with `React.memo`** — the grid now recomputes its `cardWrapStyle` per `columns` change (good), but the component itself re-renders whenever `MarketplaceScreen` does. Wrapping it in `React.memo` (and stabilising the inline `resolveBuyer` arrows with `useCallback`) would skip re-rendering the active grid when only the purchases/sales memos change.

- **Hoist `ListingGrid` + `ListingCard` into `components/marketplace/`** — both are now reusable, screen-agnostic pieces. Moving them out of `app/marketplace.tsx` into a `components/` module would let the profile "Marketplace history" surface (`app/profile/[id].tsx`) render the same grid instead of its bespoke list, unifying the two trading views.

- **Pass an `emptyState` slot into `ListingGrid`** — the active-listings branch still hand-rolls its own `<EmptyState>` outside the grid while the three section grids silently render nothing when empty. Folding an optional `empty` render prop into `ListingGrid` would let every surface share the same "nothing here yet" treatment and remove the `resolved.length === 0` ternary from the screen body.

- **Give `ListingGrid` a `numColumns`-aware `gap` token instead of negative margins** — the grid uses `marginHorizontal: -6` + per-cell `padding: 6` to fake a gutter. Now that the grid is a single component, switching to flex `gap` (supported in RN 0.71+) removes the fragile negative-margin hack and the row-wrap edge artifacts on the last row.

- **Add a `testID`/`accessibilityRole="list"` to `ListingGrid`** — a single wrapper is the right place to attach list semantics for screen readers and for future e2e tests, instead of the four anonymous `<View style={styles.grid}>` blocks that existed before. One change now covers every marketplace surface.

- **Add a `daysSincePurchase(listing, now?)` helper** to pair with `purchasesAwaitingArrival` — a "Mark as received" CTA usually nudges harder as a shipment ages ("ordered 9 days ago — did it arrive?"). A pure helper computing the gap between `soldAt` and now keeps that escalation logic out of the component.

- **Extend `markListingArrived` with an optional `force` flag** for an admin/dispute "reset arrival" path — today it's strictly idempotent (keeps the first stamp), which is correct for buyers, but a future dispute-resolution screen may need to clear/replace `arrivedAt`. A `{ force?: boolean }` option keeps the default safe while unblocking the admin case.

- **Add a `salesAwaitingDelivery(listings, userId)` mirror** of `purchasesAwaitingArrival` for the seller side — `ownerUserId === userId && soldAt != null && arrivedAt == null`. The seller-side "delivery confirmed" sub-task will want exactly this filter to badge which of their sales are still unconfirmed.

- **Surface a `coerceListing` drop-counter** — `coerceListings` silently drops malformed rows (now including bad `arrivedAt`). Returning `{ listings, dropped }` (or logging a one-time `console.warn` with the count) would let the cache-hydration path emit telemetry when a corrupt local payload loses rows, instead of failing silently.

- **Document the `arrived_at` column ahead of the migration sub-task** — add the `ALTER TABLE marketplace_listings ADD COLUMN arrived_at timestamptz` snippet to `MANUAL-TASKS.md` now (gated "pending sub-task 5") so the schema change is captured the moment the field landed in the type, per the CLAUDE.md DB-change rule.

- **Expose `purchasesAwaitingArrival` through `useMarketplace()` as a memoised `myAwaitingArrival`** — the buyer-UI sub-task will want the unreceived-purchases slice; surfacing it next to `myPurchases`/`mySales` (one `useMemo` keyed on `user`) keeps the screen from importing the pure helper and re-deriving it.

- **Fire a `purchase_received` analytics event from `markListingReceived`** — the sold/claim flow already emits funnel events; stamping receipt is the natural "delivery confirmed" funnel endpoint. Gate it behind the same `trackEvent` taxonomy so dispute/fulfillment dashboards can measure time-to-receipt.

- **Add a `receivedListingPayload(arrivedAt)` shape helper** in `lib/supabase-marketplace-shapes.ts` ahead of the cloud sub-task — mirrors `markSoldPayload`; pre-extracting the `{ arrived_at }` PATCH body gives the future `cloudMarkReceived` wrapper a typed, unit-tested surface before the migration lands.

- **Guard `markListingReceived` against a missing `user` more loudly in dev** — today it silently returns when `user?.id` is null. A `__DEV__` warning ("markListingReceived called without an authenticated user") would catch a call-site that renders the CTA outside the auth gate, instead of a confusing no-op.

- **Reconcile `arrivedAt` in the realtime UPDATE path** — once the cloud column exists, a buyer confirming receipt on device A should clear the "Mark as received" CTA on device B. `normalizeListing(incoming)` already carries `arrivedAt`, so the existing `upsertListing` in `subscribeToListings` will propagate it; add a regression test asserting the realtime echo keeps the stamp.

- **Use `parseCurrencyValue` in the item-edit save path** — `handleSaveEdit` still parses cost via `Number(editCost.replace(",", "."))`, while the listing flow uses the shared `parseCurrencyValue` (rejects ≤0 / non-finite). Switching the edit path to the same helper removes the duplicate parse and the "0 is a valid cost" inconsistency between add/edit/list flows.

- **Default the edit currency picker to the item's collection currency** — `enterEditMode` seeds `editCurrency` from `costCurrency ?? preferred ?? language-default`. When an item has no stored currency, defaulting to the parent collection's `currency` override (when set) would better match what the user sees on the collection total, instead of a possibly-different device preference.

- **Surface the full ISO-4217 search picker in `CurrencyInput`** — the inline chips only show `CURRENCY_CHIPS` (10 currencies). The add form's `CurrencySheet` offers autocomplete over the full `lib/currencies.ts` dictionary; wiring a "more…" affordance on `CurrencyInput` that opens `CurrencySheet` would let editors pick a currency outside the shortlist (the add form already can).

- **Add an analytics `item_currency_changed` event** — now that currency is editable, firing a `trackEvent` when `editCurrency !== activeItem.costCurrency` on save would measure how often users correct a mis-entered currency, informing whether the cross-device conversion work (bug-2) is worth prioritising.

- **Guard against a cost with no currency on save** — `updateItem` now writes `costCurrency: null` when cost is cleared, which is correct, but a non-null cost should never persist a null/empty currency. A tiny invariant test (cost set ⇒ costCurrency is a valid ISO-4217 code) in `item-edit-currency.test.ts` would lock the pairing before bug-2's conversion code starts trusting it.

- **Reuse `convertItemCost` inside `getCollectionTotalCost`** — the total currently maps items to `{amount, currency}` then calls `sumConverted`. Folding the per-item helper into the totals path (sum each `convertItemCost(item, target)` result) would give one conversion definition and let the total surface a per-item "skipped" reason consistent with what bug-2b renders.

- **Add a `formatConvertedCost(result, t)` UI helper** — bug-2b will format `ConvertedItemCost` in three places (item-card compact, item-card full, item detail). Extracting `≈ {amount} {currency}` vs raw-fallback formatting into one helper (with the new i18n "approx." key) avoids three drifting copies before the render task starts.

- **Round converted amounts to the currency's minor unit** — `convertItemCost` returns a raw float (e.g. 90.00000001). A `roundToCurrency(amount, currency)` step (2dp for most, 0dp for JPY/RUB-style) would stop the UI from showing 12-decimal noise once bug-2b renders the value.

- **Memoise the bound `convertItemCost` selector** — it's recreated on every context value rebuild. Wrapping it in `useCallback` keyed on `[displayCurrency, currencyRates]` keeps referential stability so item-card lists that depend on it via `useMemo` don't re-render on unrelated context changes.

- **Expose rate freshness alongside conversions** — `convertItemCost` silently uses whatever `currencyRates` is loaded. Surfacing the `fetchedAt` timestamp (or an `isStale` flag) on the context would let bug-2d's "rates updated {when}" affordance and a "showing day-old rates" hint read from one source instead of re-loading the cache.

- **Round converted totals in `getCollectionTotalCost` with `formatCostAmount`** — the collection total still renders the raw summed float. Reusing the new `formatCostAmount` (and a per-currency minor-unit rule) on the total card would stop a converted total from showing long decimal noise, matching the per-item display now shipped in bug-2b.

- **Memoise the per-card conversion in lists** — `item-card` calls `getCollectionById` (an O(n) find) + `convertItemCost` on every render. For a long grid this is O(n·m); passing a resolved `targetCurrency` prop down from the list (computed once per collection) or memoising `getCollectionById` as a `Map` would cut redundant work once bug-2c lands and currency changes trigger re-renders.

- **Show a "rates unavailable" hint when `converted===false` across a screen** — today a missing-rate item silently falls back to its stored currency with no signal. A subtle inline icon or a one-time toast ("showing original currencies — rates unavailable") would explain why some values differ, feeding naturally into bug-2d's settings hint.

- **Add an analytics `item_cost_converted` sample event** — emitting a low-rate sampled event when an item renders an "≈" converted value would measure how many users actually benefit from cross-device conversion, helping prioritise bug-2c/2d.

- **Long-press original on item-card too (without breaking navigation)** — bug-2b deliberately skipped `onLongPress` on the card cost to avoid hijacking the card's tap-to-open. A dedicated tiny `<Pressable>` around just the cost `Text` with `delayLongPress` tuned so a normal tap still bubbles to the `Link` would give native users the same long-press-to-reveal-original affordance the detail screen has.

- **Sync the upsertMyProfile path on sign-up too** — `upsertProfileBody` now carries `display_currency`, but a fresh sign-up creates the row before the user has picked a currency, persisting NULL. Seeding it from the device-local `getUserPreferredCurrency()` at first upsert would give a returning device its currency immediately, before the bug-2c hydration round-trip.

- **Reconcile display currency via the profiles realtime channel** — bug-2c hydrates on sign-in only; a currency change on device A wont reach an already-open device B until it reloads. Subscribing to the profile row (mirroring the listings realtime path) and calling `setDisplayCurrencyState` on the incoming `display_currency` would make the sync live.

- **Thread profile sync into the per-form currency write-throughs** — item-edit and listing forms call `setUserPreferredCurrency` (device-local) directly. Routing those through the new context `setDisplayCurrency` (or a thinner `syncPreferredCurrency`) would keep the profile column authoritative instead of letting a form silently diverge from the synced value.

- **Add a fetch+mock integration test for `updateMyProfileDisplayCurrency`** — todays coverage is structural (regex) + pure-shape. A test that mocks `fetchWithRetry`/`getAccessToken` and asserts the PATCH URL + `{ display_currency }` body (mirroring `supabase-marketplace.test.ts`) would guard the wrapper layer against a future refactor dropping the column.

- **Surface displayCurrency in the profile editor** — now that its a real profile field, the profile-edit screen could expose it alongside bio/avatar, so the "Display currency" control lives both in Settings (bug-2d) and on the profile, keeping the model and UI consistent.

- **Show absolute rate timestamp on long-press in settings** — the "rates updated {when}" row uses `formatRelativeDate`; mirroring the listing-detail long-press→`toast.info(formatAbsoluteDate(...))` pattern would let power users see the exact fetch time, consistent with the item-detail cost tooltip shipped in bug-2b.

- **Toast feedback after a manual rate refresh** — `handleRefreshRates` silently flips the timestamp; a success/failure toast (reusing `ToastProvider`) would confirm the network round-trip, especially when the fetch fails and the cached rates are kept.

- **Disable-state styling for the refresh row while in flight** — `refreshingRates` guards re-entrancy but the row looks identical mid-fetch. Dimming it (opacity) or swapping the label to a "Refreshing…" i18n key would give visible feedback on slow networks.

- **Surface stale-rate warning using `isStale`** — `lib/currency-rates.ts` already exports `isStale`; settings could compare `currencyRatesUpdatedAt` against `RATES_TTL_MS` and nudge the user to refresh when the cached table is >24h old, instead of only signalling the all-or-nothing unavailable case.

- **Reuse the settings currency card pattern as a shared `<DisplayCurrencyField>`** — bug-2d duplicates a picker + sheet wiring that the profile editor (and any future "preferences" surface) will want. Extracting it would keep `setDisplayCurrency`/`CurrencySheet` plumbing in one place.

## visual-upgrade PR4 follow-ups (2026-05-29)

- **Memoize `useAppTheme()` slot objects** — the hook returns the frozen `LIGHT`/`DARK` constants directly so identity is already stable, but the per-component inline `{ ...styles.x, color: theme.y }` spreads allocate a fresh object every render. For hot lists (item-card in masonry/FlatList) wrapping the dynamic style in `useMemo(() => ({...}), [theme])` would cut allocations and let `React.memo` short-circuit.

- **Add a `theme.shadow` slot instead of importing `SHADOW_SOFT` per file** — PR4 spreads the raw `SHADOW_SOFT` token in item-card. Folding shadow (and a dark-mode-tuned variant) into the `AppTheme` mapping would keep elevation consistent and let dark mode drop/soften shadows where they read as muddy.

- **Respect an in-app theme override, not just OS `useColorScheme()`** — `useAppTheme()` is purely OS-driven. A settings toggle (system / light / dark) persisted like `displayCurrency` would let users force a mode; the hook could read a lightweight `ThemeContext` first and fall back to `useColorScheme()`.

- **Dark-mode pass on the still-static nested surfaces** — empty-state's icon rings (`CARD_BG_2/3/14`) and bottom-nav's modal sheet (`CARD_BG_2/3`) stayed on light tokens in PR4. A focused sweep mapping those to `theme.cardElevated`/`theme.card` would remove the light "islands" that show through in dark mode.

- **Snapshot/visual regression harness for the themed components** — the new structural tests assert imports/tokens but not rendered output. A jest + react-test-renderer (or Storybook + Chromatic) snapshot of each shared component in light & dark would catch unintended color/radius regressions in PRs 5–8.

A single `<CoverHero radius title subtitle>` would dedupe the gradient stops and guarantee PR6/PR7 stay visually consistent.

Rather than leaving them scattered across `.suggestions.md`, fold them into a single "PR10 · dark-mode finish" task with a per-file checklist so the deferred work is actionable in one pass.
- **Add a CI guard that fails on new 6-digit hex literals** — `lint:hex` already exists; wiring it as a required check (it may already run in `validate`) plus a short CONTRIBUTING note would stop the design-token regressions the PR-series spent effort cleaning up from creeping back in.
- **Snapshot-test `useAppTheme()` LIGHT/DARK maps** — the whole visual-upgrade series routes color through `useAppTheme()`; a single snapshot of the LIGHT and DARK objects would lock the palette so an accidental token swap in `use-app-theme.ts` surfaces as a failing diff instead of silently shifting every screen.
- **Document the editorial-font + airy-geometry conventions in CLAUDE.md** — now that every screen uses `FONT_DISPLAY_EDITORIAL` for titles and `RADIUS_HERO_LG`/`RADIUS_ITEM_AIRY`/`SHADOW_SOFT` for cards, a short "Styling conventions" subsection would let future screens adopt the system without reverse-engineering it from siblings.
- **Add a real `useColorScheme` toggle in settings** — the theme infra reads the OS scheme but there's no in-app override. A "Appearance: System / Light / Dark" picker (persisted like `displayCurrency`) would make the dark-mode work the series enabled actually reachable for users whose OS scheme differs from their preference.

- **Add the migrations→scratch-DB replay as a required PR check** — `supabase-test.yml` (BE-31) now replays every migration from empty on PRs touching `supabase/**`.
