Marking it a required status check (once it's proven stable on a few PRs) would stop a broken/out-of-order migration from merging, the same way the live `supabase-migrations.yml` push is the only current safety net.
- **Pin the Supabase CLI version in `supabase-test.yml`** — the workflow installs `version: latest`, so a CLI release that changes the `config.toml` schema or `supabase db start` behavior could turn the check red with no repo change. Pinning to a known-good version (and bumping deliberately) makes the harness reproducible, matching the version-pinning the rest of the actions use.
- **Grow `supabase/tests/` into real RLS + FK-cascade pgTAP (BE-12/BE-36)** — the smoke test only asserts table/column presence. The harness is now in place, so the highest-value next step is per-table anon/leak RLS tests and `delete-account` cascade tests so security regressions fail in CI rather than in production.
- **Cache the Supabase CLI / Docker layers in `supabase-test.yml`** — `supabase db start` pulls several Docker images on every run. An `actions/cache` step (or the CLI's image cache) keyed on the CLI version would cut minutes off each PR, mirroring the Expo/Metro cache already in `ci.yml`.
- **Reuse `config.toml` for a real bootstrap-from-empty E2E (BE-4)** — now that `supabase/config.toml` is committed, BE-4's "stand up a throwaway project from committed migrations" is mostly a docs + one-time manual step. A `supabase link` + `supabase db push` against a scratch hosted project, documented in README-DEPLOY, would close the loop the local scratch-DB check can't (real auth/storage/edge wiring).

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-16, after BE-4 bootstrap docs)
- **CI assert migration apply-order list stays in sync** — `fresh-project-bootstrap-docs.test.ts` checks README-DEPLOY's apply-order block lists every committed migration in lexicographic order. Promote this into a shared helper reused by `migration-versions`/`check-migration-docs` so a single source of truth lists migrations once and every doc/test derives from it, preventing the list drifting when a new migration lands.
- **Add a `scripts/bootstrap-fresh-project.sh` from the BE-4 doc** — the README now spells out `supabase link` → `db push` → `functions deploy delete-account/delete-image/analytics-mirror`. Codifying that as an idempotent, parameterised script (project-ref + connection string as args) removes copy-paste error from the one manual step and gives BE-25's cascade verification a repeatable scratch project.
- **Surface a build-time Supabase-reachability preflight** — the bootstrap's "point a build at the project" step fails silently if the URL/key are wrong (disabled login buttons). A `scripts/check-supabase-env.ts` that pings `${EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL}/auth/v1/health` during `npm run build` (warn-only) would catch a mis-pasted credential before deploy.
- **Document the edge-function secrets each function needs** — the bootstrap deploys three edge functions, but each (delete-image SEC-1, analytics-mirror) needs its own `supabase secrets set` values. A per-function secrets table in README-DEPLOY mirroring the GitHub-secrets table would make a fresh project fully reproducible.
- **Generalise the bootstrap end-to-end checklist into a smoke pgTAP/seed** — the 4-step manual confirmation (OTP, collection+item, friend accept, RLS deny) maps directly onto the BE-12b pgTAP plan. Sharing one fixture between the manual checklist and the automated RLS suite keeps the human and CI checks asserting the same invariants.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-16, after BE-12b RLS pgTAP)
- **Make `supabase-test.yml` a required status check** — now that there's real RLS pgTAP (BE-12b) plus the smoke test, a green Supabase Tests run is meaningful. Marking it required (once stable) stops an RLS-weakening migration from merging, which the offline JS guards can't catch.
- **Extend the pgTAP fixture to BE-25 cascade tests** — `01_core_tables_rls.sql` already seeds a full 4-user social graph. Reusing that seed (factor it into a shared `supabase/tests/_fixtures.sql`) for FK `ON DELETE CASCADE` assertions (delete an auth.users row → collections/items/friend_requests vanish) closes BE-25/BE-36 cheaply.
- **Add an anon-role deny block to the RLS pgTAP** — the current test exercises the `authenticated` role across tenants. A short `set local role anon` section asserting zero rows / write denies on all four tables would prove the unauthenticated surface is fully closed, mirroring the BE-12a file-scan check executably.
- **CI guard that every RLS policy has a pgTAP assertion** — parse `20260616_core_tables_rls.sql` policy names and assert each appears (by table+command) in `01_core_tables_rls.sql`, so a new policy can't ship without coverage (generalises the plan-count guard already added).
- **Negative test for the friend_requests immutability (no UPDATE policy)** — the migration deliberately omits an UPDATE policy on friend_requests. Add a pgTAP case asserting an UPDATE by either party affects 0 rows, documenting that "unfriend = DELETE, not UPDATE" is enforced and not just convention.

- **Migration apply-order test (BE-34, partly motivated by SEC-ADMIN-1)** — SEC-ADMIN-1 had to be dated `20260617` because a same-day numeric suffix sorts *before* `20260616_core_tables_rls.sql`'s `_`. A test asserting each migration's dependency order (e.g. anything REVOKE/GRANTing `is_admin` sorts after the migration that adds the column) would catch a mis-dated security migration before it silently runs too early.
- **`information_schema` grant-audit pgTAP** — add a pgTAP case reading `role_column_grants` to assert `authenticated` holds UPDATE on every profiles column EXCEPT `is_admin`, turning the SEC-ADMIN-1 MANUAL-TASKS audit query into an executable invariant instead of a manual checklist step.
- **Generalise the column-grant guard to every sensitive column** — `is_admin` is one server-only flag; future ones (e.g. a `verified`/`role` column) will hit the same table-vs-column REVOKE trap. A small `lib/` helper listing "service-role-only columns" + a CI check that each is excluded from the per-role GRANT would prevent re-introducing the hole.
- **Edge Function for admin promotion (consideration #3)** — move admin grants fully server-side: a `promote-admin` Edge Function gated on an existing admin's service-role check, so the flag is never reachable from any client SQL path and the per-column GRANT dance becomes belt-and-suspenders.
- **Replay-idempotency harness for grants** — REVOKE/GRANT migrations are declarative but easy to get subtly wrong on re-run; a CI step that applies every migration twice against the scratch DB (BE-31 runner) and diffs `\dp public.profiles` would prove the final grant state is stable under replay.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-17, after BE-36 FK/cascade pgTAP)
- **Factor a shared `supabase/tests/_fixtures.sql`** — `01_core_tables_rls.sql` and `02_fk_cascade.sql` now each seed near-identical 2–4 user social graphs (users → profiles → collections → items → friend_requests). Extracting one `\i`-included fixture removes the duplicated UUID constants and keeps the two suites asserting over the same canonical graph as schema columns evolve.
- **pgTAP coverage for the `delete-account` Edge Function's app-layer pre-delete sweep** — BE-36 proves the DB CASCADE, but `delete-account` also explicitly deletes storage/image rows before calling `auth.admin.deleteUser`. A fake-fetcher integration test (BE-35) asserting that pre-delete request shape would close the gap between "DB cascades" and "the function actually triggers the cascade".
- **Assert `ON DELETE` *action* in catalog, not just behaviour** — add a pgTAP block reading `pg_constraint.confdeltype` (`c`=cascade, `n`=set null) for every FK to `auth.users`, so a future migration that flips a CASCADE to NO ACTION fails CI even if no seed row happens to exercise that path.
- **Cross-check FK list against a generated manifest** — derive the expected `(table, column, on_delete)` FK list from the migration SQL once and assert both the pgTAP fixture and an offline structural test consume it, so a newly added auth.users-referencing table can't ship without a cascade assertion (generalises BE-36 to BE-6's "every new table").
- **Marketplace_listings.item_id / marketplace_transfers.listing_id are text, not FKs** — both reference other rows by free-text id with no constraint (intentional, per the transfers migration comment, to survive listing deletes). Documenting this "soft reference" choice in MANUAL-TASKS + a test asserting they are deliberately NOT FKs would stop a well-meaning future migration from adding a CASCADE that re-introduces the history-loss bug.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-8 FK index coverage)
- **pgTAP index-coverage invariant** — turn BE-8's offline "every FK has a leading-column index" structural check into an executable pgTAP block reading `pg_index`/`pg_constraint` against the live-schema scratch DB (BE-31 runner), so a future `auth.users`-referencing table that ships without a covering index fails CI even if the offline regex misses it.
- **`EXPLAIN`-backed hot-path assertions** — the BE-8 indexes only matter if the planner uses them. A pgTAP test running `EXPLAIN` on the app's actual hot queries (`itemsByCollectionUrl`, `collectionsByUserUrl`, the friend_requests OR-filter) and asserting an Index Scan (not Seq Scan) would catch a silently-unused index after a column/filter change.
- **Drop the now-redundant `marketplace_listings_item_idx`?** — `item_id` is a free-text soft reference (not a FK); its single-column index is only useful if the app filters listings by item. Audit the query shapes and either document why it's kept or drop it to save write throughput — same audit lens BE-8 applied to FKs, now applied to non-FK indexes.
- **Partial index for live (non-archived) items** — `items.archived_at IS NULL` is the dominant read filter post-sale; a partial index `items(collection_id) WHERE archived_at IS NULL` would keep the hot collection-detail read tight as archived rows accumulate, without bloating the cascade-delete index.
- **Index-bloat / unused-index CI report** — add a periodic job querying `pg_stat_user_indexes` on a representative dataset to flag indexes with zero scans, closing the loop on BE-8: we added coverage, but nothing yet tells us when an index stops earning its keep.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-9 updated_at + moddatetime)
- **pgTAP for the moddatetime trigger** — add a `supabase/tests/03_updated_at.sql` block that inserts a row, captures `updated_at`, `UPDATE`s it, and asserts the new `updated_at` is strictly greater on every mutable table — turning BE-9's offline structural check into an executable invariant on the Docker supabase-test CI (the trigger silently not firing would otherwise pass CI).
- **Backfill `updated_at` from `created_at` on existing rows** — `ADD COLUMN ... DEFAULT now()` stamps every *pre-existing* row with the migration time, so the first delta pull after deploy sees the entire table as "just changed". A one-time `UPDATE ... SET updated_at = created_at` (where a creation timestamp exists) would give historical rows an honest cursor and avoid a thundering-herd first sync (BE-14 dependency).
- **Wire `updated_at` into the read shapes now** — `DbProfile`/`DbCollection`/`DbItem` don't yet select or carry `updated_at`; threading it through `lib/supabase-profiles-shapes.ts` (select lists) + the row types is the prerequisite half of BE-14's `lastSyncedAt` cursor and can ship independently as a no-behavior-change PR.
- **Assert the trigger function is `extensions.moddatetime`, not a hand-rolled one** — a future migration could shadow `handle_updated_at` with a custom function; a parity test (or pgTAP catalog read of `pg_trigger`/`pg_proc`) asserting all nine triggers point at the same `extensions.moddatetime` keeps the bump logic uniform.
- **Guard against new tables shipping without `updated_at`** — generalise BE-9's nine-table list into a CI check (like the FK-coverage guard) that fails when a `CREATE TABLE public.*` lands in `supabase/migrations/*` without a matching `updated_at` column + `handle_updated_at` trigger, so the delta-pull cursor stays schema-wide as tables are added.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-10 not-null defaults + coerce validators)
- **Route every `await res.json()` through the `coerce*` validators, not just the `to*` mappers** — `supabase-profiles.ts` still casts raw JSON to `DbProfile[]`/`DbItem[]` etc. before mapping; a few ad-hoc reads (e.g. the wishlist-collection existence check, `ensureWishlistCollection`) parse JSON inline without coercion. Auditing every `.json()` call site to feed the typed coercers would close the last gap where a malformed row bypasses the BE-10 guard.
- **Generate the not-null column list from base_schema, don't hand-maintain it** — `20260622_not_null_defaults.sql` hard-codes the (table, column, default) triples that base_schema already declares. A small script (or pgTAP) that diffs the migration's VALUES list against the `NOT NULL DEFAULT` columns in `20260423_base_schema.sql` would fail CI if base_schema gains a new client-guaranteed column the repair migration forgets.
- **pgTAP for the repair migration** — turn BE-10's offline structural test into an executable block on the Docker supabase-test CI: create a table with a nullable column holding a NULL row, run the repair, assert the row was backfilled and the column is now `attnotnull` with the expected `adbin` default — proving the three-step DDL actually fires (a silent no-op would pass the structural regex).
- **Property-test the coercers against the seed data** — feed every row in `data/seed.ts`/`data/social-seed.ts` (and a fuzz set of partial/garbage objects) through `coerceItemRow`/`coerceCollectionRow`/`coerceProfileRow` and assert the result always satisfies the TS type at runtime (no undefined required fields, arrays are arrays), catching a future field added to the type but forgotten in the coercer.
- **Share the coercion seam with the AsyncStorage hydration path** — `collections-context`/`social-context` hydrate from local JSON with their own `?? []`/`?? ""` defaulting scattered inline. Reusing the BE-10 `coerce*` helpers (or a sibling that maps camelCase local shapes) would unify "harden a row from any source" into one tested module and delete the duplicated defensive defaults.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-13a sync-engine core)
- **A `flushAll` convenience that threads state through `applyFlushToQueue`/`remapsOnly`** — every consumer (chat now, collections/items/social next) will repeat the same three-step dance: call `flushPendingQueue`, early-return on empty `sent`, then `setState` applying `applyFlushToQueue` + walking `remapsOnly` to rewrite cache ids. A higher-order `runFlush(pending, options, { onSettled })` helper that returns `{ nextPending, remaps }` (or `null` when nothing flushed) would delete that boilerplate from each context and keep the "skip no-op state update" guard in one place.
- **Surface a `failedGroups` set from `flushPendingQueue`** — the engine currently only reports successes; a consumer that wants to show a per-entity "couldn't sync" badge (BE-16's pending pill) has to diff the queue. Returning the groups that stopped at a failure (and optionally the first failing id) would let the UI distinguish "still queued, will retry" from "delivered" without a second pass.
- **Bounded retry / backoff metadata on queued entities** — an entity that always fails `deliver` (e.g. a row RLS rejects) stays at the head of its group forever, blocking everything behind it. Tracking an attempt count + last-attempt timestamp per entity (and skipping/parking after N attempts) would stop one poison row from wedging an entire group's flush order.
- **Concurrent cross-group flush** — groups are independent (a failure in one never blocks another), yet `flushPendingQueue` walks them sequentially. For many friends/collections this serialises N independent network round-trips. A `Promise.all` over groups (still sequential *within* a group to preserve send order) would cut reconnect-flush latency, gated by a small concurrency limit.
- **Generalise the BE-5 legacy-id remap into the engine's mint step** — `normalizeOwnItemIds` (items) and the chat uuid remap both exist because legacy non-uuid ids can't reconcile. The engine already mints a uuid at flush time; exposing an optional `onRemap(oldId,newId)` hook (or reusing `remapsOnly` at hydrate) would let collections/items drop their bespoke normalize pass and rely on the engine as the single place legacy ids get healed.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-13b chat adopts sync-engine)
- **Extract the `setStore` reducer half into the engine too** — every consumer now repeats the same `applyFlushToQueue` + `remapsOnly`-loop shape inside its own `setState`. A `reduceFlushedState({ pending, byGroupCache }, sent, getId, applyRemap)` helper returning `{ nextPending, nextCache }` would let chat/collections/items/social share the cache-rewrite loop instead of each re-deriving it, shrinking BE-13c/d to "define deliver + wire state".
- **A `deliverResult` richer than boolean** — `cloudSendMessage` returns the server `ChatMessage` (with the authoritative `createdAt`), but the engine's `deliver` collapses it to `!= null`, so the context can't adopt the server row. Letting `deliver` return `T | null` (null = failure) and surfacing the delivered payload in `SentEntry` would let consumers reconcile server-authoritative fields (timestamps, ordering) in the same pass.
- **Persist the pending queue through one storage seam** — chat hand-rolls `pendingByChatId` in its `ChatStore` AsyncStorage blob; collections/items/social will each need the same durable queue. A tiny `usePendingQueue(storageKey)` hook (load/persist/enqueue/applyFlush) over the engine would stop three contexts re-implementing the persistence + `pendingRef` mirror.
- **Unit-test the chat `deliver` boolean coercion** — the refactor hinges on `(await cloudSendMessage(...)) != null` mapping the `ChatMessage | null` return to the engine's `boolean` contract; a focused test (mock cloud send returning a message vs null vs the idempotent-empty synthesize path) would lock that coercion so a future signature change can't silently re-queue delivered messages.
- **Document the engine's group-key contract** — chat's group key (`chatId`) happens to equal `msg.chatId`, but the engine trusts `Object.entries(pending)` keys, not the entity. A short note (or a dev-only assert) that the queue key must match however the consumer routes `deliver` would prevent a future consumer keying by user-id while delivering by collection-id and silently mis-pruning.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-18, after BE-13c collections/items adopt sync-engine)
- **Extract `syncCollection`/`syncItem` into a reusable `useDurableUpsert(queue, getId, deliver)` hook** — `collections-context` now hand-rolls two near-identical wrappers (write → dequeue-on-success / enqueue-on-failure) plus a `pendingRef` mirror and a flush effect. BE-13d (social) will need the same shape; lifting it into one hook over `pending-upserts` would collapse both contexts to "define the cloud write + getId" and keep the persist/flush/clobber-safe-apply logic in one tested place.
- **Coalesce the per-row flush into a batch PostgREST upsert** — the flush effect re-delivers each queued entity with its own `upsertItem`/`upsertCollection` round-trip; a queue built up over a long offline session means N requests on reconnect. PostgREST accepts an array body for a single multi-row `ON CONFLICT` upsert, so a `deliverBatch(entities)` path (still uuid-keyed, still idempotent) would cut reconnect latency dramatically.
- **A "pending sync" pill driven off `hasPendingUpserts`** — BE-16 wants a syncing indicator; the queues now expose exactly the signal. Surfacing `pendingCollections`/`pendingItems` counts (plus chat's) through a shared `usePendingSyncCount()` would let the home header show "N changes waiting to sync" and a manual "retry now" that just bumps `refreshTick`.
- **Tombstone queue for offline deletes (pairs with BE-15)** — deletes today are fire-and-forget `deleteRemote*().catch()`, so a delete issued offline never retries and the row reappears on the next cloud pull. A sibling pending-DELETE queue (uuid-keyed, flushed after upserts) over the same engine would make offline deletes as durable as offline upserts; the current dequeue-on-delete guard only prevents local resurrection, not cloud divergence.
- **Reconnect trigger instead of refresh-tick polling** — the flush only fires on `ready`/`user`/`refreshTick`, so a queue parked while offline waits for the next manual refresh or screen re-mount. Wiring the flush to a real connectivity signal (the realtime client's `realtimeOnline` transition, or `NetInfo`) would flush the instant the network returns rather than on the next incidental re-render.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-19, after BE-14 delta pulls)
- **Promote the cold-bootstrap path to seed the cursor (skip the redundant first full pull)** — the empty-storage bootstrap in `collections-context` pulls everything via `fetchCollectionsByUserId` + per-collection items but never writes a sync cursor, so the very first warm `syncFromCloud` re-pulls the whole table again (since=null) before settling into delta mode. Having the bootstrap call `maxUpdatedAt` over its fetched rows and `setSyncCursor` would make the second pull a true delta and halve fresh-sign-in egress.
- **Extend delta pulls to friends'/shared/followed reads** — BE-14 only wired the user's OWN collections+items. The `friendCollections`/`subscribedCollections`/`sharedWithUser` effects still refetch in full on every `refreshTick`. The `sync-cursors` + `withUpdatedSince` primitives already generalise; threading a per-relationship cursor (keyed by the friend/owner id) through those effects would cut the largest repeat-pull cost for users following many people.
- **Server-truncate the delta window with a `Range`/`limit` + continue-cursor** — a client offline for weeks could get a huge first delta. Pairing `updated_at=gt.<cursor>&order=updated_at.asc&limit=N` with a loop that advances the cursor to the last row of each page (true keyset pagination, ties broken by id) would bound each request and dovetails with BE-28's cursor-pagination mandate.
- **Adopt `updated_at`-based LWW in the merge helpers (pre-stage BE-15)** — `mergeCollectionsFromCloud`/`mergeItemsFromCloud` currently let the cloud row unconditionally win on id conflict, which a delta pull now makes more visible: a local edit newer than the cloud copy gets clobbered on the next tick. Carrying `updatedAt` onto the domain types (or comparing the raw row) so the merge keeps whichever side is newer would make delta pulls safe against concurrent local writes and is exactly the LWW policy BE-15 calls for.
- **Reset the per-entity cursor when a tombstone/visibility change can retract rows** — delta pulls only ever ADD/UPDATE; a row that becomes invisible (unshared, made private, deleted server-side) won't appear in a `updated_at=gt` delta to be removed locally. A lightweight "full reconcile every Nth tick" (cursor=null) or a tombstone feed (BE-15) is needed so retractions eventually propagate; document the gap until then so it isn't mistaken for a sync bug.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-19, after BE-15a conflict-policy foundation)
- **Carry `deletedAt` onto the domain types so the merge helpers honour tombstones natively** — `lib/tombstones.ts` partitions raw cloud rows, but `Collection`/`CollectableItem` have no `deletedAt` field, so a tombstone can only be applied as a post-pull cache filter (BE-15b). Threading `deletedAt?: string | null` through the row coercers + domain types would let `mergeCollectionsFromCloud`/`mergeItemsFromCloud` drop a tombstoned row inline (and keep LWW newest-wins) instead of a second filtering pass.
- **Generalise the social graph's `deletedProfileIds` to consume `lib/tombstones.ts`** — `social-context` still hand-rolls its own deleted-id set in `SocialGraphStore`; now that the reusable helper exists, migrating profiles/friend_requests onto `partitionByTombstone` + `getTombstones`/`setTombstones` (keyed by `tombstoneKey("profiles", …)`) would collapse the bespoke set into the shared primitive and let admin profile-deletes propagate via `deleted_at` instead of a local-only list.
- **A durable offline-delete queue keyed on the soft-delete PATCH** — once deletes become `deleted_at=now()` upserts (BE-15b), they can ride the existing `pending-upserts` engine so an offline delete retries on reconnect like any other write, closing the "fire-and-forget delete is lost offline" gap the BE-13c suggestions flagged.
- **`tombstoneKey` for profiles/friend_requests in `clearAllUserData`** — BE-15a only clears the collections/items tombstone keys on sign-out; when the social graph adopts the helper, add `tombstoneKey("profiles", …)`/`tombstoneKey("friend_requests", …)` to the reset list so a re-login starts from a clean tombstone slate.
- **Wire BE-27's retention sweep to the `<table>_alive_idx` inverse** — the partial `WHERE deleted_at IS NULL` indexes make the "alive" read paths cheap but leave the hard-purge scan (`deleted_at < now() - interval`) unindexed. A second partial index `WHERE deleted_at IS NOT NULL` (or a plain `deleted_at` index) would let the `pg_cron` purge find expired tombstones without a seq scan as they accumulate.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-19, after BE-15b tombstone delta-sync wiring)
- **Filter tombstones on the viewer-facing reads** — BE-15b drops soft-deleted rows from the OWNED full-pulls (`fetchCollectionsByUserId`/`fetchItemsByCollectionId`/`fetchWishlistItemsByUserId`) and the owned delta, but `fetchPublicCollectionsByUserId`/`fetchCollectionsSharedWithUser`/`fetchCollectionById`/`fetchItemById` still map every row, so a viewer following a public collection can still see an item the owner just soft-deleted until their own delta retracts it. Add the same `.filter((r) => !r.deleted_at)` (or a `deleted_at=is.null` URL filter) to those reads for symmetric tombstone behaviour.
- **Server-side `deleted_at=is.null` on the alive read URLs** — the client-side `.filter((r) => !r.deleted_at)` still ships tombstoned rows over the wire and parses them. Appending `&deleted_at=is.null` to the full-pull PostgREST URLs (using the new `<table>_alive_idx` partial index) would cut payload + parse cost and lean on the DB index instead of a JS pass, while the delta URL stays unfiltered for propagation.
- **Route owned soft-deletes through the pending-upsert engine** — `softDeleteRemoteCollection`/`softDeleteRemoteItem` are still fire-and-forget `.catch(() => undefined)`, so an offline delete's cloud PATCH is lost (only the local tombstone survives, via `recordTombstones`). Modelling the soft-delete as a PATCH delivery in the BE-13c pending queue (or a sibling tombstone queue) would retry it on reconnect so the cloud and local tombstone sets can't diverge.
- **A `pg_cron` purge that consumes the accumulated tombstone set** — local tombstone id sets (`collectables-tombstones-v1-{entity}-{userId}`) grow unbounded as deletes accumulate, and the cloud keeps soft-deleted rows forever. BE-27's retention sweep should hard-DELETE rows whose `deleted_at` is older than the window AND let the client prune its local set once a row no longer comes back in any pull, so neither side leaks storage.
- **Cascade-soft-delete on the server instead of per-child client PATCHes** — `deleteCollection` now issues one PATCH per child item because no FK cascade fires on a soft delete; a collection with hundreds of items means hundreds of requests on delete. A `soft_delete_collection(collection_id)` Edge Function / SQL function that stamps `deleted_at` on the collection and its items in one statement would make the delete atomic and O(1) round-trips.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-20, after BE-17 one-time local→cloud import)
- **Re-key the import flag on `signOut`/account-switch instead of trusting the in-session ref** — `cloudImportRunRef` guards a single run per user within a session, but the durable `collectables-cloud-imported-v1-{userId}` flag is what prevents re-import across reloads. If a user signs in, the import partially succeeds (some collections upserted) then the process is killed before `markCloudImported`, the flag stays unset and the *whole* set re-uploads next load. That's idempotent (upsert by id) but wasteful; a per-entity "imported ids" set (or reusing the BE-13c pending queue for the import) would make a resumed import skip already-delivered rows.
- **Fold the import into the pending-upsert queue rather than a bespoke loop** — the BE-17 effect calls `upsertCollection`/`upsertItem` directly and only marks the flag on full success; routing the owned snapshot through `enqueueUpsert` + the existing flush effect would give the import the same retry/ordering/idempotency machinery for free and remove the duplicated try/catch loop, at the cost of a one-time "seed the queue" step gated by the flag.
- **Import owned marketplace listings + chat history too** — BE-17 only backfills collections + items; a user with local-only marketplace listings or chat messages created before cloud sync still has them stranded on-device. Generalising `selectOwnedForImport` into a per-entity registry (collections/items/listings) driven off the same flag would make the one-time import cover every locally-authored entity.
- **Surface the import in the BE-16 syncing pill** — the one-time import can upload many rows on a slow link with no UI signal. Counting the in-flight import writes into `pendingSyncCount` (or a dedicated "importing N…" state) would reuse the existing pill so the user knows their local library is being uploaded rather than seeing a silent delay.
- **Server-side import-once guard keyed on `auth.uid()`** — the flag is device-local, so the same user on a second device re-runs the import (harmless via upsert, but redundant egress). A `profiles.cloud_imported_at timestamptz` column set by the first successful import (or checked before it) would make the one-time import truly once-per-account, and doubles as a migration-progress signal for support.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-20, after BE-20 claim-listing Edge Function)
- **Drop the `marketplace_listings_update_buyer_claim` RLS policy now that claims are server-authoritative** — buyer claims route through the `claim-listing` Edge Function (service-role, atomic), so the permissive client-side buyer-claim UPDATE policy is now redundant *and* a bypass: a hand-crafted PATCH can still flip `sold_at`/`buyer_user_id` non-atomically. A migration removing that policy (keeping `update_own` for sellers) would make the Edge Function the only buyer-claim path and close the race the function was built to fix.
- **Return the claimed listing into local state instead of trusting the optimistic stamp** — `markListingSold` optimistically sets `soldAt` to client time and fires `cloudClaimListing` fire-and-forget; if the server rejects (double-claim/own-listing) the local row is wrongly shown as sold until a realtime UPDATE corrects it. Awaiting the function's `{ success, listing }` and reverting the optimistic update on `false` (with a "no longer available" toast) would make the UI truthful on a lost race.
- **Move the seller "mark sold" + item transfer into the same Edge Function** — the buyer claim now also drives `transferItemToBuyer` (a separate client write) and an in-app chat message; folding the transfer/notification into `claim-listing` (or a follow-up `accept-claim`) would make the whole buy cycle atomic so a crash between the claim and the transfer can't leave a sold listing with no copied item.
- **Rate-limit `claim-listing` per caller (BE-29 reuse)** — the function does two DB round-trips per call with no throttle; wiring `createSlidingWindowLimiter` (keyed on `auth.uid()`) at the top would stop a buyer from hammering claims across many listings and pairs naturally with the BE-29 app-level write rate-limiting work.
- **Emit an analytics event from the function on claim outcome** — the client only `trackEvent("listing_claimed")` on its optimistic success, so server-rejected double-claims are invisible to analytics. Having `claim-listing` mirror a `listing_claim_rejected` event (reason: sold/own/not-found) via the analytics-mirror path would surface contention hotspots and would not depend on a client that already moved on.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-21, after BE-22a server-authoritative subscriptions foundation)
- **Back the `subscriptions` table with a real billing webhook, not a self-serve `activate`** — BE-22b's `validate-premium` function will accept an `action: "activate"` from the client, which still lets any authed caller mint their own `status='active'` row server-side (just behind an Edge Function instead of in AsyncStorage). The durable fix is a Stripe/RevenueCat webhook (service-role) as the ONLY writer of `status='active'`/`current_period_end`; `validate-premium` then becomes read-and-lazily-expire only, so entitlement always traces to a real payment.
- **Add a `subscriptions` realtime UPDATE subscription so a lapse/cancel reflects without a reload** — once BE-22c reads the row, an expiry or admin cancel only reaches the client on the next `validate-premium` call. Subscribing to UPDATE/DELETE on the user's own `subscriptions` row (BE-19 path) and re-projecting via `rowToPremiumState` would drop paid features the moment the server flips the row.
- **A `pg_cron` sweep that flips lapsed `status='active'` rows to `'expired'`** — BE-22a relies on `validate-premium` to lazily expire a row whose `current_period_end` has passed, so a user who never opens the app keeps a stale `active` row (and the SELECT-own read would report premium until they call the function). A nightly `UPDATE subscriptions SET status='expired' WHERE status='active' AND current_period_end <= now()` (BE-27 retention work) makes the DB self-consistent independent of client traffic.
- **Server-gate the actual premium features, not just the flag** — moving the entitlement to `subscriptions` is only half of "gate paid features server-side"; the paid actions themselves (e.g. creating a private collection, exceeding the listing cap) are still enforced only in client code + RLS that doesn't consult `subscriptions`. Adding an `is_premium(uid)` SECURITY-DEFINER helper and referencing it in the relevant RLS policies (private-collection insert, listing-cap) would make the gate real even for a crafted client.
- **Index `current_period_end` for the expiry sweep** — the partial `subscriptions_alive_idx` covers the alive lookup, but the BE-27 expiry sweep above filters on `status='active' AND current_period_end <= now()`. A partial index `ON subscriptions (current_period_end) WHERE status='active'` would keep that recurring sweep from scanning the whole table as the subscriber base grows.

## Suggestions (added 2026-06-21, after BE-25 delete-account cascade coverage)
- **Define `reactions` and `collection_follows` as real migrations** — `delete-account` deletes from `reactions` and `collection_follows`, but neither table exists in `supabase/migrations/*` (they were presumably hand-created in the dashboard). The function ignores the delete error so it doesn't crash, but the cascade story is unverifiable for them: the BE-25 drift guard can't see them, and a from-empty `supabase db start` has no such tables. Adding their `CREATE TABLE` (with `user_id ... ON DELETE CASCADE`) migrations would bring them under the same FK/cascade test umbrella as every other table.
- **Have `delete-account` check each pre-delete `.error`** — the six manual `adminClient.from(...).delete()` calls discard their result, so a silent failure (RLS misconfig, missing table, transient 5xx) leaves orphaned rows and the function still returns `{ success: true }`. Aggregating the errors (and 500-ing if any owned-table delete failed before the terminal `deleteUser`) would make a partial wipe observable instead of silently incomplete.
- **Drop the now-redundant manual pre-deletes once the FK cascade is proven** — every table `delete-account` manually clears (`reactions`, `items`, `collection_follows`, `collections`, `friend_requests`, `profiles`) is ALSO ON DELETE CASCADE from `auth.users`, so the terminal `auth.admin.deleteUser` already removes them. With BE-25's cascade test green, the manual pre-deletes are belt-and-braces that can mask a broken FK; keeping just the `deleteUser` call (or asserting the cascade in an integration test before removing them) simplifies the function and makes the FK the single source of truth.
- **Promote the pgTAP `02_fk_cascade.sql` into a GDPR-erasure assertion suite** — BE-26 (GDPR export) and the right-to-erasure are the same data map. A shared fixture that seeds one account across every owned/audit table, then asserts both "export returns all of it" and "delete leaves nothing but SET-NULL audit rows" would keep export and erasure coverage from drifting apart as tables are added.
- **Emit a `account_deleted` analytics event from `delete-account` before the wipe** — the function currently leaves no trace once `deleteUser` runs (and the user's own analytics rows SET-NULL), so deletion volume/abuse is invisible. Mirroring a single anonymised `account_deleted` event (no user_id) via the analytics-mirror path would give a retention/erasure signal without re-introducing PII.

## BE-26 — GDPR data-export follow-ups
- **Add a "Download my data" button in settings wired to `cloudExportData()`** — the Edge Function + wrapper exist, but no UI calls them. A settings entry that calls `cloudExportData()`, serialises the document, and hands it to `expo-sharing`/a web `Blob` download (with localised strings in all 6 languages) would close the GDPR loop end-to-end for the user instead of leaving the capability backend-only.
- **Stream the export as NDJSON for large accounts** — `export-data` currently buffers every table into one in-memory JSON object before responding. A power user with thousands of items/messages could blow the function's memory ceiling. Switching to a `ReadableStream` that emits one table at a time (or NDJSON rows) keeps memory flat and lets the client show progress.
- **Include marketplace listings + transfers in the export** — the bundle covers profile/collections/items/friends/chat/subscriptions, but `marketplace_listings` (as seller) and `marketplace_transfers` (as buyer/seller) are also user data the GDPR export should carry. Add them to `DATA_EXPORT_TABLES`, the function reads, and `buildDataExport`.
- **Add a pgTAP integration test that actually invokes `export-data` against seeded rows** — today coverage is structural (source-regex) + pure-helper unit tests. A Docker supabase-test that seeds one account across every table and asserts the function returns exactly those rows (and none of another user's) would catch a filter regression (e.g. a dropped `.eq(user_id)`) that the regex tests can't.
- **Rate-limit `export-data` per user** — a full-account export is expensive (6 table scans under service-role). Reusing `createSlidingWindowLimiter` (BE-29) keyed on `auth.uid()` to cap exports to e.g. 1/hour would stop a client from hammering the function into a cost/DoS problem.

## BE-24 storage-decision follow-ups (2026-06-22)
- **Ship the `sign-upload` Edge Function** — the BE-24 decision (`docs/storage-decision.md`) is to keep Cloudinary but kill the unsigned `upload_preset` in `lib/cloudinary.ts`. Add a `sign-upload` function that verifies the caller's Supabase session and returns a short-lived `timestamp`+`signature` computed from `CLOUDINARY_API_SECRET` (function-secret only, never `EXPO_PUBLIC_*`), mirroring the existing `delete-image` signature code. Then switch `uploadImage` to POST the signed params instead of the preset, and record "disable the unsigned preset in the Cloudinary dashboard" in `MANUAL-TASKS.md`.
- **Wire orphan cleanup into hard deletes** — `deleteItem`/`deleteItems`/`deleteCollection` in `lib/collections-context.tsx` soft-delete rows but never call `deleteCloudinaryImages`, leaking assets per the BE-24 orphan story. On a genuine hard purge (post-tombstone-window), collect the rows' image URLs and best-effort `deleteCloudinaryImages` them so deleting an item eventually deletes its asset.
- **Add the `pg_cron` asset reconciliation sweep (ties into BE-27)** — the durable backstop named in `docs/storage-decision.md`: a periodic job that lists Cloudinary public IDs with no referencing `items`/`collections`/`profiles` row and destroys them, catching offline-at-delete and function-error stragglers the inline cleanup misses.
- **Test that soft delete preserves assets but hard purge drops them** — add a unit test around the future cleanup helper asserting a tombstoned (soft-deleted) row keeps its Cloudinary asset through the grace window, and only a hard purge calls `deleteCloudinaryImages`, encoding the `docs/CONFLICT-POLICY.md`-aligned grace-window rule so a refactor can't silently start purging undeletable rows' photos.
- **Add a structural test that `uploadImage` carries no unsigned `upload_preset` once signed upload lands** — a regex guard in `__tests__/` that fails if `lib/cloudinary.ts` still appends `upload_preset`, so the abuse surface the BE-24 decision closes can't silently regress in a future merge.

## BE-27 retention-sweep follow-ups (2026-06-23)
- **Add a pgTAP/Docker test that actually exercises `run_retention_sweeps()`** — current coverage is structural regex over the migration. A supabase-test that seeds boundary rows (analytics at 12mo/14mo, anon at 29d/31d, tombstones at 89d/91d), runs `SELECT public.run_retention_sweeps()`, and asserts exactly the over-window rows are gone would catch an off-by-one interval or a swapped predicate the regex test can't.
- **Make the retention windows configurable via GUC/`app.settings` instead of hard-coded intervals** — the 13mo/30d/90d literals live only inside the function body, so changing a window needs a new migration. Reading them from `current_setting('app.retention_analytics_months', true)` with sane defaults would let an operator tune retention (incident response, legal hold) without a redeploy, and ties into the BE-30 kill-switch idea.
- **Emit a per-sweep summary row into an `ops_log` table** — `run_retention_sweeps()` returns void and leaves no audit trail, so there's no way to confirm the cron ran or how many rows each window reclaimed. Capturing `GET DIAGNOSTICS row_count` per DELETE into a small ops table (or `RAISE LOG`) would make the sweep observable in Supabase logs / Power BI.
- **Reconcile the analytics 13-month window with PostHog's own retention** — the privacy paragraph now promises a 13-month server window, but PostHog's free-tier retention and the `analytics-mirror` ingestion cadence aren't documented together. A short note in the analytics docs mapping "PostHog raw → 13mo Supabase mirror → Power BI" would keep the disclosure honest as either side's retention changes.
- **Extend the sweep to `chat_messages`/`chat_reads` once a chat-retention policy is decided** — BE-27 prunes analytics + tombstones but chat history grows unbounded. A documented chat-retention window (e.g. messages older than N months in closed conversations) added to the same daily job would close the last unbounded-growth table, with the window mirrored into the privacy policy alongside the others.

## BE-28a pagination-bound follow-ups (2026-06-23)
- **Wire the BE-28b keyset paging loops** — `withPageLimit` now caps every newest-first list endpoint, but a collection/marketplace feed with more than `LIST_PAGE_SIZE` (200) rows is silently truncated. Add a `created_at`/`id` keyset cursor (`created_at=lt.<last>`) loop in the fetch wrappers that pages until a short page is returned, so large datasets stay complete without an unbounded scan.
- **Bound chat history with a newest-window query (deferred from 28a)** — `fetchMessagesUrl` orders `created_at.asc` with no limit, so a long conversation does a full scan. Flip it to fetch the newest `LIST_PAGE_SIZE` (`order=created_at.desc&limit=N`, reversed client-side) plus an "older messages" pager, the one list endpoint 28a intentionally skipped.
- **Surface `Prefer: count=exact` + a "load more" affordance** — once paging exists, reading the `content-range` total (already parsed for `profilesPageUrl`) lets the collection/marketplace screens show "showing 200 of N" and a load-more button instead of a silent cap, matching the existing people-browser pattern.
- **Add a lint guard that every `/rest/v1/...&order=` list URL carries a `limit=`** — a `scripts/`-style structural check (like `check-inline-hex`) that greps the `lib/*-shapes.ts` + `supabase-*.ts` builders and fails CI on an unbounded ordered list URL, so a future endpoint can't silently reintroduce a full-table scan.
- **Make `LIST_PAGE_SIZE` an `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` env (ties into BE-30)** — exposing the page cap as a runtime env lets ops shrink it during an incident (smaller payloads, less DB load) without a redeploy, reusing the BE-30 kill-switch/cache-TTL env plumbing.

## BE-28b keyset-pagination follow-ups (2026-06-23)
- **Add an "older messages" pager to chat (the deferred other half of 28b)** — `fetchMessagesForChat` now loads only the newest `LIST_PAGE_SIZE` window. A `fetchMessagesUrl` variant that takes a `before` cursor (`created_at=lt.<oldest-loaded>&order=created_at.desc&limit=N`) plus a "load earlier" affordance in the chat screen would let users scroll back through history without ever loading it all at once.
- **Composite `(created_at,id)` keyset for exact-tie correctness** — `collectKeysetPages` uses an inclusive `created_at=lte` + id-dedupe, which drops rows only in the (practically impossible) case of >`LIST_PAGE_SIZE` rows sharing one millisecond. A PostgREST `or=(created_at.lt.X,and(created_at.eq.X,id.lt.Y))` filter on a `(created_at,id)` ordering would remove that edge entirely and let the loop drop the dedupe Set.
- **Surface a "more pages were capped" signal** — `collectKeysetPages` silently stops at `MAX_KEYSET_PAGES` (50 × 200 = 10k rows). Returning a `{rows, truncated}` shape (or a `captureException` breadcrumb) when the ceiling is hit would make an unexpectedly huge dataset observable instead of quietly clipped.
- **Reuse `collectKeysetPages` for `fetchAllUserImageUrls` + `deleteAllUserData`** — the account-deletion image-gather and bulk deletes still issue single unbounded `select`/`DELETE` calls; routing the reads through the keyset loop (and chunking the deletes) would keep account deletion correct for a power user with thousands of items.
- **Parallelize the first keyset page with the cache hydrate** — the loops currently run fully before the UI updates. Emitting the first page immediately (then appending later pages) via a streaming callback would keep large-collection screens responsive instead of blocking on the full multi-page fetch.

## BE-28c explicit-projection follow-ups (2026-06-23)
- **Add a lint guard banning `select=*` in the REST builders** — a `scripts/`-style structural check (mirroring `check-inline-hex`) that greps every `lib/*-shapes.ts` + `supabase-*.ts` read URL and fails CI on a `select=*`, so a future endpoint can't silently reintroduce an unbounded projection that drifts from its coercer.
- **Generate the column constants from the coercers (single source of truth)** — `PROFILE_COLUMNS`/`COLLECTION_COLUMNS`/`ITEM_COLUMNS` are hand-maintained snake_case lists that must stay in lockstep with `coerce*Row`. A small typed map (camel↔snake) the coercers and the constants both derive from would make a new field impossible to add to one without the other.
- **Drop `created_at`/`updated_at`/`deleted_at` from the single-row by-id projections** — `collectionByIdUrl`/`itemByIdUrl` feed `fetchCollectionById`/`fetchItemById`, which never read the sync-metadata columns; trimming them to the pure coercer set (a `*_DETAIL_COLUMNS` variant) shaves a few bytes per detail-screen open.
- **Project only the columns each narrow read needs** — `fetchAllUserImageUrls` already uses `select=cover_photo`/`select=photos`/`select=avatar`; audit the remaining inline reads for over-fetching (e.g. the realtime row coercers) and split a "list" vs "detail" projection where the list screen only renders a subset.
- **Extend the parity test to assert the projection is a *subset* of the table** — the BE-3 test now checks each selected column exists; a complementary check that the coercer reads no column absent from the projection (so a future coercer field without a matching `*_COLUMNS` entry fails) would close the reverse drift direction, dovetailing with BE-37.

## BE-29 write-rate-limit follow-ups (2026-06-24)
- **Surface a "writes throttled" toast/breadcrumb when `appWriteLimiter` denies** — a throttled mutation now silently re-queues, so a user hitting the cap sees a stuck "syncing…" pill with no explanation. Emitting a one-shot toast (and a `captureException` breadcrumb) on the first denial per window would make the rare throttle observable instead of looking like a hang.
- **Schedule a flush retry when a window is full** — `createRateLimitedDeliver` returns `false` and the entity waits for the *next* organic flush (reconnect/refresh), which may be far off if the user goes idle. Arming a short timer (e.g. `windowMs/maxEvents`) to re-trigger the flush after a throttle would drain the backlog promptly without a manual refresh.
- **Make the cap an `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` env (ties into BE-30)** — `MAX_WRITES_PER_WINDOW`/`WRITE_RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MS` are compile-time constants; exposing them as runtime envs lets ops tighten the write budget during a Supabase incident (or loosen it for a bulk-import build) without a redeploy, reusing the BE-30 kill-switch plumbing.
- **Per-path sub-budgets under the shared window** — one app-wide budget means a chat-send storm can starve collection upserts (and vice-versa). Optional per-path limiters (chat/collections/social) layered under the shared global would isolate a runaway on one path from blocking another's legitimate writes.
- **Count only *successful* deliveries against the window** — the wrapper consumes a token before `deliver`, so a path that's failing on the network burns budget on attempts that never reach Supabase. Moving the `allow()` to fire only on a `true` return (or refunding on `false`) would make the cap track real quota usage rather than attempt count.

## BE-30 incident-response env follow-ups (2026-06-24)
- **Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_AI_VISION_DISABLED` kill-switch** — `lib/ai-vision.ts` calls a paid Gemini endpoint on every scan. A truthy-literal kill-switch (mirroring `isAnalyticsDisabledByEnv`) that short-circuits `analyzeImage` to a null/empty result would let ops stop AI spend instantly during a cost spike or upstream outage, with no code change.
- **Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_DISABLED` kill-switch independent of the DSN** — today the only way to silence Sentry is to blank `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_DSN`, which loses the configured value. A dedicated disable flag (force `captureException` to a no-op while keeping the DSN secret intact) would let ops mute a noisy error storm without destroying config.
- **Extract a single pure `isEnvFlagEnabled` truthy parser** — `isRealtimeDisabledByEnv` and the new `isAnalyticsDisabledByEnv` now both hand-roll the `1`/`true`/`yes` whitelist. A shared pure helper in a react-native-free module (so both the realtime and analytics-config purity tests can import it) would collapse the duplication and guarantee every future kill-switch parses identically.
- **Document the build-time inlining caveat next to each kill-switch** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` values are baked into the bundle at build time, so "without redeploy" really means "re-run the deploy action with a flipped secret, no PR". A one-line note in `README-DEPLOY.md`'s incident-response rows would stop an operator from expecting a live runtime toggle that doesn't exist for static-hosted web.
- **Add a CI structural test enumerating every incident-response env knob** — a single test that asserts each kill-switch/TTL env (`REALTIME_DISABLED`, `ANALYTICS_DISABLED`, `PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS`, …) is documented in both `.env.example` and `README-DEPLOY.md` and wired via a literal `process.env.X` access would keep the family in lockstep and catch a future knob that ships code but no docs (or vice-versa).

- **BE-34 follow-up: wire `findVersionCollisions` into `lint:migration-docs` (or a new `lint:migrations`)** — the new `lib/migration-apply-order.ts` collision guard only runs under `npm test`. Calling it from a CI lint script (alongside `check-migration-docs`) would fail a `git push`/PR *before* the slower full test run when someone adds a colliding-timestamp migration, mirroring how `check-inline-hex`/`check-migration-docs` gate fast.

- **Fold `migration-versions-unique.test.ts` onto the shared helper** — that older test re-implements version-prefix parsing and dup detection inline. Re-pointing it at `parseMigrations`/`findVersionCollisions` removes the duplicated regex/grouping logic so the two suites can't drift on what counts as a "version".

- **Lexicographic-vs-numeric apply-order divergence warning** — `20260527142510_…` sorts *before* `20260527_…` by filename but *after* by numeric version; the helper picks numeric (the runner's order). A non-fatal test/log that flags any pair where `ls`-order disagrees with version-order would catch a future mixed-width prefix that a human reviewer reading the directory listing would misread the apply sequence of.

- **CI guard that every migration version is monotonic vs. the last committed one** — beyond uniqueness, a check that each *new* migration's version is greater than the current max on `main` would stop a back-dated timestamp (e.g. a hotfix authored with an older clock) from inserting itself mid-history and applying out of intended dependency order on a fresh `db reset`.

- **Generate the MANUAL-TASKS apply-order section from `computeApplyOrder`** — MANUAL-TASKS.md and README-DEPLOY list a hand-maintained apply order. A small script that emits the canonical ordered list from `computeApplyOrder(readdir(...))` (checked in CI to match the docs) would keep the documented order in lockstep with what the runner actually does as migrations are added.

## BE-35 cloud-wrapper integration-test follow-ups (2026-06-25)
- **Promote the `require.cache` native-peer stubbing into a shared test util** — `__tests__/cloud-wrapper-harness.ts` proves the real wrappers CAN be loaded under `node --test` by seeding `react-native`/auth-js/realtime-js/async-storage stubs. Extracting a generic `loadWithNativeStubs(specifier)` would let the many other structural `*-wiring.test.ts` files (realtime, profiles, sentry) upgrade from source-text assertions to true behavioural tests, retiring the brittle regex pins.
- **Cover the remaining `supabase-profiles.ts` mutation wrappers** — BE-35 exercised marketplace + chat; the profiles module's `upsertCollection`/`upsertItem`/`sendFriendRequest`/`cloudAcceptFriendRequest`/`addReaction` still use the module-private `supabaseRest` (no injectable `fetcher`/`tokenProvider` seam). Refactoring `supabaseRest` to accept an optional `{ fetcher, tokenProvider }` (defaulting to today's behaviour) would let the same harness assert their request shape + the POST `Prefer: resolution=merge-duplicates` idempotency header.
- **Assert the `Content-Type`/preflight-minimisation contract in the integration tests** — `supabaseRest` deliberately omits `Content-Type` on body-less GETs and `Prefer` on non-POSTs to shrink the iOS-Safari CORS preflight surface. A test that asserts the recorded GET headers carry NO `Content-Type`/`Prefer` would lock in that regression-prone optimisation behaviourally, not just by code comment.
- **Add an end-to-end requeue test that chains a wrapper into `flushPendingQueue`** — BE-35 verifies each wrapper returns the right false/null sentinel; a follow-up that feeds a failing `cloudAddListing` through `lib/pending-upserts.ts`'s `flushPendingQueue` and asserts the entity stays in the queue (then re-delivers on the next ok response) would close the loop on the actual "error→requeue" behaviour end-to-end.
- **Stub-drift guard for the seeded native peers** — the harness stubs `Platform`, `AuthClient.getSession`, and the realtime enum constants by hand; if `@/lib/supabase` starts touching another react-native API at module-eval time the stub silently under-specifies and the suite breaks opaquely. A tiny test that imports the stub shapes and asserts they expose exactly the members the wrappers read at load time would turn that into a clear failure.

## BE-37 schema-parity follow-ups (2026-06-25)
- **Persist marketplace `arrived_at` through the cloud** — `markListingReceived` only mutates local state; now that `arrived_at` exists in the schema (20260628) and the read projection, add a `cloudMarkArrived(id, arrivedAt)` PATCH wrapper + an RLS UPDATE policy scoped to `auth.uid() = buyer_user_id` so "received" survives reinstall/cross-device like `sold_at` does.
- **Extend the parity guard to row-coercers, not just builders** — the test derives columns from URL/body builders; a dropped field read only inside `coerceItemRow`/`rowToListing`/`chatRowToMessage` (without a matching `select=` column) would slip through. Cross-check each `*_COLUMNS` projection against the keys its coercer reads so a coercer and its projection can never drift apart.
- **Reverse parity: flag schema columns no builder ever touches** — today the guard is one-directional (builder ⇒ column). A complementary check that lists table columns absent from every builder/projection would surface dead columns and forgotten features (e.g. a column added by migration but never wired into a read), catching the inverse drift.
- **Generalise the parity test to auto-discover `*-shapes.ts` modules** — the builder list is hand-maintained per module; a fourth shapes file would be silently uncovered. A glob over `lib/*-shapes.ts` + a structural assertion that every exported `*Url`/`*Body`/`*Payload` builder is referenced by the parity test would make new shape modules fail-closed instead of fail-open.
- **CI check that every `select=` column is FK/index-backed for hot filters** — extend the migration-aware tooling so a column used in a URL `=eq.`/`order=` filter is asserted to have a leading-column index (reusing the FK-index-coverage audit), catching seq-scan-on-read regressions at lint time rather than in production latency.

## SEC-7 OAuth callback token-hygiene follow-ups (2026-06-26)
- **Scrub the address bar on the error path too, not just before navigation** — `scrubAuthParamsFromLocation` runs once at the top of `finishAuth`, but if `setSession`/`exchangeCodeForSession` throws the screen stays on `/auth/callback` showing the retry button while the (now-consumed) tokens are already gone from the URL — good. But a *malformed* link that hits the `authCallbackBadLink` branch never had tokens to scrub; verify no flow leaves a partially-valid token in the bar after a thrown error, and add a regression test that the URL is clean in the error/`setError` branch as well.
- **Centralise the sensitive-param list with the auth client's own URL parser** — `SENSITIVE_HASH_PARAMS`/`SENSITIVE_QUERY_PARAMS` are hand-maintained; if Supabase adds a new token field (e.g. a future `id_token`) the scrub silently misses it. Deriving the strip-list from the same constants the callback reads (`access_token`/`refresh_token`/`code`/`token_hash`/…) — or a single shared `AUTH_URL_PARAMS` map consumed by both the reader and the scrubber — would keep them from drifting apart.
- **Set `referrerpolicy=no-referrer` / a Referrer-Policy meta on the web build** — the scrub closes the in-tab leak, but a hardened `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` (or `strict-origin`) header/meta on the GitHub Pages build is defence-in-depth against any token surviving one tick into an outbound request before `replaceState` runs. Pairs naturally with the pending SEC-15 CSP/security-headers task.
- **Belt-and-suspenders: clear `window.name` and any bfcache copy** — some OAuth providers and SPA shims stash redirect state in `window.name`; a follow-up that also blanks `window.name` on the callback and adds a `pageshow`/`Cache-Control: no-store` guard would stop a back-forward-cache restore from resurrecting the pre-scrub URL on the back button.
- **Behavioural (not just structural) ordering test via a fake auth client** — the current test asserts scrub-before-`router.replace` by source-index. A stronger test would render/drive `finishAuth` with a stubbed `authClient` + a recording `window`, asserting `history.replaceState` is observed *before* the first `await client.setSession` resolves — locking the ordering behaviourally so a refactor that moves the scrub after the async session set fails loudly.

## SEC-9 shared-`assertCaller` follow-ups (2026-06-26)
- **Behavioural integration test of the real Edge Functions, not just the gate** — `assert-caller.test.ts` executes the helper and source-asserts adoption, but the six functions themselves still only get structural coverage (they import `esm.sh` + `Deno.*`). Reuse the BE-35 `cloud-wrapper-harness` trick (seed `require.cache` with native-peer stubs + a stub `Deno.serve`/`Deno.env`) to actually invoke each function's handler and assert a 401 is returned *before* any `adminClient` query fires — turning "401 before work" from an inferred invariant into an executed one.
- **Order-lint: assert `assertCaller` precedes the first service-role read in every function** — today the ordering ("verify before any service-role op") is enforced per-file by hand-written index assertions. A single structural test that, for each adopter, asserts `src.indexOf("assertCaller") < src.indexOf("SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY")` (and `< createClient(..., serviceRoleKey)`) would fail-closed if a future edit moves a privileged read above the gate.
- **Fold the BE-23 key self-check into the gate** — every function repeats the `assertServiceRoleKey` try/catch → 500 "function misconfigured" block right after `assertCaller`. A companion `assertServiceRoleConfig(key, name, corsHeaders)` (same `{ok}|{response}` shape) would collapse that second copy-pasted block the way SEC-9 collapsed the auth one, leaving each function with two one-line gates instead of ~20 lines of boilerplate.
- **Method/`OPTIONS`/CORS preflight also lives in `_shared`** — five of the functions hand-roll identical `corsHeaders`, an `OPTIONS` short-circuit, a `json()` helper, and a `405` non-POST guard. Centralising those in `_shared/http.ts` (consumed alongside `assertCaller`) would make the CORS-tightening SEC-10 task a one-file change instead of six, and remove the last copy-pasted security-relevant surface from the function bodies.
- **Optional caller-allowlist / role check in `assertCaller`** — the gate proves *a* valid session; some functions (e.g. an admin-only op) need *a specific* caller. Extend `assertCaller` with an optional predicate `(user) => boolean` returning 403 on failure, so authorization (not just authentication) has one tested home and admin-gated functions can't forget the check.

## SEC-10 Edge Function CORS follow-ups (2026-06-26)
- **Finish the `_shared/http.ts` consolidation the SEC-9 suggestion called for** — SEC-10 centralised CORS but each function still hand-rolls the `OPTIONS` short-circuit, the per-request `json()`/`jsonResponse` closure, and the `405` non-POST guard. A `withCors(req, handler, opts)` wrapper (or `serveJson`) in `_shared/http.ts` that evaluates CORS, answers preflight, rejects non-POST, and injects a `json` helper would collapse ~15 lines of boilerplate per function into one call and leave zero copy-pasted HTTP surface.
- **Behavioural test that a disallowed origin gets a 403 from the real handler** — `cors-shared.test.ts` proves `evaluateCors` rejects and source-asserts each function early-returns `forbiddenOriginResponse`, but no test drives an actual function with a hostile `Origin` to confirm the 403 fires *before* `auth.getUser()`/any service-role read. Reuse the `cloud-wrapper-harness` `Deno.serve`/`Deno.env` stub trick to invoke each handler with `Origin: https://evil.example` and assert a 403 with no `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` and no downstream query.
- **Reflect the deep-link only for the deep-link, and consider credentials mode** — `collectables://` in `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` is harmless for native (which ignores CORS) but is an unusual value to echo to a browser. Audit whether any browser flow actually needs it; if the functions ever move to cookie auth, add `Access-Control-Allow-Credentials: true` (which is incompatible with the `*`-style fallback) and tighten the no-Origin fallback so credentialed requests can't be replayed cross-site.
- **Lint that no Edge Function reintroduces a wildcard or an inline `corsHeaders` object** — the no-`*` guard lives in the per-function structural test list, which a *new* function would silently skip. A `scripts/check-edge-cors.ts` wired into `lint:ci` that globs `supabase/functions/*/index.ts` and fails if any file contains `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` as a literal (i.e. doesn't route through `_shared/cors.ts`) would make new functions fail-closed.
- **Validate/normalise `ALLOWED_ORIGINS` entries and warn on misconfig** — `getAllowedOrigins` trusts the operator secret verbatim; a trailing slash, a path, or `*` pasted in would silently never match (or, with `*`, re-open the hole). Normalise each entry to scheme+host, reject `*`/paths, and `console.warn` once at cold start when an entry is dropped, so a fat-fingered secret surfaces in the function logs instead of as silent 403s.

## SEC-13 PII-in-telemetry guard follow-ups (2026-06-27)
- **Runtime prop-stripping in `trackEvent`, not just a build-time scan** — `__tests__/analytics-pii.test.ts` catches a PII key at CI time, but a dynamically-built props object (`{ [key]: value }`, a spread, or a key from a variable) slips past the static scanner *and* `trackEvent` forwards it verbatim. Add a `sanitiseProps(name, props)` step in `trackEvent` that drops any key not in `ANALYTICS_EVENTS[name].props` and any key `isPiiPropKey(key)` flags (dev-warn on drop), so the deny rule holds even for props the structural test can't see.
- **Value-shape guard, not only key-shape** — the guard rejects PII *keys* but a safe key can still carry a free-text *value* (e.g. `source: userTypedText`). Add a runtime assertion/strip that property values are short scalars (string ≤ N chars from a known enum set, number, boolean, null) and reject/truncate anything that looks like prose or an email/URL, closing the "right key, wrong value" gap.
- **Extend the scan to `identifyUser`/`setSentryUser` traits** — SEC-13 covers `trackEvent`/`addBreadcrumb`/`captureException` but `identifyUser(userId, traits)` and `setSentryUser({id,email})` also reach the processors. Email on the Sentry user is an intentional, documented exception; a test should assert *only* `{id,email}` flow there and that `identifyUser` traits are PII-key-free, so a future `identifyUser(id,{displayName})` fails loudly.
- **Wire a `lint:telemetry` script into `lint:ci`** — the PII scan currently rides in the test suite (`npm test`), which is skipped/partial in the expo-absent container. Extract the call-site scan into `scripts/check-telemetry-pii.ts` (pure node, relative imports) and add it to `lint:ci` next to `lint:hex`/`lint:migration-docs`, so the guard runs even when the `@/`-alias test suites can't load.
- **Automate the 90-day `analytics_events` prune instead of documenting it** — the retention window is enforced only by an operator remembering to run the `MANUAL-TASKS.md` delete. Ship a versioned migration that installs the `pg_cron` job (guarded by `cron` extension availability) so the documented 90-day window is actually applied, with a test asserting the doc window and the migration interval stay in lockstep.

## SEC-14 secret-scanning follow-ups (2026-06-27)
- **Pre-commit hook so a credential never reaches a remote** — `lint:secrets` runs in CI and `lint:ci`, but the secret only gets caught *after* it is pushed (and thus already in the public git history, requiring a rotate-and-force-push). Add a `.husky`/`simple-git-hooks` `pre-commit` (or a `scripts/install-git-hooks.ts`) that runs `scanForSecrets` over the *staged* diff only (fast), blocking the commit locally before the secret ever leaves the machine.
- **Entropy/assignment fallback rule for unknown secret shapes** — the rule set is an allow-list of *known* vendor patterns; a novel API key (a 40-char hex DB password, a base64 webhook secret) with no recognisable prefix sails through. Add an optional high-threshold Shannon-entropy rule scoped to obvious assignment contexts (`(secret|token|password|api[_-]?key)\s*[:=]\s*["'][A-Za-z0-9+/]{20,}`), behind the `secret-scan-ignore` escape hatch, to catch the long tail without drowning the report in false positives.
- **Decode-and-classify every JWT in the bundle, not just `service_role`** — `isPrivilegedSupabaseJwt` only flags `role === "service_role"`, but any privileged custom claim (`is_admin`, a `supabase_admin` role, a long-lived service token from another vendor) would ship silently. Generalise the validator to decode the payload and flag any role/claim NOT on a small public allow-list (`anon`, `authenticated`), so the bundle guard fails closed on unfamiliar privileged tokens.
- **Scan the source map separately and surface the original file** — `check-bundle-secrets.ts` greps `*.map`, but a minified single-line `*.js` match reports `column 1` of a 2 MB line, which is useless for triage. Parse the adjacent `.map` to translate a bundle hit back to its `lib/…`/`components/…` origin, so a leaked secret points the operator at the source file to fix rather than at an opaque chunk.
- **CI annotations + a redaction self-test** — pipe `formatSecretReport` through GitHub `::error file=…,line=…::` workflow commands so a hit shows inline on the PR diff, and add a test asserting the report/annotation path can never emit the raw secret (only `redact()` output), so the scanner itself can't become the thing that leaks the credential into a public CI log.

## SEC-15 web CSP / security-headers follow-ups (2026-06-27)
- **Nonce-based `script-src` instead of per-build hashes** — the build hashes each inline script into `script-src`, so any byte change to Expo's bootstrap or our SW-registration silently drops the script from the policy and bricks the SW until the next build re-hashes. Switch to a per-build random nonce (`'nonce-<base64>'`) stamped on each inline `<script nonce=…>` and into the CSP in one pass, so the inline-script allow-listing can never drift out of sync with the document.
- **Report-only rollout via `Content-Security-Policy-Report-Only` + a collector** — ship the strict policy first as report-only (or a second report-only meta) pointing at a lightweight endpoint (a Supabase function or PostHog event) so real violations from prod browsers/extensions surface for a week before the enforcing policy can break a user's session; promote to enforcing once the report stream is clean.
- **CI guard that the CSP allow-list matches the code's real egress** — a new `fetch()` to a host outside `connect-src` (a new vendor SDK, a moved Supabase region) would be silently blocked at runtime with no test failure. Add a test that greps `lib/`/`components/` for literal `https://`/`wss://` hosts and asserts each is covered by a `CSP_CONNECT_SRC` entry (and vice-versa: no dead allow-list entry), so the policy and the code can't diverge.
- **Verify the CSP survives the real `expo export` output, not just a fixture** — the end-to-end test runs the transform over a hand-written shell; the live Expo metro output could carry an inline script shape (e.g. a JSON router manifest or an inline bootstrap) the fixture doesn't model. Add a post-`build` smoke step (gated on `dist/` existing) that loads `dist/index.html`, asserts the CSP meta is present and that every inline `<script>` body has a matching `'sha256-'` token in `script-src`.
- **Subresource Integrity (SRI) on the emitted bundle `<script src>`/`<link>`** — `script-src 'self'` trusts every same-origin asset, but GitHub Pages has no integrity guarantee if the deploy artifact is tampered between build and serve. Have `build-spa-fallback.ts` compute SRI digests for the hashed `_expo/static/**` bundle/CSS references and add `integrity=…`+`crossorigin` attributes, so a mutated chunk is rejected by the browser.

## SEC-22 security-review-wiring follow-ups (2026-06-28)
- **CI-fail the security pass on unresolved findings, not just comment** — the new `claude-security-review.yml` posts a review comment, but a PR can still be merged with open findings. Add a follow-up gate (a required check that re-reads the bot's verdict, or a label like `security-reviewed` the bot sets) so a diff touching `lib/supabase-*`/`functions/`/`auth` cannot merge until the security pass is acknowledged/green — turning the advisory pass into an enforced one.
- **Keep the `paths:` filter and the template's surface list from drifting** — the workflow globs and the PR template's "Security review" bullet list are maintained by hand in two files. Add a test (extend `security-review-wiring.test.ts`) that parses both and asserts the human-readable surfaces in the template map 1:1 onto the workflow `paths:` globs, so adding a new sensitive lib to one without the other fails CI.
- **Add a CODEOWNERS rule for the sensitive surfaces** — back the automatic review with a `.github/CODEOWNERS` requiring a human security reviewer (the maintainer) on the same globs, so even if the Action is skipped/flaky, a person must approve `functions/`/`supabase-*`/`auth`/`cloudinary` diffs before merge.
- **Concurrency + ready-for-review gating to avoid duplicate spend** — a rapid push series re-triggers the review on every `synchronize`; add a `concurrency:` group keyed on the PR number (cancel-in-progress) and consider gating on `pull_request.draft == false` so the (token-costly) security pass runs once per ready revision, not once per intermediate push.
- **Generalise the glob→RegExp matcher into a shared util** — the test inlines a mini glob engine; the same logic is useful for the CSP egress guard and any future path-gated workflow test. Extract it to `lib/glob-match.ts` (pure, node-testable), reuse it here, and unit-test the `**`/`*`/`.`/`/` edge cases directly so every workflow path-filter test shares one verified matcher.

## SEC-8 npm-audit-triage follow-ups (2026-06-28)
- **Promote the audit gate to blocking once the breaking bumps land** — the CI `npm audit --audit-level=high` step is non-blocking because the remaining moderates only fix via a react-native@0.86 / expo@56 major bump. Track a framework-upgrade task that performs those bumps behind a `npm run build` + full-suite verify, then flip `continue-on-error: true` off so a *new* high/critical actually fails the PR instead of merely annotating it.
- **`npm audit --json` parsed into a structured gate (not the human report)** — the bare `npm audit --audit-level=high` exits non-zero on any high but prints an unstructured wall of text. Add `scripts/check-audit.ts` that runs `npm audit --json`, filters to high/critical whose `fixAvailable !== false`, and fails only on *actionable* advisories (so an unfixable transitive high doesn't permanently red the gate), emitting GitHub `::error::` annotations per package.
- **Dependency review + Dependabot for proactive bumps** — `npm audit` is reactive (scans what's already in the lockfile). Add `actions/dependency-review-action` on PRs (blocks a PR that *introduces* a new high/critical dep) and a `.github/dependabot.yml` weekly `npm` schedule grouped by `dev`/`prod`, so patch-level security bumps arrive as auto-PRs that ride the existing CI instead of waiting for a manual `npm audit fix`.
- **Pin the triage to an `allowlist` file so re-triage is diffable** — today the accepted moderates live as prose in SECURITY.md. Add a machine-readable `.audit-allowlist.json` (advisory id + package + expiry date + reason) that `scripts/check-audit.ts` consults, so an accepted advisory auto-expires (forcing a re-review) and a newly-appeared high that isn't on the list fails CI — turning "accepted/unfixable" from a doc claim into an enforced, dated decision.
- **Separate prod-vs-dev audit surfaces** — every remaining advisory is build/test tooling, but `npm audit` lumps them with runtime deps. Add a second `npm audit --omit=dev --audit-level=moderate` step (blocking) that scans only what can ship to the client, so a moderate in a *runtime* dependency (e.g. a future `posthog-js`/`@supabase/*` issue) is caught hard while the dev-tooling noise stays in the non-blocking informational step.

## SEC-5a signed-upload foundation follow-ups (2026-06-28)
- **Ship SEC-5b (the actual upload rewire)** — the foundation is inert until `lib/cloudinary.ts uploadImage` stops using the unsigned `upload_preset`. Wire it to call `cloudSignUpload()`, append the `signedUploadFields(...)` to the FormData (web + native branches), POST to the Cloudinary upload endpoint, and fall back to the preset ONLY when `cloudSignUpload` returns null (Supabase unconfigured / no session). Until then the open write endpoint remains.
- **Per-asset ownership + cleanup ties to the per-user folder** — `sign-upload` scopes every upload under `collectables/users/<uid>`, which finally gives `delete-image` a basis for per-asset ownership (only destroy `public_id`s under the caller's folder) instead of authorizing any session to delete any asset. Track a hardening task that uses the folder prefix to gate destroys and to drive the BE-27 orphan-cleanup sweep per user.
- **Eager-expire / single-use signatures** — Cloudinary signed-upload timestamps are valid for ~1h by default; a leaked `{timestamp,signature,folder}` is replayable in that window. Add an optional `eager`/`public_id` binding or a short `timestamp` skew check, and document the replay window so the client requests a fresh signature per upload batch rather than caching one.
- **Server-side incoming-transformation hardening on the preset/signed path** — even signed uploads should reject non-images and oversized files server-side. Document (and, where Cloudinary allows, sign) an incoming transformation / `allowed_formats=image` / `max_file_size` so a signed request still can't smuggle a non-image; pairs with the console-side preset lockdown noted in MANUAL-TASKS.
- **Integration test the signed round-trip with a fake Cloudinary** — extend the `cloud-wrapper-harness` pattern to drive `cloudSignUpload` against a recording fetcher and assert the request shape (user token, empty body, endpoint) + that `parseSignedUpload` rejects a junk/secret-leaking response; then a SEC-5b test that the signed FormData carries `api_key`/`timestamp`/`signature`/`folder` and never `upload_preset`.

## SEC-5b signed-upload wiring follow-ups (2026-06-28)
- **Surface a per-upload telemetry signal for signed-vs-fallback** — `uploadImage` silently falls back to the unsigned `upload_preset` whenever `cloudSignUpload` returns null. Add a `trackEvent("image_upload", { signed: boolean })` (PII-free, per SEC-13) so operators can see how often the open-preset path is still hit in production — a non-trivial fallback rate means sessions are uploading without a JWT and the preset can't yet be locked down.
