- **Retry the signature once before falling back** — a transient `sign-upload` failure (cold-start, network blip) currently downgrades a fully-authed user to the unsigned path. Wrap the `cloudSignUpload()` call in the existing `fetchWithRetry` one-shot (or call it twice) so a momentary failure doesn't leak an upload to the open preset when the user actually has a session.
- **Lock down / remove the unsigned `upload_preset` once fallback is rare** — with SEC-5b shipped, the only remaining open write surface is the `collectables` unsigned preset. Track the console-side task to set the preset to *signed* (or delete it) after telemetry confirms the fallback path is unused for authed users, closing the C1-High open-write endpoint for good.
- **Thread `cloudSignUpload`'s injectable seam into `uploadImage`** — the wrapper exposes `{fetcher,tokenProvider}` but `uploadImage` calls it arg-less, so the signed branch can't be driven by the `cloud-wrapper-harness` recording fetcher. Add an optional injection param to `uploadImage` (default to the real `fetch`/`cloudSignUpload`) so an integration test can assert the signed FormData carries the 4 fields and hits the signed endpoint without RN.
- **Validate the signed upload response shape** — `postUpload` reads `data.secure_url` unconditionally; a Cloudinary error body that 200s with a different shape would return `undefined`. Coerce the response (`typeof data.secure_url === "string"`) and throw a clear error otherwise, so a malformed signed-upload response surfaces as a real failure instead of persisting an empty image URL.

## Marketplace arrived_at cloud-sync follow-ups (2026-06-29)
- **Re-pull a listing's `arrived_at` on reconnect/foreground so a missed realtime UPDATE self-heals** — `cloudMarkReceived` fires the PATCH and the realtime UPDATE echoes it, but a device that was offline when the buyer confirmed receipt only learns of the stamp on the next full `cloudFetchListings`. Add a targeted `cloudFetchListingById` refresh on app-foreground for any sold listing whose local `arrivedAt == null` so the seller's "delivery confirmed" indicator converges without a manual pull-to-refresh.
- **[DONE 2026-06-29 — MKT-1] Make `cloudMarkReceived` idempotent server-side via a `arrived_at is.null` PATCH filter** — today the wrapper PATCHes unconditionally; a retried/duplicate confirm would overwrite the first receipt timestamp with a later one. Append `&arrived_at=is.null` to `markReceivedUrl` so the server only stamps the *first* confirmation (mirrors the local `target.arrivedAt` idempotency guard) and a racing double-tap can't move the stamp forward.
- **RLS policy review for the `arrived_at` write** — confirm the `marketplace_listings` UPDATE policy actually lets the *buyer* (not just the owner) PATCH `arrived_at`, and ONLY that column. A buyer-scoped column-level grant (or a dedicated `mark-received` Edge Function like `claim-listing`) would prevent a buyer from also overwriting `asking_price`/`notes` through the same RLS-gated PATCH endpoint. Document the decision in MANUAL-TASKS.md.
- **Queue `cloudMarkReceived` through the write-rate-limiter + offline requeue** — `markListingSold`/`addListing` go through the BE-29 `appWriteLimiter` and persist-then-sync queue, but `markListingReceived`'s `void cloudMarkReceived(...)` is fire-and-forget: an offline confirm stamps locally and is never retried, so the cloud and seller never learn. Route it through the same `createRateLimitedDeliver` + flush path the other mutations use.
- **pgTAP integration test for the buyer-receipt cascade + RLS** — add a `supabase/tests/` case that seeds a sold listing, asserts the buyer can PATCH `arrived_at` but the seller cannot, asserts a non-party gets 0 rows, and (per BE-25) that the row CASCADE-deletes with the buyer's account. The current coverage is structural (URL/body shape) only; the live RLS contract for the new write path is unverified.

## MKT-1 buyer-receipt idempotency follow-ups (2026-06-29)
- **Distinguish "already stamped" from "permission denied" in `cloudMarkReceived`** — with the `arrived_at=is.null` filter + `return=representation`, a 200 with an empty array now means *either* the row was already received *or* RLS hid it from this caller. Both currently resolve `true`. Parse the representation body: treat a returned row as a genuine first-stamp, an empty array on an already-`arrived_at` row as an idempotent no-op (still `true`), and surface a distinct signal when RLS actually rejected the buyer so a real authorization failure isn't swallowed as success.
- **Apply the same `is.null` first-write guard to `markSoldUrl` (`sold_at`)** — `cloudMarkSold` PATCHes `sold_at` unconditionally just like the old `cloudMarkReceived` did; a duplicate "mark sold" tap can move the sale timestamp forward. Mirror the MKT-1 pattern with `&sold_at=is.null` so the first sale stamp is authoritative, then add a shapes test asserting the filter.
- **Add a `lib/postgrest-filters.ts` helper for `column=is.null` query params** — `markReceivedUrl` now hand-concatenates `&arrived_at=is.null`; as more idempotent first-write filters land (`sold_at`, future `cancelled_at`), extract a tiny pure `isNullFilter(column)` / `andFilter(url, clause)` builder (percent-encoding-aware, `?`-vs-`&` separator-aware like `withPageLimit`) so the PostgREST filter syntax lives in one tested place instead of being duplicated across shape builders.
- **Buyer-foreground self-heal for `arrived_at` (pairs with the seller-side suggestion)** — the existing follow-up covers the *seller* learning of a confirmation via foreground re-pull; the buyer's own device that fired an offline confirm also needs reconciliation. On foreground, for any purchase whose local `arrivedAt` is set but whose last cloud write `cloudMarkReceived` returned `false` (queued), re-fire through the BE-29 limiter so the buyer's optimistic stamp actually reaches the server.
- **Structural test that every "first-write-wins" PATCH builder carries its `is.null` guard** — once `arrived_at` and `sold_at` both use the pattern, add a guard test that greps the marketplace shape builders for unconditional timestamp PATCH URLs missing an `is.null` filter, so a future first-write column (e.g. `delivered_at`) can't silently ship a last-write-wins overwrite bug. Mirrors the SEC-style structural-adoption guards.

## CI-1 security-review workflow follow-ups (2026-06-30)
- **Add a CI step that fails fast if a workflow references a non-existent marketplace plugin** — CI-1 was a silent failure: the `claude-security-review` job errored at plugin-install on every PR for days because `security-review@claude-code-plugins` doesn't exist, but nothing surfaced it (the job failed without blocking merge). Add a tiny `scripts/check-workflow-plugins.ts` (+ `lint:workflows`) that parses every `.github/workflows/*.yml` `plugins:` input and asserts each referenced `<plugin>@<marketplace>` resolves against a known allow-list (e.g. `code-review`), so a typo'd or removed plugin fails `lint:ci` instead of dying invisibly in Actions.
- **Make the security-review (and code-review) job status visible / required** — both Claude review jobs currently run with `pull-requests: read` and post comments, but a hard install/auth failure just shows a red check most contributors ignore. Decide whether `claude-security-review` should be a required status check on `main` for PRs that touch the sensitive `paths:`, and document the policy in `SECURITY.md` so a broken gate can't merge unreviewed sensitive diffs again.
- **Pin `anthropics/claude-code-action@v1` to a commit SHA** — both review workflows use the floating `@v1` tag, so a breaking change in the action (or its bundled CLI dropping a built-in command) can silently re-break the gate exactly like CI-1. Pin to a SHA with a `# v1.x.y` comment and bump via Dependabot, matching the security posture of the rest of the pipeline.
- **Surface the built-in `/security-review` findings as a sticky PR comment summary** — confirm `claude-code-action@v1` posts the built-in command's findings as a PR comment (the plugin form did this automatically); if not, wire `comment-pr`/a summary step so the security pass produces a visible, actionable artifact rather than just job logs, otherwise the gate "runs" but no one sees the result.
- **Add a scheduled smoke test that the review workflows actually invoke a resolvable command** — a weekly `workflow_dispatch`/`schedule` job that runs `claude-code-action@v1` with `/security-review` against a no-op diff and asserts exit 0 would catch marketplace/CLI drift proactively (the class of breakage behind CI-1) instead of waiting for the next sensitive PR to rediscover it.

- **Lift the public→private premium gate into a `canMakeCollectionPrivate(isPremium, current)` helper in `lib/premium-helpers.ts`** — the create-collection and collection-detail edit screens now each inline the same predicate (`!isPremium && next === "private" && (current ?? "private") !== "private"`). Extracting it next to the other premium-derived defaults removes the duplication, makes the transition rule unit-testable without React, and guarantees the two gates can't drift apart.
- **Add a `defaultCollectionVisibilityForUser(isPremium)` helper and reuse it in both create + edit** — create-collection initialises `useState(isPremium ? "private" : "public")` inline; the edit screen seeds `editVisibility` from the stored value. A shared helper keeps the "free accounts default to public" rule in one place and lets a structural test assert both screens consume it.
- **Replace the locked-chip toast with the conversion-friendly upsell sheet across BOTH the create and edit flows** — the existing `.suggestions.md` upsell-sheet idea was scoped to `app/create-collection.tsx`; now that the edit screen has the identical locked Private chip, the sheet (benefit copy + one-tap "Activate premium" CTA) should be a shared component wired into both tap handlers so the upgrade prompt is consistent.
- **Re-validate premium server-truth before opening the collection-edit modal** — the edit gate reads the client-cached `isPremium`. A user whose subscription lapsed server-side but whose local cache is stale could still see an unlocked Private chip until the next `cloudValidatePremium`. Firing a lightweight foreground re-validate when the edit modal opens (or on screen focus) closes the brief trust gap on the paid feature.
- **Add an analytics event when a non-premium user taps a locked Private chip (create or edit)** — today the lock is silent telemetry-wise. A taxonomy-safe `trackEvent("premium_gate_blocked", { surface: "create" | "edit", feature: "private_collection" })` (id/enum props only, SEC-13 compliant) would quantify how often the gate fires and feed the upsell-sheet conversion decision.

- **Reuse `defaultCollectionVisibilityForUser` to seed the collection-detail edit modal too** — `app/collection/[id].tsx` initialises `editVisibility` from the stored collection value and falls back to a hard-coded `"private"`. For a brand-new-collection edge case the fallback could lean on the same premium-derived default helper, keeping the "free accounts lean public" rule in exactly one place across create + edit.
- **Add a `canMakeCollectionPrivate(isPremium, current)` companion helper in `lib/premium-helpers.ts`** — both the create save-gate (`finalVisibility = isPremium ? visibility : "public"`) and the edit transition-gate now express the public→private premium rule inline. A single predicate helper (returning whether the transition is allowed) would let both screens and a unit test share one source of truth, mirroring how `defaultCollectionVisibilityForUser` consolidated the default-state rule.
- **Extend the i18n structural test to assert `visibilityPrivatePremiumOnly`/`premiumTitle` exist in every language map** — the premium gate now surfaces these strings on two screens (create + edit). A regression dropping the key from a non-English map would silently render English; a `__tests__/i18n-translations.test.ts` guard (the next backlog item) closes that gap.
- **Co-locate the listing-cap and premium-badge derived defaults next to `defaultCollectionVisibilityForUser`** — the task note references "listing cap, premium badge, etc." as sibling premium-derived defaults, but those rules still live in their own modules/components. Gathering them into `lib/premium-helpers.ts` (or a `lib/premium-defaults.ts`) would make the full set of free-vs-premium defaults reviewable and testable in one file.
- **Add a structural test asserting no screen inlines the `isPremium ? "private" : "public"` ternary** — now that the canonical helper exists, a lint-style scan over `app/`/`components/` that fails if the raw ternary reappears would prevent the consolidated rule from silently drifting back into a component.

- **Generalise the i18n premium-gate key-coverage test into a parametrised "critical keys present in every language" guard** — the new `languageBlock(code)` slicer could check a list of business-critical keys (premium gate, marketplace, auth errors) rather than just `visibilityPrivatePremiumOnly`, so any future user-facing string that must never silently fall back to English is enforced structurally.
- **Add a full i18n parity test that fails if a non-en map declares a key absent from `en`** — today the spread-`...en` pattern means a typo'd override key in `ru`/`be`/etc. would add a dead key rather than override the intended one. A test asserting every non-en key exists in `en` would catch override typos that silently render the English fallback.
- **Provide real translations for `visibilityPrivatePremiumOnly` in ru/be/pl/de/es** — all five currently inherit the English string via `...en`. The premium-gate toast now shows on two screens (create + edit collection), so non-English users see English copy on a conversion-critical prompt. Translating the five maps closes the localisation gap the new test only structurally guards.
- **Extract the `languageBlock(code)` slicer into a shared `__tests__/i18n-test-helpers.ts`** — both the existing English-keys test and the new premium-gate test parse the same `lib/i18n-context.tsx` source; a shared block extractor would de-duplicate the regex and let future i18n structural tests reuse it.
- **Wire a CI assertion that the count of keys in each language map is within N of `en`** — a coarse drift signal: if a language map is missing many keys (e.g. half), it likely regressed. A `lint:i18n` script reporting per-language key counts would surface large gaps that per-key tests miss.

- **Convert the edit-collection public→private locked chip to the new `PremiumUpsellSheet`** — `app/collection/[id].tsx` still fires `toast.error(visibilityPrivatePremiumOnly)` when a non-premium user taps the locked Private chip in the edit modal. Now that the reusable sheet exists, swapping the toast for `<PremiumUpsellSheet onActivated={() => /* keep edit private */}>` would give both create and edit flows the same conversion-friendly upsell instead of a fire-and-forget toast.
- **Convert the marketplace listing-cap upgrade hint to the upsell sheet** — `marketplaceUpgradeHint` is surfaced when a free user hits the one-active-listing cap. Reusing `PremiumUpsellSheet` (with a marketplace-specific `title`/`body`) there would consolidate every "you hit a premium wall" moment onto one component and one CTA instead of scattered hints.
- **Track an "upsell shown / activated" analytics funnel** — `trackEvent("collection_created", …)` already fires, but the new sheet has no instrumentation. Emitting `premium_upsell_shown` (with a `source` like `create_collection_private`) and `premium_upsell_activated` would measure the sheet's conversion lift over the old toast — the explicit reason the task swapped them.
- **Add a `source`/`feature` prop to `PremiumUpsellSheet`** — the component is reusable but anonymous; a typed `source` prop threaded into the activation toast and a future analytics event would let each call site (create, edit, marketplace) be attributed without duplicating copy, and would pair naturally with the funnel suggestion above.
- **Mount `PremiumUpsellSheet` once at shell level behind a `usePremiumUpsell()` hook** — every screen that needs it currently has to own `useState` + render the modal. A context-driven `showPremiumUpsell({ title, body, onActivated })` (mirroring the existing `confirmDialog` pattern) would let any gated affordance trigger the sheet with one call and no per-screen modal plumbing.

- **[DONE 2026-07-02] Apply the same in-flight `pending`-promise dedup to `lib/analytics.ts`** — `initSentry()` now guards concurrent boots so the native bridge handshakes once; `lib/analytics.ts:initAnalytics` likely has the identical "flip `initialised` only after the loader awaits" shape, so two racing calls (auth-state change + language switch) can double-load the PostHog SDK. Mirror the `let pending` pattern (and clear it in the reset helper) for parity.
- **Promote the `pending`/`initialised`/`runInit` lazy-init shape into a shared `lib/lazy-init.ts:makeLazySingleton(run)` helper** — both `lib/sentry.ts` and `lib/analytics.ts` hand-roll the "init once, dedup concurrent callers, allow reset" lifecycle. A 20-line factory returning `{ init, reset, isReady }` would let the next telemetry SDK (Clarity) inherit race-safety for free and keep the dedup invariant in one tested place.
- **Add a structural test asserting `initSentry` returns the `pending` promise on a concurrent call** — the new dedup is verified behaviourally with a gated loader, but a regex guard (`/if \(pending\) return pending/` in `lib/sentry.ts`) would fail-closed if a future refactor accidentally drops the early-return and reintroduces the double-handshake race without changing observable timing in the fast test path.
- **Surface `lastInitError` on `getSentryStatus()` instead of only `console.warn`-ing loader failures** — `runInit`'s catch logs `[sentry] init failed` and silently flips `initialised`; storing the caught error in a module-scoped `lastInitError` and exposing it on the status snapshot would let the diagnostics screen (and a future `sentry-doctor` script) show *why* init failed rather than just `reason: "init-failed"`.
- **Reset `pending` defensively inside `runInit`'s own `finally` as a belt-and-braces guard** — today `pending` is cleared by `initSentry`'s `finally`, which is correct, but co-locating a `pending = null` reset with the `initialised = true` flip in `runInit` would keep the two lifecycle flags in sync even if a future caller invokes `runInit` directly, eliminating a class of "init done but pending still set" states.

- **Adopt the new `addBreadcrumb` `level` argument at real severity call sites** — the wrapper now accepts `"warning"`/`"error"`, but every existing crumb (only `navigation-breadcrumbs.tsx` today) still emits the default `"info"`. Emitting `addBreadcrumb("user denied photo permission", …, "warning")` from the image-picker permission-denied path and `addBreadcrumb("upload failed", …, "error")` from `lib/cloudinary.ts`'s catch would make the crash timeline colour-code the run-up to a failure instead of a flat grey list.
- **Add a `console.error`/no-op ESLint guard against passing an unknown breadcrumb `level`** — `SentryBreadcrumbLevel` is a compile-time union, but a call site that builds the level dynamically (`level as string`) could smuggle an invalid value into `sdk.addBreadcrumb`. A tiny runtime clamp in `addBreadcrumb` (`const lvl = LEVELS.has(level) ? level : "info"`) plus a test would keep a bad dynamic value from reaching the SDK where Sentry silently drops the crumb.
- **Thread a matching `level` into `captureException`'s `context`** — breadcrumbs now carry severity but captured exceptions are always default-level. Adding an optional `level` field to `captureException`'s context (mapped onto Sentry's event `level`) would let non-fatal handled errors (e.g. a retried network failure) be tagged `"warning"` so they don't inflate the fatal-crash rate in the dashboard.
- **Promote the fake-SDK loader harness (`makeFakeSdk`) into `__tests__/helpers/fake-sentry-sdk.ts`** — `sentry-opt-out.test.ts` and the new `sentry-breadcrumb-level.test.ts` both re-declare the same `Call[]` recorder + `bootWithFakeSdk` helper. Extracting it into one shared helper would let every future functional Sentry test (setUser scoping, rate-limit windows) reuse the recorder without copy-paste drift.
- **Document the breadcrumb-severity convention in a `lib/sentry.ts` doc block** — now that `level` is a real knob, a short comment table ("info = navigation/lifecycle, warning = recoverable/user-declined, error = failed operation about to surface an exception") would keep call sites consistent so the crash timeline's colours stay meaningful instead of every dev picking a level ad-hoc.

- **Surface `lastInitError` on `getSentryStatus()` as a `lastInitError` field** — the new `getSentryLastInitError()` getter is a separate call; folding the error's message into the `SentryStatus` snapshot (the object already returned by the `__sentryStatus()` devtools global) would let the diagnostics screen show *why* `reason: "init-failed"` in one read instead of two.
- **Build the `scripts/sentry-doctor.ts` self-check now that `getSentryLastInitError()` exists** — the stored cause was the missing half; a `npm run sentry:check` that boots the wrapper, prints DSN reachability + `getSentryLastInitError()`, and exits non-zero on failure would let operators validate wiring without the Sentry UI (already queued in suggestions, now unblocked).
- **Reset `lastInitError`/`initErrorLogged` inside `shutdownSentry()` too** — today only `__resetSentryForTests` clears them, so a mid-session diagnostics-toggle-off then a successful re-init leaves a stale `lastInitError` reported by the getter. Clearing on shutdown keeps the getter honest across the opt-out lifecycle.
- **Cross-tag the init failure into a Sentry-independent breadcrumb buffer** — when init fails there's no SDK to receive breadcrumbs, so the run-up context is lost. A tiny in-memory ring buffer that `addBreadcrumb` also writes to (drained into the SDK once ready) would let a later successful init replay the pre-init breadcrumbs that led to the original failure.
- **Assert the one-shot guard structurally in `sentry-tests-peer-dep-free`-style test** — a regex guard (`/if \(!initErrorLogged\)/` in `lib/sentry.ts`) would fail-closed if a future refactor drops the guard and reintroduces per-retry `console.error` spam, catching the regression without relying on the behavioural shutdown+re-init timing.

## Analytics init-dedup follow-ups (2026-07-02)
- **Promote the `pending`/`initialised`/`runInit` lazy-init shape into a shared `lib/lazy-init.ts:makeLazySingleton(run)` helper** — `lib/sentry.ts` and `lib/analytics.ts` now both hand-roll the identical "return the in-flight promise, flip `initialised` in `finally`, clear `pending`" dance. A single tested helper (returning `{ init, isReady, reset }`) would collapse the duplication and guarantee both wrappers stay in lock-step, so a future fix to one can't drift from the other.
- **Add a structural guard that every telemetry init keeps its concurrent-dedup shape** — a regex test (`/if \(pending\) return pending/` in both `lib/sentry.ts` and `lib/analytics.ts`) would fail-closed if a refactor drops the guard, the same way `sentry-tests-peer-dep-free` pins the lazy-import invariant. Cheap insurance against silently reintroducing the double-boot race.
- **Surface an `analytics-doctor` / `getAnalyticsStatus()` snapshot mirroring `getSentryStatus()`** — `lib/analytics.ts` still only exposes `isAnalyticsReady()`; the Sentry side grew a structured `{ ready, initialised, optedOut, reason }` snapshot for debugging "why isn't it capturing?". A parallel getter (plus a stored `lastInitError` like Sentry now has) would let a settings "diagnostics" panel explain a not-ready analytics wrapper.
- **Replace the `console.warn` on analytics loader-failure with a one-shot `console.error` + stored `lastInitError`** — `lib/sentry.ts` already migrated to the one-shot-guard + stored-cause pattern (est 1300 task); `lib/analytics.ts:runInit` still `console.warn`s on every failed boot with no persisted cause. Mirroring it keeps the two telemetry wrappers symmetric and makes the failure diagnosable.
- **Reset `pending` defensively inside `runInit`'s own `finally` as a belt-and-braces guard in `lib/analytics.ts`** — today `pending` is cleared by `initAnalytics`'s `finally`, which is correct, but co-locating a defensive clear next to where `initialised` flips (mirroring the same suggestion already logged for `lib/sentry.ts`) would make `runInit` self-contained and robust to a future caller that invokes it directly.

## Sentry CaptureContext follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Mirror the typed `CaptureContext` narrowing onto `addBreadcrumb`'s `data` param** — `captureException` now takes a structured `{ scope?, extra? }` union, but `addBreadcrumb(message, data?: Record<string, unknown>, level?)` still passes a loosely-typed `data` bag. Narrowing it to a shared `BreadcrumbData` shape (or reusing `CaptureContext["extra"]`) would give breadcrumb call sites the same IntelliSense and kill the same drift risk the capture path just fixed.
- **Add a `level?: "fatal" | "error" | "warning" | "info"` field to `CaptureContext`** so callers can down/up-rank a captured exception (e.g. a recoverable retry-exhausted fetch as `warning`) instead of everything landing at Sentry's default `error` severity. `toSentryCaptureContext` would forward it verbatim, and it composes cleanly with the existing `scope`/`extra` mapping.
- **Structural test that no `captureException` call site passes an ad-hoc key** — a repo-wide regex guard asserting every `captureException(err, { … })` uses only `scope`/`extra` would fail-closed if a future edit reintroduces the old `{ context: "…" }` (or invents `{ route }`, `{ tags }`) shape, pinning the convention the way `sentry-capture-wiring` pins the individual call sites.
- **Forward a `fingerprint?: string[]` through `CaptureContext`** so high-volume, same-root-cause errors (e.g. every realtime handler throw) can be grouped under one Sentry issue instead of fragmenting by stack. `toSentryCaptureContext` already builds a partial-scope object; adding `if (context.fingerprint) payload.fingerprint = …` is a two-line extension.
- **Promote `scope` into an actual Sentry tag key namespace** (`tags: { "app.scope": scope }`) to avoid colliding with any built-in `scope` tag Sentry may reserve, and document the tag name in `docs/` so dashboard filters reference a stable key. Cheap rename now, painful migration later once dashboards are built on the current key.

## Sentry DSN validation follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Surface the malformed-DSN state through `getSentryStatus()`** — `resolveSentryConfig` now disables Sentry on a bad DSN, but the status snapshot still reports `reason: "missing-dsn"` for a *present-but-malformed* DSN (dsnPresent is true, so it falls through to "init-failed"). A dedicated `"malformed-dsn"` reason (derived from `isValidSentryDsn(activeConfig.dsn)`) would make the smoke-test diagnostic point at the real fix.
- **Reuse `isValidSentryDsn` in a `scripts/check-required-env.ts` / deploy-time guard** — validating the DSN shape at build time (in `lint:ci`) would fail the deploy before shipping a broken telemetry pipeline, rather than only catching it lazily at first `resolveSentryConfig` call in the browser.
- **Extend the DSN regex to reject the deprecated secret-key form** (`https://<public>:<secret>@host/id`) explicitly with a clearer warning, since Sentry dropped the secret half years ago and a pasted legacy DSN is a common migration foot-gun that currently just fails the `[^@/]+` public-key class opaquely.
- **Add a matching `isValidPostHogHost`/DSN guard to `lib/analytics-config.ts`** — the analytics wrapper trusts its host/key envs unchecked the same way Sentry used to; mirroring the validate-then-disable-with-one-shot-warning pattern keeps the two telemetry configs symmetric.
- **Unit-test the exact `SENTRY_DSN_PATTERN` against a table of real-world DSNs** (self-hosted `http://` on a custom port, region-scoped `o123.ingest.us.sentry.io`, DSNs with a path prefix) to pin the accepted grammar before someone tightens/loosens the regex and silently disables a valid production DSN.

## Sentry tracesSampleRate follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Warn once when `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_TRACES_SAMPLE_RATE` is set but out-of-range/non-numeric** — today `resolveTracesSampleRate` silently swallows a bad value and falls back to 0.1, mirroring the malformed-DSN foot-gun. A one-shot `console.error` (reusing the existing `malformedDsnWarned` pattern) would tell the operator their tuning knob was ignored.
- **Add a `profilesSampleRate` knob alongside traces** — Sentry's continuous profiling is gated on `profilesSampleRate`; exposing `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_PROFILES_SAMPLE_RATE` through the same `resolveTracesSampleRate`-style parser and threading it into `mod.init` would let performance profiling be tuned without a redeploy, same as traces.
- **Extract the shared `[0,1]` clamp-or-default parser into `lib/env.ts:resolveUnitInterval`** — `resolveTracesSampleRate` and the pending `profilesSampleRate` both need "parse, validate in [0,1], else default"; a single tested helper (parameterised by the default) removes the copy-paste and pairs with the already-suggested `resolveNumericEnv` promotion.
- **Assert `tracesSampleRate` reaches `mod.init` for staging too** — the init test now covers a custom rate in production; a staging case would pin that non-production-but-enabled environments also honour the knob, guarding a future refactor that special-cases environments.
- **Document the cost/quota tradeoff of raising the sample rate** in `README-DEPLOY.md` (e.g. "0.1 = 10% of transactions; raising to 1.0 can exhaust the free-tier performance-unit quota") so an operator tuning the knob understands the billing implication before bumping it.

### runtime-config aggregator follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Add the `runtime-config-parity.test.ts` guardrail** — scan `lib/*-config.ts` for the `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` names they read and assert each appears in `README-DEPLOY.md`; ties the aggregator's env surface to the docs so a new knob can't land undocumented (already parked as a plain bullet — promote it now that the aggregator exists).
- **Migrate call sites onto `runtimeConfig`** — sweep imports of `cloudinaryConfig`/`sentryConfig`/`analyticsConfig` across `lib/` and `app/` to `import { runtimeConfig } from "@/lib/runtime-config"`, then a structural test can forbid deep-importing the individual `*-config.ts` singletons outside the aggregator.
- **Freeze `runtimeConfig` with `Object.freeze`** (and each slice) so a downstream module can't mutate the shared memoised config object and leak state between features; add a test asserting the object is frozen.
- **Emit a one-shot startup summary from the aggregator** — a `describeRuntimeConfig()` helper that returns `{ cloudinary: cloudName, sentry: enabled, analytics: enabled }` (never secrets) for a single boot-time `console.info`, giving operators a one-line "what's wired" signal without three separate logs.
- **Co-locate the next env-driven module here by convention** — document in `lib/runtime-config.ts`' header (and CONTRIBUTING/README-DEPLOY) that any new `EXPO_PUBLIC_*`-driven feature must add its resolver+singleton and register it in `runtimeConfig`, making the aggregator the enforced single place for env validation.

### runtime-config parity follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Extend the parity scan to APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md + eas.json** — the new `runtime-config-parity.test.ts` only checks `README-DEPLOY.md`; a companion assertion that every `lib/*-config.ts` `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` also has an `eas secret:create` line keeps the iOS/EAS secret set from drifting behind the web-deploy set (pairs with the already-parked `eas-secrets-parity.test.ts`).
- **Fold the parity scan into the `runtime-config.ts` aggregator's own test** — instead of re-deriving env names by regex, expose a `RUNTIME_CONFIG_ENV_VARS` const from each resolver and assert docs cover *that* list, so a renamed var can't silently slip the regex.
- **Wire `npm run lint:migration-docs`-style dedicated `lint:env-docs` script** so the env↔docs parity runs as its own named CI step (clearer failure attribution than a buried test) and can be invoked locally before pushing a new knob.
- **Add a reverse assertion** — every `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` documented in `README-DEPLOY.md` that a `lib/*-config.ts` no longer reads should be flagged as a stale doc row, catching env vars removed from code but left in the secrets table.
- **Backfill APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md** with the three newly-documented vars (`EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_ENV`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_APP_VERSION`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_RELEASE`) as `eas secret:create` entries so the native build path matches the web secrets set that README-DEPLOY.md now lists.

### deployment-env dedup follow-ups (2026-07-02)

- **Route the PostHog/next config through `normaliseDeploymentEnv` too** — when the third env-driven module lands, wire its environment resolution through `lib/deployment-env.ts` from day one instead of re-rolling the collapse, so the "single source of truth" property holds as the surface grows.
- **Add a structural test forbidding a re-introduced local `normaliseEnvironment`** — grep `lib/*-config.ts` and assert none declare their own `function normaliseEnvironment`, so a future config can't silently fork the collapse rule again.
- **Make `lib/env.ts` node-safe by lazy-loading `react-native`** — move the `Platform` import inside `getAppBaseUrl` (mirroring the Sentry SDK lazy-import pattern) so `lib/env.ts` can host pure helpers like `normaliseDeploymentEnv` directly and its structural-only tests can become real unit tests.
- **Introduce a `"preview"` deployment bucket end-to-end** — the dedup now makes this a one-line change in `lib/deployment-env.ts`; add `"preview"` to `DeploymentEnvironment`, decide its reporting policy once, and both Sentry + analytics inherit it consistently.
- **Re-export `normaliseDeploymentEnv` + `DeploymentEnvironment` from `lib/runtime-config.ts`** so the aggregator is the one import surface for every env-config primitive (config singletons + the shared env parsers), matching the "single place for env validation" goal.

## iOS infoPlist codification follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Add `expo.ios.icon` once the 1024×1024 asset lands** — the infoPlist block is now codified but `expo.ios.icon` was deliberately skipped because `assets/icon.png` doesn't exist yet (guide section 4 is a MANUAL step). When the icon is exported, add the key plus a one-line extension to `__tests__/appstore-ios-config.test.ts` asserting the referenced path resolves on disk, closing the last section-3 gap.

- **Localize the three usage-description strings via `expo.locales`** — Apple renders `NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription` in the system language, and `CFBundleLocalizations` now declares 6 languages but the permission strings are English-only. Expo supports per-language `InfoPlist.strings` via the `locales` key pointing at JSON files; wiring `locales/{ru,be,pl,de,es}.json` (strings pulled from the existing i18n maps) would make the permission prompts match the app language.

- **Add the `scripts/check-appstore-config.ts` pre-flight validator** — the next task in `.tasks.md` already; the new structural test covers app.json↔guide parity, but a `lint:ci`-wired validator that also checks `bundleIdentifier` non-empty and (future) icon path resolution catches regressions in the lint stage before the test suite runs.

- **Assert the expo-image-picker plugin string and infoPlist string stay intentionally distinct** — `app.json` now carries two photo-permission strings: the plugin's `photosPermission` and `infoPlist.NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription` (which wins at prebuild). A comment-style structural test documenting that the infoPlist value overrides the plugin's would prevent a future engineer from "fixing" one and wondering why the prompt didn't change.

- **Generate the guide's section-3 JSONC block from app.json** — the parity test asserts guide ⊇ app.json strings, but the guide's fenced ```jsonc block is still hand-maintained and could drift structurally (e.g. a renamed key). A tiny `scripts/generate-appstore-snippet.ts` that re-emits the block from `app.json`'s actual `ios` object (run in `lint:ci` with a diff check) would make app.json the single source of truth.

## App Store config pre-flight follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Fold `__tests__/appstore-ios-config.test.ts`'s value checks into the pure validator** — the structural test and the new `findAppstoreConfigIssues` overlap on the four required keys; moving the guide-parity and AppLanguage-lock-step assertions into optional validator inputs (`guideContent?`, `supportedLanguages?`) would leave one source of truth for "submission-ready" and shrink the test to a thin harness.

- **Require `expo.ios.icon` once the asset lands** — the validator deliberately treats the icon key as optional today; when `assets/icon.png` is exported, flip the check to required (one-line change in `findAppstoreConfigIssues`) so a future removal of the key redlines CI the same way a dropped bundleIdentifier does.

- **Extend the pre-flight to Android submission keys** — a `check-playstore-config` sibling (or a `platform: "ios" | "android"` parameter) validating `expo.android.package`, `versionCode` strategy, and `adaptiveIcon` completeness would give the Play Store track the same lint-stage safety the iOS track now has.

- **Validate `associatedDomains` format in the pre-flight** — the validator checks infoPlist keys but not `associatedDomains`; asserting every entry matches `applinks:<hostname>` (no scheme, no path) would catch the classic `https://`-prefixed mistake that silently breaks Universal Links at review time.

- **Print a diff-style hint on failure** — `formatAppstoreConfigReport` lists issues but not the expected shape; appending the canonical minimal `ios` block (generated from `REQUIRED_INFO_PLIST_KEYS`) to the error output would let an engineer fix the regression from the CI log alone without opening APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md.

## Privacy-manifest single-source follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Wire the manifest into expo prebuild via `expo.ios.privacyManifests`** — Expo SDK 50+ aggregates a `privacyManifests` key from app.json into the native `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` at prebuild. Emitting that JSON shape from `lib/privacy-manifest.ts` into app.json (and asserting parity in the existing test) would make the committed plist authoritative for `eas build` instead of a reference artefact.

- **Auto-patch the guide table instead of print-and-paste** — `scripts/generate-privacy-manifest.ts` prints the table for manual pasting; teaching it to splice the rendered table between the section-6 header and the following paragraph (mirroring `build-spa-fallback`'s patch pattern) would remove the last manual step and let `privacy:generate` fully own both artefacts.

- **Derive PRIVACY.md from the same module** — the guide's section 6 says the public privacy policy must "mirror the table above"; a `renderPrivacyPolicyMarkdown()` emitter producing the user-facing PRIVACY.md section from `PRIVACY_MANIFEST` would extend the single source of truth to the hosted policy page GitHub Pages serves.

- **Add required-reason API coverage checks** — `ACCESSED_API_TYPES` declares UserDefaults/CA92.1 today, but Sentry and PostHog SDKs also touch file-timestamp and system-boot-time APIs on iOS. A structural test greping `node_modules/@sentry/react-native` + `posthog-react-native` for their shipped `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` files and asserting our manifest doesn't contradict them would catch an SDK bump that adds a new required-reason API.

- **Validate the plist with a real parser in CI** — the shape test asserts substrings; adding a tiny DTD-less XML parse (e.g. `fast-xml-parser` devDependency, or a 20-line hand-rolled well-formedness check) would catch a malformed emit (unbalanced tags after a future edit) that substring assertions can miss.

## EAS-secrets parity follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Close the web-deploy gap for Cloudinary/PostHog vars** — the parity scan surfaced that `deploy.yml` injects only Supabase + Sentry vars, while the guide's EAS list also carries `EXPO_PUBLIC_CLOUDINARY_*`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_POSTHOG_*`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_APP_URL`, and `EXPO_PUBLIC_CLARITY_PROJECT_ID`. If image upload/analytics are expected to work on the GitHub Pages build, those secrets need `env:` lines in the "Build web" step; if they're intentionally native-only, document that in README-DEPLOY.md and encode it as a second exemption map in the parity test.

- **Extend the parity scan to `.env.example`** — the tracked `.env.example` is the fourth artefact carrying the same names; folding it into `eas-secrets-parity.test.ts` (every EAS secret has an example line) would complete the four-way triangle the suggestions file has been circling.

- **Parse deploy.yml's `env:` blocks structurally instead of regexing the whole file** — the current scan matches `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` anywhere (including comments), which can't distinguish "injected" from "mentioned". A tiny YAML parse (js-yaml devDep or the existing hand-rolled approach in workflow tests) keyed on `jobs.build.steps[].env` would make the "injected in web builds" set exact.

- **Assert the guide's §14 intro sentence stays true** — §14 says "mirror the GitHub Actions secrets listed in README-DEPLOY.md"; a one-line test that README-DEPLOY.md's GitHub-secrets table is a superset of the EAS list (not just each name individually) would catch a future README restructure that silently drops the table the sentence points at.

- **Generate §14's `eas secret:create` block from a typed module** — same single-source pattern as `lib/privacy-manifest.ts`: a `lib/eas-secrets.ts` const listing `{name, required, note}` could emit both the guide's fenced block and a future `scripts/eas-secrets-push.sh` helper, ending the hand-maintained command list entirely.

## EAS preview build-on-merge follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Add EXPO_TOKEN to the workflow's secret-status report pattern** — deploy.yml prints `[set]/[missing]` for each Sentry secret; mirroring that one-liner in eas-preview.yml's probe step (it already echoes on missing) plus a badge in README-DEPLOY.md would make "why didn't my merge queue a build" answerable from the Actions log alone.

- **Extend the job to an ios+android matrix once a Play Store track exists** — the task said "matrix" but only iOS has a submission checklist today; when `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` gets a Play sibling, flip `strategy.matrix.platform: [ios, android]` and parameterize `--platform ${{ matrix.platform }}` (the structural test's `--profile` assertion already generalizes).

- **Path-filter the trigger to native-relevant changes** — every docs-only merge queues (then supersedes) an EAS build today; adding `paths-ignore: ['**.md', '.tasks/**', 'docs/**']` to the push trigger would save EAS minutes without losing coverage, since JS-only changes still affect the Hermes bundle and should keep building.

- **Post the queued build URL back to the commit status** — `eas build --no-wait --json` emits the build ID/URL; piping it into a `gh api` commit-status (or a step summary) would link each main commit to its Expo build page, closing the "results live in the Expo dashboard, not GitHub" visibility gap the README note admits to.

- **Pin eas-cli to a major version** — `npx eas-cli@latest` tracks Expo's release train; a breaking CLI flag rename would fail the job silently-ish. Pinning `eas-cli@^16` (matching eas.json's `cli.version >= 16`) and bumping deliberately keeps the workflow deterministic, and a structural test can assert the pin matches eas.json's declared range.

## Sentry version-guard follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Generalize the guard into a `lib/check-pinned-majors.ts` table** — the same "config-shape rewrites across majors" risk applies to `@supabase/auth-js`, `@supabase/realtime-js`, and `posthog-react-native`. A declarative `{ name, expectedMajor, reason }[]` scanned by one script would extend the protection for ~10 lines per package instead of a new script each.

- **Assert the installed node_modules version too when present** — the guard reads package.json + the lockfile; adding a best-effort `node_modules/@sentry/react-native/package.json` read (skipped when absent) would also catch a locally-mutated install that diverges from the lockfile before the developer even commits.

- **Fail on tilde→caret widening** — `^7.5.0` passes today because only the major is compared, but caret invites minor bumps that Sentry has occasionally used for breaking RN-bridge changes. A stricter option: assert the declared range starts with `~` so widening the contract is a deliberate, reviewed edit.

- **Surface the guard's constant in `.sentry-setup.md`** — the setup doc walks through SDK installation; a line noting "the repo pins major 7 via lint:sentry-version — bump EXPECTED_SENTRY_MAJOR when upgrading" would route future upgraders to the right file instead of letting them fight CI.

- **Add a Renovate/Dependabot ignore rule for @sentry/react-native majors** — the guard fails CI on a major bump PR, but configuring the bot to open majors as draft (or not at all) plus a `dependencyDashboard` note would prevent red-CI noise and make the upgrade path explicitly manual.

## Sentry-doctor follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Fix the stale `.sentry-setup.md` reference in deploy.yml** — the sourcemap-upload step's comment says "See .sentry-setup.md §10" but no such file exists in the repo. Either restore/commit the doc or repoint the comment at README-DEPLOY.md's new "Sentry self-check" section; a tiny docs-parity test could keep workflow comments honest.

- **Teach sentry-doctor to load `.env` itself** — today the operator must `source .env` first; a 10-line dotenv-style parser (the repo already avoids the dotenv dep) reading `.env` when present would make `npm run sentry:check` a true one-command diagnostic.

- **Add an `--event` smoke mode** — an optional flag that sends a real test envelope through the DSN (mirroring the in-app "send test error" path) and polls the issues API for its arrival would upgrade the reachability probe into an end-to-end delivery check.

- **Cross-check the doctor's release against the deployed bundle** — deploy.yml stamps `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_RELEASE=collectables@<sha>`; fetching the live GitHub Pages `index.html`, extracting the bundle hash, and comparing the tagged Sentry release to the deployed sha would catch "deploy succeeded but release tagging silently stopped" drift.

- **Wire sentry-doctor into a weekly scheduled workflow** — a cron GitHub Action running `npm run sentry:check` with the repo secrets (and opening an issue on failure) would catch expired auth tokens and quota-suspended DSNs before an incident needs them, at zero marginal effort since the script already exits non-zero on hard failures.

## Sentry lazy-import guard follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Measure the actual layout-import bundle cost** — `app/_layout.tsx`'s static `Sentry.wrap`/`ErrorBoundary` import means the SDK still lands in every web bundle despite the lazy path in `lib/sentry.ts`. A `scripts/analyze-bundle.ts` pass (expo export + source-map-explorer) would quantify whether a lazy `ErrorBoundary` shim (render children until the SDK loads) is worth the complexity.

- **Provide a `SentryRootWrapper` indirection** — moving the two static imports behind a `components/sentry-root.tsx` that itself lazy-requires the SDK when `sentryConfig.enabled` (falling back to a passthrough boundary otherwise) would let even the layout drop the static import, shrinking dev/test web bundles; the allowlist in the new structural test then shrinks to zero.

- **Extend the recursive scanner to other heavyweight SDKs** — the `appCodeFiles()` walker in `sentry-lazy-import.test.ts` is generic; a table of `{ module, allowlist }` entries (posthog-react-native → lib/analytics.ts only, @supabase/realtime-js → lib/realtime.ts only) would enforce the same import-discipline for every optional-at-runtime dependency.

- **Guard the loader-injection seam** — `InitOptions.loader` exists so tests can inject a fake SDK; a structural assertion that no *production* module passes a `loader:` option (grep app/, components/) would prevent someone from wiring an eager custom loader that defeats the gate.

- **Document the allowlist rationale in CLAUDE.md's architecture section** — the "static import only in _layout.tsx, everything else via @/lib/sentry" rule now lives in a test message; a one-line architecture note would surface it at code-writing time instead of at CI-failure time.

## Power BI generated schema-doc follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Generate the "Schema reference" column table too** — section 4's `Column / Postgres type` table is still hand-maintained; deriving it from `supabase/migrations/20260508_analytics_events.sql` (the migration-structural-test helpers already parse column lists) would close the last hand-synced surface in the Power BI doc.

- **Reuse the marker-injection helper for other generated docs** — `injectPowerbiSchemaBlock` is the generic "replace between markers, throw when missing" shape; extracting a `lib/doc-markers.ts` (`injectBlock(source, begin, end, content)`) would let the privacy-manifest table in `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` move from "must contain verbatim" test-assertions to the same regenerate-and-commit flow.

- **Emit a Power Query M snippet per event** — the generated table lists property keys; also generating a ready-to-paste `Table.ExpandRecordColumn` M expression per event (keys pre-filled) would save the report builder the manual expand-clicking the doc currently describes.

- **Feed `ANALYTICS_EVENTS` descriptions into PostHog event definitions** — the taxonomy's `description` strings are now surfaced in the BI doc, but PostHog's event-definition metadata (the tooltip analysts see) is still empty; a `scripts/sync-posthog-event-definitions.ts` hitting PostHog's API with the same map would give both tools the same glossary.

- **Assert generated-block freshness inside `build:powerbi`** — `scripts/build-powerbi-template.ts` bundles `docs/powerbi-connection.md` into the template zip; having it call `injectPowerbiSchemaBlock` first (or run the `--check` mode) would guarantee a stale doc never ships inside the distributed `.pbit` asset even when someone bypasses `lint:ci`.

## Power BI connection CLI follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Reuse `parseDotEnv` in sentry-doctor** — the ".env self-loading" suggestion for `scripts/sentry-doctor.ts` is now a 3-line change: import `parseDotEnv` from `lib/powerbi-conn.ts` (or hoist it into a shared `lib/dotenv-lite.ts`) so `npm run sentry:check` works without `source .env` first.

- **Derive `<region>` from a documented env var** — an optional `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_REGION` (documented in README-DEPLOY.md) would let `powerbi:conn` print a fully copy-pasteable pooler host instead of the `aws-0-<region>` placeholder; validation could assert it matches `[a-z]{2}-[a-z]+-\d`.

- **Add a `--uri-only` flag** — printing just the Postgres URI (no summary prose) would make the CLI composable: `npm run -s powerbi:conn -- --uri-only | pbcopy` for clipboard workflows, or as input to `psql` smoke checks in CI against a preview branch.

- **Offer a Metabase/psql variant in the same output** — the summary already contains everything Metabase and `psql` need; a second stanza ("Metabase: host/port/db/user in separate fields", "psql: full URI") would serve the planned `docs/metabase-connection.md` fallback path without a second script.

- **Structural test that the doc's §2–3 values match the CLI's** — a test that greps `docs/powerbi-connection.md` for the pooler host shape, port, database, and username pattern and asserts they equal the constants in `lib/powerbi-conn.ts` would keep the guide and the CLI from drifting apart (today both hard-code `aws-0-<region>.pooler.supabase.com`).

## Metabase fallback doc follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Validate the three SQL measures against a seeded fixture** — the same idea as the pending DAX-validation task: a `__tests__/bi-sql-equivalents.test.ts` running the doc's DAU / funnel / conversion SQL against an in-memory seeded table (or a pure-JS reimplementation over fixture rows) would catch a typo in either guide's formulas.

- **Extract the shared SQL into `docs/bi/queries/*.sql`** — both guides now describe the same three measures; keeping the SQL as standalone files (included into each doc by a marker-injection step like the generated schema table) would guarantee Power BI's documented SQL-equivalents and Metabase's queries never diverge.

- **Document a read-only Postgres role for BI** — both guides currently require the service-role secret; a `MANUAL-TASKS.md` snippet creating a `bi_readonly` role with `SELECT` on `analytics_events` only would remove the biggest operational risk of hooking a third-party BI tool to production.

- **Add a docker-compose profile for local Metabase** — a `docs/metabase/docker-compose.yml` with a pinned Metabase version + persistent volume would make the fallback reproducible and let CI smoke-test that the container boots.

- **Generate a Metabase collection export** — Metabase supports serialized collection import; shipping a `docs/metabase/collectables-starter.json` (the three questions pre-built, mirroring the `.pbit` starter template) would close the last parity gap with the Power BI guide's §7.

## Power BI cost-projection follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Price-drift canary** — the doc hard-codes 2026 list prices ($10 Pro, $20 PPU, ~$260 F2); a yearly-dated "verified as of" line plus a lint that fails 12 months after that date would force a re-check instead of letting stale prices mislead a budgeting decision.

- **Fold the analytics-cost-projection task into a single `docs/costs.md`** — the pending `.tasks` item for a PostHog/Supabase linear-projection table overlaps this doc's "data volume won't trigger us" claim; one consolidated cost page with per-vendor sections would avoid three scattered cost docs drifting apart.

- **Viewer-count decision flowchart** — a small mermaid diagram (author-only → $0; +scheduled → Metabase or $10; +viewers → $10×N or Metabase) would compress the two tables into the one glance the founder actually wants.

- **Track the F-SKU floor** — Fabric F2 pricing changes more often than Pro/PPU; since we cite it only as an "not our scale" anchor, consider replacing the dollar figure with a link-out to Microsoft's pricing page to reduce drift surface.

- **Cost telemetry cross-check** — once the analytics-mirror volume is measurable, a `scripts/estimate-bi-cost.ts` reading `analytics_events` row counts and printing "you are at X% of the free ceiling; projected paid date Y" would turn both projection docs into a live gauge.

## BI SQL fixture-validation follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Assert the CHECK constraint + RLS posture in the same pgTAP file** — the fixture already exercises inserts; two more cheap asserts (`throws_ok` on a 201-char event name, `is_empty` on an `anon`-role SELECT) would make 03_bi_sql_equivalents also guard the analytics_events security contract end-to-end.

- **Generate the pgTAP queries from the doc** — the three SQL blocks now live in `docs/metabase-connection.md` and the pgTAP file; a small extractor (```sql fences → `supabase/tests/03_*.sql` between markers) would collapse the parity test from token-matching to literal identity.

- **Seed-fixture reuse for the DAX starter template** — the 11-row fixture models exactly the funnel/DAU/conversion shapes; exporting it as `docs/powerbi/fixture.csv` would let a report author validate the .pbit measures against known-good numbers without touching production.

- **Property-payload coverage** — every fixture row uses the default `{}` properties; seeding one row with a realistic payload and asserting `properties ->> 'mode'` round-trips would validate the doc's jsonb-expansion idiom too.

- **Run pgTAP on a nightly schedule, not just on supabase/** paths** — a formula typo introduced by editing only the docs wouldn't re-trigger the workflow; a weekly `schedule:` cron on supabase-test.yml closes that gap at near-zero cost.

## Timing-safe secret comparison follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Adopt `timingSafeEqualStrings` for any future header-secret gate** — `analytics-mirror` is the only shared-secret webhook today, but the next one (e.g. a Stripe/Cloudinary notification endpoint) should import the `_shared/timing-safe-equal.ts` helper from day one; a structural test listing the "webhook functions" (like the cors/assert-caller adoption lists) would enforce it as the fleet grows.

- **Unicode-normalise before comparing** — `timingSafeEqualStrings("é", "é")` is `false` because NFC and NFD encode differently; secrets are operator-pasted opaque strings so this is correct today, but a `{ normalize?: "NFC" }` option (documented as off by default) would prevent a confusing mismatch if a secret is ever pasted through a normalising input.

- **Rotate-friendly dual-secret window** — accept `POSTHOG_WEBHOOK_SECRET` OR `POSTHOG_WEBHOOK_SECRET_NEXT` (each compared constant-time) so an operator can rotate the PostHog webhook secret with zero downtime: set NEXT, flip PostHog, promote NEXT→current, unset NEXT. Mirrors the SECURITY.md runbook's rotation guidance.

- **Length-leak note in SECURITY.md** — the byte-length short-circuit (like the old loop's) reveals only the secret's length to a probing attacker; a one-line note in the SECURITY.md security-model section documenting this accepted trade-off would pre-empt a future "is this a vuln?" report.

- **`node:` specifier compatibility guard** — a tiny structural test asserting every `supabase/functions/**` import is either `https://esm.sh/...`, a relative `.ts`, or an allow-listed `node:` builtin (crypto only, today) would catch an accidental bare-npm-specifier import that deploys fine locally but fails at the edge.

## analytics-mirror payload-limit follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Stream-abort instead of read-then-measure** — the authoritative check still buffers up to the full oversized body before rejecting; reading `req.body` via a `ReadableStream` reader and aborting the moment the running byte count crosses `MAX_PAYLOAD_BYTES` would bound memory too, not just the insert.

- **Make the cap operator-tunable** — a `POSTHOG_WEBHOOK_MAX_BYTES` Edge Function secret (validated positive-integer, defaulting to `MAX_PAYLOAD_BYTES`) would let an operator widen the bound for a legitimate high-volume batch destination without a redeploy, mirroring the `ALLOWED_ORIGINS` pattern.

- **Event-count bound to pair with the byte bound** — 256KB can still hold thousands of tiny events; capping `events.length` (say 500) with the same 413/`{ maxEvents }` shape would bound the Postgres insert row count directly rather than indirectly through bytes.

- **413 telemetry breadcrumb** — a rejected payload is a misconfiguration signal (PostHog batching turned way up, or a rogue caller); logging a one-line `console.error("analytics-mirror: payload too large", declaredBytes)` (no body content — SEC-20 hygiene) would make the reject visible in Edge Function logs, and pairs with the existing "Sentry breadcrumb on 207" suggestion.

- **Adopt the gate fleet-wide via a structural adoption list** — like the `cors-shared`/`assert-caller` adoption guards, a test asserting every body-reading Edge Function (`claim-listing`, `accept-friend-request`, …) either uses `payload-limit` or is explicitly allow-listed (tiny fixed-shape bodies) would keep the next webhook-scale function from shipping unbounded.

## extractEvents promotion follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Decide the bare-array contract explicitly** — a top-level `[{event}, …]` payload now yields no events (400 "empty payload"); if any real webhook vendor sends bare arrays, one line (`Array.isArray(payload) ? payload : …`) would accept them as a batch. Worth a deliberate decision + test either way rather than inheriting it.

- **Type the return as `readonly PostHogWebhookEvent[]`** — `extractEvents` returns the caller's own `batch` array by reference; a `readonly` return type would stop a future function edit from mutating the parsed payload in place.

- **Fold the 413 event-count bound into `extractEvents`'s call site** — with the byte cap (#220) and the promoted extractor both in place, `events.length > MAX_EVENTS` is now a one-liner in the function with a pure constant next to `MAX_PAYLOAD_BYTES`; pairs with the earlier "event-count bound" suggestion.

- **Property-based fuzz over the webhook trio** — a tiny generator feeding random JSON shapes through `extractEvents` → `buildAnalyticsEventRow` and asserting "never throws anything but AnalyticsMirrorPayloadError, never returns a row without a name" would pin the whole pipeline's failure envelope, not just the enumerated cases.

- **Retire the `@ts-nocheck` in analytics-mirror/index.ts** — with `extractEvents` gone the function body is mostly typed imports + fetch globals; a `deno check` CI step (or a ts-expect-error-scoped header for the `Deno` global only) would restore type safety over the one remaining unchecked Edge Function source.

## Insert-timeout follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Idempotent inserts to defuse the timeout double-insert window** — a timed-out insert may still land server-side, and PostHog's retry would then insert the batch again; a deterministic event UUID (hash of name+distinct_id+timestamp) with `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` (or a unique index + `upsert`) would make retries safe. Needs a migration, so mirror into MANUAL-TASKS.md.

- **AbortSignal plumbing when supabase-js supports it** — `withTimeout` deliberately does not cancel the losing insert (PostgREST offers no abort through the client today); if `@supabase/supabase-js` gains per-query `abortSignal` on inserts, threading the deadline's signal through would stop the orphaned work instead of just unblocking the response.

- **Surface 504s in the ops dashboard** — a timeout burst means the database is degraded, which is exactly when telemetry matters; folding the "Sentry breadcrumb on 207" suggestion into a shared `reportMirrorAnomaly(status)` that also fires on 504 would give one pane of glass for both partial failures and slowness.

- **Retry-After header on the 504** — PostHog honours standard backoff, but an explicit `Retry-After: 30` on the 504 (and maybe the 413) is a one-liner that makes the contract explicit for any future non-PostHog webhook source pointed at the mirror.

- **Fleet-wide deadline adoption** — the other service-role functions (`delete-account`, `export-data`) run multi-statement cascades that can also hang; adopting `withTimeout` there (with per-function ceilings) plus a structural adoption-list test would bound every Edge Function's worst case, not just the webhook's.

## Edge Sentry reporting follow-ups (2026-07-03)

- **Also report the 504 timeout path** — `reportMirrorAnomaly` takes a status; a second call site on the new insert-timeout 504 (and arguably the 413) would put database slowness on the crash dashboard too, completing the "single pane of glass" the 207 report started.

- **Rate-limit the anomaly reports** — a PostHog destination misconfigured at scale could 207 on every webhook, turning the mirror into a Sentry-quota drain; a tiny module-scoped counter (e.g. max 5 reports/min, mirroring `lib/sliding-window-limiter.ts`'s shape) inside `sentry-report.ts` would cap the blast radius.

- **Attach a sampled error message** — the report is deliberately counts-only, but the *first* `errors[0].error` string (a transformer message like "missing event name", never user data) would make the Sentry issue actionable without grepping logs; needs a careful PII review since the message is constructed from payload state.

- **Envelope `sent_at` vs event `timestamp` drift** — both come from one `new Date()` today; if the helper ever batches or retries, split them so Sentry's clock-skew correction keeps working.

- **Deno-side contract test** — the helper is Node-tested, but a `supabase/tests`-style smoke (or a `deno check supabase/functions/**` CI step, already suggested for the `@ts-nocheck` retirement) would prove the `.ts`-extension import graph of all five `_shared` modules stays Deno-resolvable as it grows.

## Migration-asserts helper follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Adopt `sql-migration-asserts` across the remaining ~18 `*-migration.test.ts` suites** — the shared helper shipped with only the two seed adopters (analytics_events, chat_messages); a mechanical sweep of `base-schema`, `marketplace-*`, `subscriptions`, `core-tables-rls`, etc. onto `loadMigrationSource`/`assertColumns`/`assertIndex`/`assertRlsEnabled` would delete a few hundred duplicated regex lines and make the adoption-guard test's allowlist unnecessary.

- **Add `assertPolicy(source, name, { for, clause })` to the helper** — the chat_messages test still hand-rolls `CREATE POLICY "..." FOR SELECT ... USING` shapes; a structured policy assert (name + command + USING/WITH CHECK presence) is the next most-duplicated pattern across the RLS-era migration tests (`core-tables-rls`, `subscriptions`, `marketplace-transfers`).

- **Add `assertIdempotent(source)`** — a helper that fails when a migration contains a bare `CREATE TABLE`/`CREATE INDEX`/`ADD COLUMN` without `IF NOT EXISTS` (outside `DO $$` guards), pinning the re-runnable-migration convention the repo already follows by hand.

- **Wire `assertManualTasksDocuments` into `scripts/check-migration-docs.ts`** — the lint script and the test helper now both encode the "every migration is documented in MANUAL-TASKS.md" rule independently; extracting one shared pure module (`lib/migration-docs.ts` already exists — reuse it in the helper) would keep the two enforcement points from drifting.

- **Teach `assertIndex` an optional `unique` flag** — `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` shapes (chat_id integrity, subscriptions one-row-per-user) currently can't use the helper; a `{ unique?: boolean }` third arg keeps those tests on the shared shorthand instead of falling back to raw regexes.

## Migration-naming lint follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Fold `lint:migration-docs` into `lint:migration-naming`** — the new scanner already surfaces undocumented migrations (it reuses `findUndocumentedMigrations`), so CI now reports that failure twice; retiring the older step (or making it an alias) removes the duplicate signal while keeping the shared pure matcher.

- **Enforce version-prefix monotonicity** — extend `findMigrationNamingIssues` to flag a new migration whose numeric prefix sorts *before* the latest applied one (eg. adding `20260101_x.sql` today); `migration-apply-order.test.ts` covers ordering of existing files, but a lint-time check catches a back-dated filename before it lands.

- **Flag duplicate version prefixes at lint time** — two files sharing `20260628_` apply in lexicographic-slug order, which is surprising; `migration-versions-unique.test.ts` guards exact duplicates, but the lint step could warn on same-day prefixes with interdependent SQL (or simply mirror the uniqueness rule so the failure shows up in the lint report alongside naming issues).

- **Add a `--fix` suggestion mode** — for a misnamed file the report could compute the nearest conforming name (lowercase, underscores, today's date prefix) and print the exact `git mv` command, making the failure self-serviceable for contributors who don't know the convention.

- **Scan `supabase/tests/` naming too** — pgTAP files follow an implicit `NN_snake_case.sql` order-prefix convention (`01_…`, `03_bi_sql_equivalents.sql`); the same pure module could host a second pattern so the CI harness's execution order is as guarded as the migrations'.

## Analytics event-name contract follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Bound property keys too** — `analytics_events.properties` is unconstrained jsonb; a companion test iterating each event's `props` array and pinning ASCII camelCase + a length cap would keep Power Query column names stable the same way the name test now keeps `name` insertable.

- **Pin the event-name prefix taxonomy** — names currently follow an implicit `<domain>_<verb>` shape (`chat_opened`, `premium_activated`); a test asserting exactly one underscore-separated domain from a known set would stop a future `openedChat` slipping into the union and fragmenting BI group-bys.

- **Share the NAME_CAP constant** — the 200 cap now lives in the migration, the name-bounded test, and (implicitly) the analytics-mirror row builder; exporting `ANALYTICS_NAME_MAX = 200` from `lib/analytics-events.ts` and consuming it in the test + `buildAnalyticsEventRow`'s validation would collapse three copies into one.

- **Reject over-cap names in the Edge Function pre-insert** — today an over-long name from a rogue producer fails the DB CHECK and burns a 207 error row; `buildAnalyticsEventRow` could enforce `length <= 200` itself so the failure is a typed per-row error with a clear message instead of a Postgres constraint string.

- **Event-name usage parity** — a structural test that greps `app/`+`lib/`+`components/` for `trackEvent("` literals and asserts each is a member of `ANALYTICS_EVENT_NAMES` (and vice versa, that every union member has at least one call site or a documented "server-only" marker), catching dead taxonomy entries and untyped ad-hoc emits in one sweep.

## Analytics-mirror kill-switch follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Consume `mirrorDisabled` somewhere visible** — the flag is a typed contract with no consumer yet; a first adopter could be a settings-screen diagnostics row ("event mirror: on/off") or a `trackEvent` breadcrumb tag, so operators can confirm the switch took effect in a deployed bundle without reading source.

- **Server-side counterpart** — the client flag can't stop PostHog from POSTing to the Edge Function; a matching `ANALYTICS_MIRROR_DISABLED` function secret that makes `analytics-mirror` return 202-and-drop would complete the incident-response story (client contract + server tap both off).

- **Extract the truthy-literal parser** — `isAnalyticsDisabledByEnv` is the third copy of the "1/true/yes" idiom (realtime + analytics + now mirror reuse the same one, but `lib/supabase-realtime.ts` still has its own); a shared `lib/env-flags.ts:isEnvFlagSet()` would make the next kill-switch a one-liner.

- **Kill-switch documentation table** — README-DEPLOY.md now documents four independent operator switches (realtime, analytics, mirror, runtime-supabase-config); a short "incident response" section listing them side-by-side with blast radius would save an operator scanning a 20-row table mid-incident.

- **Parity test for kill-switch semantics** — a structural test asserting every `EXPO_PUBLIC_*_DISABLED` var read anywhere in `lib/` goes through the same truthy-literal parser (no ad-hoc `=== "true"` comparisons) would keep switch behaviour uniform as more are added.

## Fake-DOM helper follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Auto-restoring variant** — a `withFakeDom(opts, fn)` wrapper that installs the fakes, runs `fn`, and restores in a finally block would remove the try/finally boilerplate from every call site and make the leak-on-forgotten-restore failure mode impossible.

- **Leak canary in test-globals** — the global `beforeEach` in `__tests__/test-globals.ts` could assert `globalThis.window === undefined` and fail loudly naming the previous test when a suite forgets `restore()`; today a leaked fake DOM surfaces as a confusing downstream failure in whichever web-gated module runs next.

- **Grow the stub toward meta-tag injection** — the next likely web-only consumer (OpenGraph/SEO meta tags) needs `document.querySelector("meta[...]")` and `setAttribute`; adding those to the fake (recorded in a `fake.attributes` log) keeps the "one shared stub" promise ahead of demand.

- **localStorage stub sibling** — several web-only paths (`clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig`, theme persistence) gate on `window.localStorage`; a `setupFakeStorage()` companion in the same helpers directory (backed by a Map, with a quota-exceeded switch) would complete the browser-globals toolkit.

- **Type the created script nodes** — `fake.created` is `FakeNode[]` but clarity's assertions cast to `{ id?; src?; async? }` by hand; exporting a `FakeScriptNode` with those optional fields (what `createElement` actually returns) would drop the per-test casts.

## Clarity custom-tag follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Wire the traits mirror** — `AnalyticsProvider` already computes the `identifyUser` traits (isPremium, language, environment); a `useEffect` that calls `addClarityCustomTag` for each coarse trait after `initClarity()` succeeds would light up replay segmentation end-to-end (the original motivation for the wrapper).

- **Re-tag after re-init** — tags don't survive `shutdownClarity()` + re-inject (fresh queue shim); a module-level `pendingTags` map replayed inside `initClarity()`'s success path would make `addClarityCustomTag` set-and-forget across diagnostics toggles.

- **Tag-key allowlist** — a `CLARITY_TAG_KEYS = ["isPremium", "language", "environment"] as const` union (mirroring the analytics-events taxonomy pattern) would stop ad-hoc keys drifting into the replay tool where they're hard to clean up.

- **Expose `upgrade` reason API** — Clarity also supports `clarity("upgrade", reason)` to prioritise session recording; a sibling `upgradeClaritySession(reason)` wrapper (same gates) would let rare-but-interesting flows (premium purchase, listing sold) force full replay retention.

- **Structural no-globals guard** — a test asserting no file under `app/`/`components/` references `window.clarity` directly (the wrapper is the only sanctioned access) would keep the gate discipline as adoption grows, mirroring the sentry lazy-import allowlist test.

## Clarity input-mask audit follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **ESLint no-restricted-imports rule** — the lint script catches raw `<TextInput` post-hoc; an eslint `no-restricted-imports` entry for `react-native`'s `TextInput` in `app/**` + `components/**` (pointing at `MaskedTextInput`) would surface the violation in the editor as-you-type instead of at `lint:ci` time.

- **Mask non-input PII surfaces** — Clarity records all DOM text, not just inputs; a `MaskedText` sibling wrapper (stamping the same `dataSet`) for the few places raw user PII renders as plain text (settings email row, profile edit preview) would extend the guarantee beyond form fields.

- **Runtime DOM audit in dev** — a `__DEV__`-only web effect that queries `document.querySelectorAll("input:not([data-clarity-mask])")` after mount and `console.warn`s the offenders would catch inputs rendered by third-party components (e.g. a future date-picker lib) that the static grep can't see.

- **Verify the exported bundle carries the attribute** — extend `scripts/verify-bundle-inlining`-style post-build checks with a grep for `data-clarity-mask` in `dist/_expo/static/js/web/*.js` so a react-native-web upgrade that changes `dataSet` handling fails the deploy, not production replay privacy.

- **Consolidate scan-dir walkers** — `check-inline-hex`, `check-clarity-input-mask`, and future greps each hand-roll a recursive `.tsx` walker; a shared `lib/walk-source-files.ts` (`collectFiles(dirs, ext)`) would keep scan scope (app/ + components/) consistent across all lint steps.

## Clarity disabled-warning follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Explain *why* analytics is disabled** — the warning says "dev environment or missing PostHog key" but `lib/analytics-config.ts` knows which it is; threading a `disabledReason` through `analyticsConfig` would make the one-line warning actionable without opening the resolver.

- **Symmetric PostHog warning** — the mirror case (PostHog key set, `enabled === false`) is equally silent today; the same once-guarded `console.warn` in `lib/analytics.ts:initAnalytics` would cover the other dashboard an operator stares at.

- **Surface on the diagnostics screen** — a `getClarityStatus()` snapshot (`{ injected, optedOut, warnedDisabledWithId }`) mirroring `getSentryStatus()` would let the settings/diagnostics screen show "replay tag: blocked (analytics disabled)" instead of relying on the console.

- **Route through Sentry breadcrumb** — when Sentry is active, `addBreadcrumb("clarity blocked", { reason })` alongside the warn would make "did replay ever load?" answerable from crash reports (pairs with the existing "clarity loaded" breadcrumb suggestion).

- **Once-guard helper** — `warnedDisabledWithId` is the third module-scoped warn-once flag in `lib/`; a tiny `lib/warn-once.ts` (`warnOnce(key, message)` backed by a Set, reset hook for tests) would standardise the pattern and its test reset story.

## Clarity-loaded breadcrumb follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Breadcrumb on shutdown too** — `shutdownClarity()` (opt-out, kill-switch) leaves no trace in the crash timeline; a paired `addBreadcrumb("clarity shutdown")` would let a crash report distinguish "replay never loaded" from "replay was torn down mid-session".

- **Category field** — Sentry breadcrumbs support a `category` (e.g. `"telemetry"`); threading an optional category through `lib/sentry.ts:addBreadcrumb` would group the clarity/navigation crumbs visually in the Sentry timeline instead of one flat list.

- **Allow-list as shared constant** — `BREADCRUMB_ALLOWED_DATA_KEYS` lives only inside `__tests__/analytics-pii.test.ts`; exporting it from a `lib/telemetry-allowlist.ts` consumed by both the test and a future runtime assert would make the PII contract visible to authors at the call site.

- **Init-failure breadcrumb** — `initClarity()`'s catch path returns false silently; an `addBreadcrumb("clarity load failed", {}, "warning")` there would surface CSP/adblock injection failures in crash reports where they're actionable.

- **PostHog loaded breadcrumb** — the same cross-tagging argument applies to the analytics SDK: a "posthog loaded" breadcrumb in `lib/analytics.ts` init success would complete the "which telemetry was live at crash time?" picture.

## Analytics-env docs follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Env-var docs parity test generator** — the README-DEPLOY table, APPSTORE eas-secret block, and `.env.example` each list overlapping-but-different env sets; a structural test that derives the expected set from `lib/*-config.ts` literal-access readers and asserts all three docs cover it would end per-var doc tasks like this one.

- **`.env.example` entry** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_ENV` is documented in both deploy docs but absent from `.env.example`; a commented-out line there is where local operators actually discover overrides.

- **Deploy workflow passthrough audit** — verify `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` actually exports `EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_ENV` into the build env when the secret exists; a documented-but-not-forwarded secret is the silent failure this doc row invites.

- **Table anchor links** — README-DEPLOY's secrets table and APPSTORE §14 duplicate descriptions; cross-linking each eas-secret comment to the README row (single source for semantics) would stop the two descriptions drifting.

- **Staging example** — both docs only show `production`; a one-line "staging build" example (`EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_ENV=staging` with SENTRY_ENV=production) would demonstrate the only scenario the override actually exists for.

### Expo-install drift gate follow-ups (2026-07-04)
