- **Widen the watched list to `@sentry/react-native`** — the Sentry SDK major is already pinned by `lint:sentry-version`, but a *minor* drift Expo recommends (native-module compatibility) currently lands in the advisory bucket; adding `@sentry/` to `WATCHED_PACKAGE_PREFIXES` (with the major-pin check keeping breaking bumps out) would close the same TestFlight gap for the crash-reporting SDK.

- **Cache the last-green expo-check result** — the CI step re-queries the Expo registry on every push; persisting `{sdkVersion, packageHashes} → clean` in the Actions cache and skipping the network call when nothing dep-related changed would cut a ~20s network dependency from most runs and make the step immune to registry blips on doc-only PRs.

- **Turn `unreachable` into a visible-but-green annotation** — today a registry outage soft-skips with a log line nobody reads; emitting a GitHub Actions `::warning::` (the CLI already knows the state) would surface "the drift gate did not actually run" on the PR checks page without blocking.

- **Assert the parser against a captured fixture of real expo output** — the drift-line regex is pinned to today's `pkg@ver - expected version: X` shape; checking in a `__tests__/fixtures/expo-install-check.txt` captured from a real full-network run (refreshed when Expo SDK bumps) would catch upstream format changes as a test failure instead of silent `unreachable` skips.

- **Fold the three version gates into one `lint:deps` umbrella** — `lint:sentry-version`, `lint:expo-install`, and the npm-audit step all police dependency health with separate scripts and CI steps; a single `scripts/check-deps.ts` orchestrator (shared report format, one CI step, per-gate soft/hard flags) would shrink ci.yml and give future gates (bundle-size budget is already suggested) a home.

### Premium-upsell instrumentation follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Fire `premium_upsell_shown` from the listing-cap gate too** — the premium listing cap (`lib/premium-helpers.ts`) blocks free users elsewhere in the marketplace flow; emitting the same event with `feature: "listing_cap"` would turn the new event into a complete premium-friction funnel instead of a single-feature probe.

- **Track upsell outcomes, not just impressions** — add a `premium_upsell_dismissed` / reuse `premium_activated` with a `source: "upsell_sheet_private_collection"` so the sheet's conversion rate (shown → activated) is measurable; today we'd only see the top of the funnel.

- **Debounce repeat taps on the locked chip** — a frustrated user tapping the locked chip 5× in a row emits 5 events and skews the "does anyone click it" signal; a per-mount once-flag (mirror the `chat_opened` debounce pattern) would make the count mean unique encounters.

- **Add a `docs/analytics-platform.md` section on gate-instrumentation conventions** — codify the `premium_upsell_shown` shape (`feature` slug + `source` screen) so future premium gates (private profiles, export limits) reuse the taxonomy instead of inventing `upsell_viewed_v2`-style variants.

- **Surface a PostHog insight recipe for the hide-the-chip decision** — the `[needs-data]` follow-up task needs a specific query ("premium_upsell_shown where feature=private_collection, last 30 days, unique users"); documenting it next to the DAX measures in `docs/powerbi-connection.md` makes the go/no-go check a copy-paste instead of dashboard archaeology.

### Bundle-size budget follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Print a size delta against the previous main build** — persist the last-green total (Actions cache or a gh-pages sidecar JSON) and have `check-bundle-size` log "+38 KiB vs main"; a slow leak of 20 KiB per PR never trips a fixed budget but is obvious as a trend line.

- **Per-chunk budgets** — today the gate sums all `dist/_expo/static/js/web/*.js`; budgeting `entry-*.js` separately from lazy chunks would catch a lazy `import()` silently collapsing into the entry bundle (the exact regression the gate exists for) even when the total stays under 4.5 MiB.

- **Gate the deploy workflow too** — ci.yml and deploy.yml build independently; adding the same `lint:bundle-size` step after deploy's `expo export` (with `--source-maps` stripped first) would catch a size regression that only reproduces in the secrets-enabled production build.

- **Emit a GitHub Actions `::notice::` with the headroom** — surfacing "188 KiB left" on every green run makes shrinking headroom visible on the checks page before it becomes a red build, mirroring the expo-install drift gate's advisory pattern.

- **Add gzip/brotli-aware measurement** — 4.4 MiB raw is ~1.1 MiB over the wire; measuring compressed size (Node's `zlib.brotliCompressSync` over each chunk) reflects real user cost and makes the budget meaningful for slow-connection UX rather than disk size.

### Public privacy policy follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Host `PRIVACY.md` at `/privacy` on GitHub Pages** — App Store review needs a public URL; render it to `dist/privacy/index.html` during the build (a small md→HTML pass in `scripts/build-spa-fallback.ts`, no new deps) so the policy ships with every deploy.

- **Link the policy from the app's Settings screen** — an in-app "Privacy policy" row (opens the hosted `/privacy` URL) next to the Diagnostics toggle closes the loop between the opt-out control and the disclosure that explains it; Apple reviewers look for exactly this pairing.

- **Auto-bump the effective date** — a lint step that fails when `PRIVACY.md` changes in a diff without its `_Effective date:_` line changing keeps the revision date honest without relying on reviewer memory.

- **Drive the sub-processor list from `lib/privacy-disclosure.ts`** — the backlog already plans a typed constant of `{name, url, dataTypes, retention}`; generating the policy's sub-processor table from it (like the Power BI schema doc) would make PRIVACY.md, the App Privacy table, and the future in-app disclosure provably consistent.

- **Add the account-deletion request path in-app** — the policy promises deletion via email; Apple's 5.1.1(v) increasingly expects in-app account deletion. A Settings → "Delete account" flow (Supabase `auth.admin.deleteUser` via an Edge Function) would upgrade the promise and simplify the policy paragraph.

### Analytics cost-projection follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Re-derive the 27k events/DAU constant from live data** — once PostHog has 30 days of production traffic, replace the estimate with `events last 30 days ÷ average DAU` (a `scripts/print-analytics-cost.ts` that queries the Supabase mirror could print the refreshed table).

- **Add a DAU gauge to the Power BI starter template** — the projection doc names ~30 DAU as the budgeting signal; a template page showing current DAU against the 37-DAU ceiling makes the crossing visible without opening the doc.

- **Unify the three retention figures** — `docs/analytics-platform.md` says the Supabase mirror keeps 90 days, while APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md/PRIVACY.md promise 13 months for server-side events; a single constant (e.g. in `lib/privacy-disclosure.ts`) plus a drift test would stop the docs from disagreeing about the same table.

- **Alert on free-tier burn rate** — a scheduled Edge Function (or the analytics-mirror itself) that counts current-month mirrored events and captures a Sentry warning event at 80% of 1M turns the projection into an operational alarm.

- **Fold the two cost-projection docs into a `docs/costs/` index** — PostHog and Power BI each have a tipping-point doc now; a one-page index listing every service's first paid trigger (Supabase storage, Cloudinary bandwidth, EAS builds too) gives the founder a single budget page.

### lint:peer-dep-free follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Add a `.husky/pre-push` (or simple `git config core.hooksPath`) hook that runs `lint:peer-dep-free`** — the task's motivation was a pre-push gate; the script exists but nothing invokes it locally yet.

- **Fold it into `lint:ci` as an early fast-fail** — running the 0.7s isolation guard before the 7s+ full suite makes the failure reason obvious at the top of the CI log.

- **Generalize to a `lint:invariants` umbrella** — other sub-second structural guards (analytics-events parity, runtime-config parity) could join a single fast pre-push script.

- **Do the SENTRY_TEST_FILES glob promotion (next backlog task)** — the hand-maintained list is the remaining fail-open gap; a `readdirSync` glob makes new sentry-*.test.ts files guarded automatically.

- **Print the elapsed time in the script output** — a `time`-style one-liner in the npm script keeps the "<100ms-class" promise honest as the file grows.

### Peer-dep-free glob follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Extend the glob guard to `lib/` modules** — the same static-import invariant matters for source files that lazily load the SDK; a `lib/**` sweep asserting only `lib/sentry.ts` may reference `@sentry/react-native` (and only inside `import(`) would close the front half.

- **Guard dynamic `require("@sentry/react-native")` too** — the regex only blocks static `import ... from`; a CommonJS-style require in a test would slip through.

- **Apply the same pattern to posthog** — `posthog-react-native` has the identical peer-dep-isolation story (`lib/analytics.ts` lazy loader); a `analytics-tests-peer-dep-free` glob guard would mirror the invariant.

- **Drop the count floor when it becomes noise** — the `>= 21` assertion will need bumping if sentry tests are ever consolidated; consider replacing with "glob count equals `ls` count" once the migration proves stable.

- **Run `lint:peer-dep-free` in the pre-merge path** — still pending from the previous suggestion block; the glob makes it strictly more valuable since new files are auto-guarded.

### SDK-absent smoke job follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Cache node_modules between the two CI jobs** — `sentry-sdk-absent` re-runs a full `npm ci` (~25s); sharing the install via actions/cache keyed on the lockfile (or a composite setup action) halves the added CI time.

- **Extend the absent-scope pattern to posthog** — `rm -rf node_modules/posthog-*` + the analytics test glob would prove the same lazy-load isolation for the analytics SDK.

- **Assert the job count in the branch-protection docs** — if the repo ever turns on required checks, the new job name needs to be in the required list; a README-DEPLOY note would prevent a silent gap.

- **Run the smoke with `--experimental-test-isolation=process`** — per-process isolation would make the test-globals reset unnecessary and the suite immune to the state-leak class entirely (needs a Node version check first).

- **Surface the discovered state-leak footgun in CONTRIBUTING/CLAUDE.md** — "always run sentry tests via npm test or with --import test-globals" is tribal knowledge as of today; one doc line saves the next person the same 25-false-failure detour.

### /privacy hosting follow-ups (2026-07-04)

- **Link the hosted /privacy URL from the app's Settings screen and the App Store Connect privacy-policy field** — the page now exists; the two consumers that need its URL still point nowhere.

- **Serve /privacy in the SW's offline fallback** — the exemption lets the network win, but offline warm clients now get a browser error page for /privacy; caching the policy page separately would keep the disclosure reachable offline.

- **Add a smoke check to the deploy workflow** — a post-build `test -f dist/privacy/index.html && grep -q "Privacy Policy" dist/privacy/index.html` step would catch a renderer regression at deploy time, mirroring the bundle smoke check.

- **Render a "last updated" footer from git** — the effective-date line is hand-maintained; deriving a "page generated from commit X on DATE" footer at build time gives reviewers provenance for free.

- **Promote the mini markdown renderer for other static pages** — a /terms or /support page (also App Store requirements) can reuse `renderPrivacyPage`'s skeleton with a title parameter.

## After: translated privacy pages + language picker (2026-07-05)

- **Translate the full PRIVACY.md, not just the Sentry paragraph** — the translated pages today carry only the crash-reporting disclosure with a "full policy in English" note; GDPR Art. 12 arguably covers the whole policy. The renderer and build loop already handle arbitrary markdown, so this is pure translation work per `PRIVACY.md.<code>`.

- **Auto-redirect /privacy by `Accept-Language`-equivalent** — GitHub Pages can't read headers, but the SPA can: when the app links to the policy (Settings → Privacy), build the href as `/privacy/<currentLanguage>/` from `useI18n()` so an in-app visitor lands on their own language instead of English.

- **Add `<link rel="alternate" hreflang>` tags to every privacy page head** — search engines and compliance scanners discover the translations only via the visible nav today; emitting the standard hreflang cluster (plus `x-default` → the EN page) in `renderPrivacyPage` is ~10 lines and makes the language set machine-readable.

- **Drift-guard the translated Sentry paragraph against the English source** — a test that hashes the EN Sentry blockquote in PRIVACY.md and stores the hash alongside each `PRIVACY.md.<code>` (e.g. an HTML comment `<!-- source-sha: … -->`) would fail CI when the English disclosure changes but a translation wasn't re-reviewed.

- **Surface the privacy-page link in the in-app language it's viewed in** — `app/settings.tsx` could add a "Privacy policy" row (via `t()`) opening `/privacy/<lang>/`; today the policy is only reachable by URL, so most users never see the disclosure the app worked to translate.

### Privacy-disclosure single source of truth (2026-07-09)

- **Render the PRIVACY.md sub-processor blockquotes from `SUB_PROCESSORS`** — today the prose paragraphs are hand-written and only the names/links/retention table are drift-guarded; a `renderSubProcessorSection(e)` template plus a verbatim-containment test (like the retention table) would make the whole "Where your data is stored" section regenerable.

- **Wire the in-app Settings → Privacy disclosure off `SUB_PROCESSORS`** — add a "Privacy & sub-processors" section to `app/settings.tsx` that maps `SUB_PROCESSORS` → `subProcessorSummaryLines()` rows with `Linking.openURL(e.privacyUrl)` taps, closing the third surface the disclosure module was built for (needs 6-language i18n for section title only; vendor facts stay EN).

- **Guard translated privacy pages against `SUB_PROCESSORS` facts** — `__tests__/privacy-page-i18n.test.ts` hardcodes the Sentry facts (sentry.io links, 90 days); re-derive those assertions from `SUB_PROCESSORS.find(e => e.id === "sentry")` so a retention change updates every guard from one place.

- **Add `dpaUrl` for Cloudinary and Clarity if/when published** — the interface already supports it; a periodic check (or a `lint:privacy-links` script that HEADs each `privacyUrl`/`dpaUrl` in CI-with-network) would catch dead vendor links before a reviewer does.

- **Emit a machine-readable `/privacy/subprocessors.json`** — `scripts/build-spa-fallback.ts` could serialize `SUB_PROCESSORS` next to the rendered privacy pages so enterprise/compliance scanners (and the future in-app screen on web) consume the same data over HTTP instead of re-parsing markdown.

### Privacy-page deploy smoke follow-ups (2026-07-05)

- **Extract the duplicated smoke-check shell into a `scripts/check-privacy-page.ts`** — the identical if/grep block now lives in both deploy.yml and ci.yml; a `npm run lint:privacy-page` script (tsx, reads `dist/privacy/index.html`) would give one source of truth, and the workflows shrink to one-liners.

- **Assert more than the title marker** — grep for the effective-date line and one sub-processor name (e.g. "Sentry") so a renderer bug that emits the `<title>` but drops the body still fails the check; the current single-marker grep passes on a page that is 99% empty.

- **Smoke-check `dist/404.html` and `dist/sw.js` in the same step** — build-spa-fallback.ts emits three artefacts but only /privacy is verified; a missing 404.html silently breaks every deep link on GitHub Pages, which is a worse regression than a broken policy page.

- **Verify the SW privacy exemption in the artifact** — grep `dist/sw.js` for the `/privacy` exemption path so a refactor of `lib/spa-fallback.ts` that drops the network-first carve-out is caught before warm clients start getting the SPA shell at the policy URL.

- **Post-deploy URL probe** — the deploy job knows `steps.deployment.outputs.page_url`; a final `curl -sf "$URL/privacy/" | grep -q "Privacy Policy"` step in the deploy job would verify the page as actually served by Pages (CDN, basePath, trailing-slash), not just as built.

### Diagnostics crash-report footer follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Extend the footer to analytics + replay** — the diagnostics toggle governs Sentry, PostHog, and Clarity together, but the new footer only reports crash events; once `getAnalyticsStatus()` (already planned) exists, a second line "Analytics: enabled — last event 5 min ago" would complete the "is anything leaving my device" picture.

- **Persist `lastEventSentAt` behind a debug flag** — the stamp is session-scoped by design, so a crash-on-launch app always shows "nothing sent yet" even though the previous session uploaded a report; an opt-in AsyncStorage mirror (admin/`__DEV__` only) would make the footer truthful across restarts without normalising telemetry bookkeeping for regular users.

- **Long-press the footer for the full snapshot** — wiring the existing `getSentryStatus()` fields (reason, environment, release, dsnPresent) into an alert/sheet on footer long-press gives testers the whole diagnostic without devtools, mirroring the planned `__sentryStatus()` global.

- **Stamp breadcrumbs too?** Deliberately not done — breadcrumbs are buffered client-side and only leave the device attached to an event, so stamping them would claim "sent" for data still on-device. Document this invariant in `lib/sentry.ts` if a future contributor tries to add it.

- **Audit remaining EN-only key clusters** — the diagnostics card was silently English for 5 of 6 languages until today's fix; a one-off script that diffs each language block's declared keys against `en`'s and reports clusters with 0 overrides (vs. feature areas that are fully translated) would surface the next such gap (premium? marketplace?) before a user does.

### app.json parity walker follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Extend the walker to `app.config.ts` overrides** — if the project ever adopts a dynamic config, the walker should evaluate the exported config instead of parsing app.json, otherwise drift can hide in the TS layer while the JSON stays green.

- **Pair by an explicit `x-parity` marker instead of name-containment** — the substring heuristic (`sentry` in `@sentry/react-native/expo`) could mispair a future extra key like `router` with `expo-router`; an optional `expo.extra.<key>.__plugin` field naming the package would make pairings exact while keeping the zero-registration default.

- **Assert one-sided fields too, behind an allowlist** — today only fields present on both sides are compared; a field that exists only in `expo.extra.sentry` (e.g. `url`) is unchecked by design, but an allowlist of known one-sided fields would catch a typo like `organisation` landing next to `organization`.

- **Run the walker against `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` pairings** — the privacy manifest generator has the same duplicated-declaration shape (module constant ↔ committed artefact); the parity walker pattern could be generalised into a tiny `lib/config-parity.ts` reused by both suites.

- **Surface parity failures in the CI summary** — a failing deepEqual prints the two values, but a `## Config drift` GitHub Actions job-summary line (echo to `$GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY`) naming the drifted field would save digging through the node:test TAP output.

### sourcemapsExpected follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Render the minified-traces hint on the settings diagnostics footer** — the data is now in `getSentryStatus()`; a second footer line ("Stack traces: readable / minified — add SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN") gated on `ready && !sourcemapsExpected` and admin/`__DEV__` closes the loop the field was built for.

- **Mirror the flag in ci.yml's web build** — CI builds without the token today produce `sourcemapsExpected: false` implicitly (var unset), which is correct, but inlining the same expression keeps the two workflows' env blocks symmetric and greppable.

- **Verify the flag landed in the bundle** — extend the planned `scripts/verify-bundle-inlining.ts` to also grep the deploy artifact for `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_SOURCEMAPS:"1"` when the secret-status step printed SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN [set], catching a babel-inlining regression on the new var.

- **Assert release parity between the flag and action-release** — when `sourcemapsExpected` is true, the uploaded release (`collectables@<sha>`) must equal the bundle's `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_RELEASE` or Sentry can't match the maps; a structural test that both lines use the same `github.sha` expression pins this.

- **Fold the workflow-derived vars into a single doc section** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_RELEASE` and `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_SOURCEMAPS` are both "set by the workflow, not by operators"; a dedicated README-DEPLOY subsection (and matching EAS_EXEMPT reason strings) would stop the secrets table from growing rows that aren't actually secrets.

### env-inlining CI guard follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Widen the scan roots beyond `lib/*-config.ts`** — `lib/sentry.ts`, `lib/analytics.ts`, and future SDK wrappers read env too; scanning all of `lib/**/*.ts` (with an allowlist for the `readFooEnvFromProcess` helpers' own files if ever needed) catches the footgun before a module earns the `-config.ts` suffix.

- **Retire the per-module structural assertions in `__tests__/sentry-env-inlining.test.ts`** — the "does not pass process.env whole" cases are now subsumed by the generic in-process guard in `__tests__/env-inlining.test.ts`; keeping both means two places to update when a helper is renamed.

- **Promote `stripComments` into a shared `lib/source-scan.ts`** — `scripts/check-secrets.ts` and `scripts/check-inline-hex.ts` scan raw source and can false-positive on commented-out code; reusing the comment-blanking pass would make all three lints comment-aware with one implementation.

- **Assert every key returned by `readFooEnvFromProcess` helpers is consumed by its resolver** — a key added to the helper but never read in `resolveFooConfig` (or vice versa) is silent drift; a structural test can diff `Object.keys(readFooEnvFromProcess())` against the `env.EXPO_PUBLIC_*` accesses in the same file.

- **Generate the `readFooEnvFromProcess` helpers from a `const` tuple** — the planned `lib/expo-public-env.ts` (`.tasks` line 177) can't use a loop (Metro needs literal accesses), but a tiny codegen script emitting the literal-access object from a declared var-name tuple would keep helpers mechanical and un-typo-able, verified by the new lint.

### expo-public-env shared reader follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Migrate `lib/runtime-config-gate.ts` onto the shared reader** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_ALLOW_RUNTIME_SUPABASE_CONFIG` is still read via an inline default-parameter access; routing it through a `makeExpoPublicEnvReader` tuple would put every EXPO_PUBLIC_ var behind the same parity contract.

- **Export a `ALL_EXPO_PUBLIC_VAR_NAMES` union from the three tuples** — `__tests__/runtime-config-parity.test.ts` currently regex-scans sources for env names; deriving the doc-parity check from the concatenated tuples would make it AST-free and immune to comment mentions.

- **Fail `lint:env-inlining` on readers that bypass the factory** — extend the scan to assert every `read*EnvFromProcess` export in `lib/*-config.ts` is produced by `makeExpoPublicEnvReader`, so a future module can't reintroduce the untyped hand-rolled shape.

- **Surface reader parity drift in Sentry, not just console.warn** — the warn-once branch is invisible in production; a `captureMessage("expo-public-env parity drift", { module })` (lazy import, mirrored from `lib/sentry.ts`) would make an `as`-cast escape observable.

- **Type `resolveFooConfig(env)` parameters with the tuple-derived shape** — `resolveSentryConfig` still accepts `Record<string, string | undefined>`; narrowing to `ExpoPublicEnv<typeof SENTRY_ENV_VAR_NAMES>` (plus a widening overload for tests) would catch a resolver reading a var it never declared.

### DSN-inlined diagnostics row follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Add the "stack traces readable/minified" companion row** — `sourcemapsExpected` is already in the snapshot; a second gated row ("Stack traces: readable ✅ / minified ❌ — add SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN") completes the tester-facing build-provenance story.

- **Show the release + environment under the DSN row** — `sentryStatus.release`/`environment` let a tester confirm *which* deploy they're on ("collectables@<sha> · production") without asking; both fields are already returned.

- **Extract a `buildDiagnosticsRows(status, gates)` pure helper** — the settings screen now derives three diagnostics strings inline; a pure helper in `lib/sentry-diagnostics.ts` would make the ✅/❌ logic unit-testable directly instead of via source-regex structural tests.

- **Tap-to-copy the full `getSentryStatus()` JSON from the row** — a long-press on the DSN row copying the snapshot to the clipboard turns "send me a screenshot" support threads into one paste.

- **Mirror the gate for the analytics key** — once `getAnalyticsStatus()` lands (.tasks line 187), render the same inlined-✅/❌ row for `EXPO_PUBLIC_POSTHOG_KEY` so both telemetry pipelines are verifiable from the same card.

### verify-bundle-inlining follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Derive the deploy-step env list from the build step at workflow-generation time** — the mirror rule is enforced by a structural test today; a small YAML-anchor (`&build-env` / `*build-env`) would make the two lists physically one, removing the drift class entirely.

- **Watch `EXPO_PUBLIC_POSTHOG_KEY` once the build step passes it** — the checker already lists it, but the deploy's `expo export` env omits it, so analytics is silently disabled in production web builds; wiring the secret into the build step (then the verify step) lights up PostHog and the check together.

- **Extend the verifier to assert the negative case for private secrets** — the same bundle read can assert `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`, `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` etc. do NOT appear in the artifact, merging `lint:secrets:bundle` and this check into one pass over dist.

- **Verify `EXPO_PUBLIC_SENTRY_SOURCEMAPS=1` reached the bundle when the auth token was set** — closes the loop for the `sourcemapsExpected` diagnostics flag the same way the DSN check does for capture.

- **Print a GitHub Actions job-summary table** — `echo "| var | status |" >> $GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY` from the verify step would surface inlining state on the run's summary page instead of buried in step logs.

### getAnalyticsStatus follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Render the analytics row on the settings diagnostics card** — the crash-report footer pattern is established; a second footer line driven by `getAnalyticsStatus().reason` ("Analytics: flowing / blocked — kill-switch") completes the card.

- **Unify the two status shapes behind a `TelemetryStatus` base type** — `getSentryStatus()` and `getAnalyticsStatus()` share `ready/initialised/optedOut/reason`; a common base in a `lib/telemetry-status.ts` would let the diagnostics screen map over both uniformly.

- **Track `lastEventSentAt` in the analytics wrapper** — Sentry stamps it on capture; mirroring it in `trackEvent` unlocks the same "last sent 3 minutes ago" footer for analytics.

- **Add a `triggerAnalyticsTestEvent()` twin of `triggerSentryTestError`** — a devtools global that fires a dedicated `diagnostics_test` event lets a tester verify the PostHog pipeline end-to-end from the console.

- **Expose the rate-limiter state in the snapshot** — a `rateLimited: boolean` (limiter window currently saturated) field would explain "events flowing but my clicks aren't arriving" without reading source.

### lazy-sdk factory follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Adopt `makeLazyLoader` for the dev-menu module** — `lib/dev-menu.ts:loadDevMenuModule` hand-rolls a similar conditional import; routing it through the factory unifies every lazy-import site.

- **Add an `onFirstLoad` hook to the factory** — Sentry wants a breadcrumb and Clarity a console note on first successful load; a `{ onFirstLoad?: (mod) => void }` option removes per-wrapper boilerplate.

- **Expose a `__resetLazyLoaderForTests` per loader** — the cached promise survives `__resetSentryForTests`, so a test that stubs the module registry after a real load sees the stale module; a reset handle mirrors the other test hooks.

- **Structural test for thunk-literal specifiers** — a scan asserting every `makeLazyLoader(() => import(` call passes a string literal (not a variable) would protect Metro's code-splitting requirement as new SDKs adopt the factory.

- **Preload on idle for high-probability SDKs** — a `loader.preload()` alias invoked from `requestIdleCallback` after first paint would hide the PostHog import latency behind idle time instead of the first tracked event.

### call-site parity test follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Extend the scanner to multi-line first args** — `trackEvent(\n  "name"` (prettier wrapping) would be missed today; a small multi-line regex or TS AST walk closes the gap.

- **Cover prop keys, not just names** — the same walk can capture the object-literal keys passed as the second arg and diff them against `ANALYTICS_EVENTS[name].props`, pre-empting the planned `assertValidProps` runtime guard with a static one.

- **Emit the call-site inventory into the Power BI doc** — "fired from app/create.tsx:214" per event helps analysts trace odd values back to code; the scanner already collects file:line.

- **Fail on `trackEvent(` with a non-literal first arg** — a variable event name defeats both the union and this test; asserting the scanned pattern accounts for every `trackEvent(` occurrence catches indirection.

- **Reuse the walker for `captureException` scopes** — the same parity shape can assert every `scope:` string passed to Sentry capture appears in a documented scopes list.

### prop-literal typing follow-ups (2026-07-09)

- **Type `trackEvent`'s payload per event** — overload `trackEvent<N extends AnalyticsEventName>(name: N, props?: Partial<Record<AnalyticsEventProps<N>, string | number | boolean | null>>)` so a typo'd prop key fails at the call site, not in a future runtime guard.

- **Implement `assertValidProps` on top of the literal tuples** — the planned `lib/analytics-validate.ts` (.tasks line ~199) can now derive its allowlist from `ANALYTICS_EVENTS[name].props` with full type safety.

- **Derive the Power BI doc's prop column types** — with literal keys available, the generator could annotate each prop with its observed value type from call sites.

- **Ban prop-name drift between events** — a lint asserting shared concepts use one spelling (`source` not `screen`/`origin` mixed) keeps dashboard slicers mergeable.

- **Export `ALL_ANALYTICS_PROP_NAMES`** — a flattened literal union across events, useful for the PII scrubber to assert no prop name collides with a reserved PostHog `$`-prefixed property.

## app.config.ts version auto-resolve follow-ups (2026-07-10)

- **Assert app.config.ts ↔ app.json non-version parity in CI** — today `__tests__/app-version.test.ts` walks `Object.keys(appJson.expo)` and deep-equals each field against the config export, but a key added *only* to app.config.ts (never to app.json) would be invisible to structural tests that parse app.json (`sentry-eas-config.test.ts`, `app-json-parity.test.ts`). A reverse-direction check (`Object.keys(appConfig)` ⊆ app.json keys + {extra}) would pin "app.json stays the single declarative source" as an invariant.

- **Surface `expoPublicAppVersion` on the settings diagnostics screen** — `extra.expoPublicAppVersion` now ships in the bundle manifest but nothing reads it yet. A "App version: 1.0.0 (release collectables@<sha>)" row on `app/settings.tsx`, sourced from `expo-constants` + `getSentryStatus().release`, would let testers confirm which build they're on without opening devtools.

- **Sync `ios.buildNumber` from package.json too** — `app.json`'s `ios.buildNumber` is still a hand-maintained `"1.0.0"` that will silently drift from the auto-resolved `version` on the first npm version bump. Either derive it in app.config.ts (e.g. `buildNumber: APP_VERSION`) or add a parity lint so an App Store submission never ships mismatched version/buildNumber.

- **Teach `scripts/sentry-doctor.ts` about the new fallback chain** — the doctor validates release tagging against the deploy workflow; extending it to print the resolved local fallback (`collectables@<package.json version>`) and flag when app.json's vestigial `expo.version` disagrees with package.json would catch confusion before a release goes out under the wrong tag.

- **Deprecate the vestigial `app.json` `expo.version` field** — with app.config.ts overriding it, the static `"1.0.0"` is dead weight that invites "I bumped the version but nothing changed" bugs when someone edits app.json instead of package.json. Either add a comment-adjacent lint (check-appstore-config) asserting the two match, or drop the field from app.json entirely and let the dynamic config own it.

## Analytics payload validation follow-ups (2026-07-10)

- **Extend `assertValidProps` to value-type validation** — the guard now checks *keys* only; a payload passing `hasPrice: "yes"` (string where the schema doc implies boolean) still ships. Adding an optional per-prop type hint to `AnalyticsEventDefinition` (`props: [{ key: "hasPrice", type: "boolean" }]`) would let the same guard catch type drift that breaks Power BI aggregations.

- **Type `trackEvent` payloads per event** — `AnalyticsEventProps<N>` already exists as a literal union; changing `trackEvent`'s signature to `trackEvent<N extends AnalyticsEventName>(name: N, props?: Partial<Record<AnalyticsEventProps<N>, string | number | boolean | null>>)` would move most typo detection from runtime to compile time, making the runtime guard a backstop for casts only.

- **Report prod-stripped keys to Sentry** — a stripped key in production is a shipped bug that nobody sees (console.warn on a user device goes nowhere). Routing the once-per-key warning through `captureException` (or a breadcrumb) would surface "call site X ships undeclared prop Y" in the dashboard with zero user impact.

- **Structural test pinning the validate-before-gates ordering** — the dev-throw behaviour depends on `assertValidProps` running before the `userOptedOut`/`sdk` short-circuits in `trackEvent`; a regex/AST test asserting the call order in `lib/analytics.ts` would stop a well-meaning refactor from silently demoting the guard to enabled-only paths.

- **Reuse the guard in `identifyUser` traits** — traits are just as schema-relevant as event props (PostHog person properties feed the same dashboards), but `identifyUser` currently accepts any `AnalyticsTraits` blob. Declaring an `ANALYTICS_TRAITS` registry and running the same split/warn/strip logic would close the other half of the taxonomy.

## Diagnostics events-taxonomy list follow-ups (2026-07-10)

- **Link each catalog row to its PostHog event definition** — the settings list shows name/description/props; a tap-through that opens `https://<posthog-host>/data-management/events?search=<name>` (admin only, web) would let the operator jump from "what do we track" to "what did we actually receive" in one gesture.

- **Render the catalog on the /privacy page too** — the privacy policy's analytics paragraph promises a bounded event set but doesn't enumerate it. `renderPrivacyPage` could inject the same `getAnalyticsEventCatalog()` rows into a static table at build time, making the public disclosure literally generated from the code that enforces it.

- **Show per-event "last fired" timestamps** — wiring a tiny `recordEventFired(name)` map into `trackEvent` (in-memory, diagnostics only) would upgrade the static catalog into a live "which funnels are actually emitting on this device" debugging panel, mirroring `lastEventSentAt` on the Sentry side.

- **Collapse the catalog behind a search filter once it grows** — at 11 events a flat list is fine; past ~25 the diagnostics card needs a filter input. Adding it early (reusing the currency-sheet query pattern already in settings.tsx) keeps the screen usable as the taxonomy grows.

- **Localise event descriptions via an opt-in map** — descriptions are EN-only by design today; if the GDPR opt-out task ever surfaces them to end users, an optional `descriptionKey` field on `AnalyticsEventDefinition` resolved through `t()` (falling back to the EN string) would let translations arrive incrementally without breaking the schema doc generator.

## Analytics i18n-parity test follow-ups (2026-07-10)

- **Generalise the language-block slicer into a shared test helper** — `languageBlock()` is now copy-pasted across `settings-dsn-inlined-row.test.ts`, `analytics-events-i18n-parity.test.ts` and likely other i18n structural tests; a `__tests__/helpers/i18n-blocks.ts` export would keep the block-boundary regex in one place when the i18n file layout changes.

- **Promote the all-or-none key rule to every `TranslationMap` key** — the parity test guards only `analyticsEventDesc_*`; a generic test asserting `Object.keys(en) === Object.keys(<lang>)` for all 6 blocks (via the TypeScript `TranslationMap` type it already enforces at compile time) would catch a runtime-only drift like a key added through string concatenation.

- **Wire the `analyticsEventDesc_` convention into the schema doc generator** — when a translated description does land, `scripts/generate-powerbi-schema-doc.ts` should prefer the EN i18n string over the taxonomy literal so the docs and the app never disagree about what an event means.

- **Add a lint that the taxonomy descriptions stay ASCII-safe** — descriptions flow into a markdown doc and PostHog metadata; a stray smart-quote or RTL character from a copy-paste would render fine in-app but corrupt the generated doc diff. A 5-line regex test keeps the pipeline clean.

- **Test the diagnostics list against the parity convention** — if `analyticsEventDesc_*` keys ever appear, `app/settings.tsx` should render `t()` strings instead of raw taxonomy text; a structural test asserting the settings screen switches on key presence would complete the loop the parity test starts.

## useAnalytics() hook follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Migrate the eight `trackEvent` screen imports to `useAnalytics().track`** — `app/create.tsx`, `app/create-collection.tsx`, `app/collection/[id].tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`, `app/listing/[id].tsx`, `app/chat/[id].tsx` still import `@/lib/analytics` directly; moving them onto the hook makes the "no direct SDK imports in app/**" rule enforceable and gives every call site the live `optedOut` value for free.

- **Add an import-boundary lint step for `@/lib/analytics` in `app/**`** — once the screens use the hook, a `lint:analytics-imports` scanner (same shape as `lint:hex`) failing on `from "@/lib/analytics"` inside `app/**` (whitelisting `getAnalyticsStatus`/`getAnalyticsEventCatalog` or moving them onto the context too) would pin the boundary permanently.

- **Expose `status` on the context value** — `useAnalytics()` returns `{ identify, reset, track, optedOut }`; adding `status: getAnalyticsStatus()` refreshed on diagnostics flips would let the settings screen drop its module import and render the "events flowing / blocked because X" row purely from the hook.

- **Memoise a no-op context for the opted-out state** — when `optedOut` is true the delegates still call into the module wrappers which no-op per-call; swapping in a frozen no-op value object would make the opt-out contract visible in the React DevTools props and shave the per-call gate walk.

- **Add a fake-dom functional test for the provider value identity** — the structural test pins the memo dependency array textually; a functional test (mounting via the existing `__tests__/helpers/fake-dom.ts` harness) asserting the context value is referentially stable across re-renders with unchanged `diagnosticsEnabled` would catch a future dep-array regression the regex can't see.

## identifyUser debounce follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Flush the pending identify on app-background** — a user who signs in and immediately backgrounds the app within the 500ms window loses the identify until next foreground; an `AppState` listener that flushes (rather than cancels) the pending timer on `background` would close the gap without giving up the debounce.

- **Promote the timer shape into the planned `useDwellTimeEffect` hook** — the debounced-effect-with-cleanup pattern in `AnalyticsProvider` is the same primitive the `chat_opened` dwell tracker and the future `listing_view` event need; when `lib/use-dwell-time.ts` lands, the identify effect should be its first consumer.

- **Make the window env-tunable like the signup freshness window** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_IDENTIFY_DEBOUNCE_MS` (default 500) would let QA set 0 in E2E runs where the test asserts an identify fired synchronously, instead of sprinkling `setTimeout` waits through the harness.

- **Count skipped identifies in the diagnostics snapshot** — incrementing a `debouncedIdentifySkips` counter in the cleanup (when a timer is cancelled with a newer one armed) and surfacing it via the future `getAnalyticsSnapshot()` would quantify how much quota the debounce actually saves.

- **Functional fake-timer test for the collapse behaviour** — the structural test pins the code shape; a node test that stubs `setTimeout`/`clearTimeout` (mock timers via `node:test`'s `mock.timers`) around an extracted pure `scheduleIdentify(...)` helper would assert two rapid trait changes yield exactly one identify call, catching a logic regression the regex can't.

## getAnalyticsSnapshot follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Render the snapshot on the settings diagnostics card** — the helper now exists but nothing consumes it; a "Last identify" row under the existing analytics-status row (formatting `lastIdentifyAt` with the same relative-time helper the chat list uses, traits as `key=value` chips) closes the loop the task opened.

- **Track `lastEventAt`/`lastEventName` the same way** — `trackEvent` has no equivalent bookkeeping, so "are events flowing right now" still requires the PostHog live-events tab; recording the last captured event name + timestamp behind the same defensive-copy contract would make the diagnostics card answer both halves.

- **Expose the snapshot via a `globalThis.__analyticsSnapshot()` devtools global** — `getAnalyticsStatus` is already mirrored as `__analyticsStatus()` from `app/_layout.tsx`; registering the snapshot beside it lets a developer inspect identify state from the web console without navigating to settings.

- **Include a `gatedReason` on skipped identifies** — when an identify is blocked (opt-out, sdk-null, disabled), the snapshot stays silent; recording `lastIdentifySkippedReason` would distinguish "never attempted" from "attempted but gated", which is exactly the ambiguity the diagnostics screen exists to resolve.

- **Persist the snapshot across reloads for web** — an in-memory snapshot resets on every page refresh, so web debugging often races the reload; mirroring the last identify into `sessionStorage` (never `localStorage` — traits are user data) would survive the refresh while still dying with the tab.

## identify-scheduler follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Rewire `AnalyticsProvider` onto the scheduler** — already queued as the next sub-task in `.tasks.md`; the provider's inline setTimeout becomes `scheduler.update(...)` + `dispose()` in cleanup, deleting the duplicated debounce logic.

- **Reuse the scheduler for Sentry user context** — `setSentryUser` in auth-context fires synchronously on every auth change; routing it through a second `createIdentifyScheduler` instance (reset = clear user) would give crash reports the same double-mount protection for free.

- **Add a `flush()` method** — an explicit "fire the pending identify now" hook would let an app-background listener or a pre-navigation hook guarantee the identify lands before the JS thread pauses, complementing the debounce rather than fighting it.

- **Surface pending state** — a `isPending()` accessor would let the future diagnostics snapshot row distinguish "identify sent" from "identify armed but still inside the window", removing a class of "why is lastIdentifyAt null" confusion during dev.

- **Consider trait-diffing** — the scheduler re-identifies even when userId+traits are deep-equal to the last fired call (e.g. an unrelated re-render with a fresh traits object); a shallow-equality skip would cut redundant identifies beyond what the debounce window catches.

## provider-scheduler rewire follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Prune the now-stale "Rewire `AnalyticsProvider` onto the scheduler" suggestion above** — it shipped today; the identify-scheduler follow-ups block still lists it as queued, and a reader scanning suggestions can't tell it's done without cross-checking `.tasks.md`.

- **Flush-on-dispose option** — `dispose()` silently drops a pending identify on unmount; a `createIdentifyScheduler({ ..., flushOnDispose: true })` mode (fire immediately instead of cancel) would let a navigating-away user still be identified, and pairs with the existing `flush()` suggestion.

- **Feed `diagnosticsEnabled` into the scheduler as a gate** — today an identify armed just before the user flips the diagnostics toggle off still fires (the SDK-level opt-out then no-ops it); passing an `isGated()` predicate would stop the timer from even reaching the wrapper, keeping the "nothing leaves this device" promise airtight at the scheduler layer.

- **Type the traits parameter as required at the provider call site** — `scheduler.update(user?.id ?? null, { language, isPremium })` passes traits even for the null branch where they're ignored; an overload (`update(null)` / `update(userId, traits)`) would make the ignored-traits case unrepresentable.

- **Reuse the lazy-ref-scheduler shape for the dwell tracker** — the `useRef<IdentifyScheduler | null>` + lazy-init pattern the provider now uses is exactly what the planned `chat_opened` dwell-time hook needs; extracting a tiny `useLazyRef(create)` helper before the second consumer lands would prevent a copy-paste drift.

## OAuth signup_completed follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Include the `language` prop on the signup event** — the registry already allows `["method", "provider", "language"]` but neither call site sends `language`; threading the active i18n language in (via a small getter on `lib/i18n-context.tsx` or by firing from a component with `useI18n()` access) would let the funnel segment signups by locale from day one.

- **Fire `login_completed` for returning users from the same callback** — the `onAuthStateChange` handler now distinguishes fresh vs returning SIGNED_IN users; the returning branch is currently silent, so DAU-by-auth-method requires PostHog's autocapture. A `login_completed` event with the same `signupEventProps` shape would complete the auth funnel.

- **Persist the seen-set across the OAuth redirect on web** — on web the OAuth flow reloads the page, so the `useRef` seen-set is fresh when the redirected SIGNED_IN arrives; that's exactly the signup we want to catch, but if Supabase re-emits SIGNED_IN after a quick manual reload within the 5-minute window the event double-fires across page loads. Mirroring fired ids into `sessionStorage` (dies with the tab, never `localStorage`) would extend exactly-once across reloads.

- **Unit-test the exactly-once race with a fake auth client** — the structural guards pin both call sites share the set, but a functional test driving a stub `authClient` (emit SIGNED_IN, then resolve verifyOtp for the same fresh user, assert one `trackEvent`) would catch a future regression where one site stops consulting the set; the fake-SDK loader harness from `analytics-init.test.ts` is reusable here.

- **Surface `app_metadata.provider` on the Sentry user context** — `setSentryUser` in the same effect sends only `{ id, email }`; adding the provider tag would let crash triage segment by auth method (OAuth-webview crashes vs OTP), mirroring how the analytics side now derives it.

## signup-freshness-window follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Soft ceiling warning for absurd overrides** — a `EXPO_PUBLIC_SIGNUP_FRESHNESS_WINDOW_MS=86400000` (24h) override would count every same-day OTP login as a signup; mirroring the profile-TTL's `isBelowRecommendedNumericEnv` with an `isAboveRecommendedNumericEnv(raw, 3_600_000)` one-shot warning would flag staging configs that leaked into production.

- **Extract a pure `lib/numeric-env.ts`** — `resolveNumericEnv` lives in `lib/env.ts`, which imports react-native `Platform`, so node-pure modules (auth-helpers today, future tunables) must have the resolved value threaded in from a react module; moving the parser family into a pure module (env.ts re-exports) would let pure modules read their own env vars and make the parser functionally testable instead of regex-pinned.

- **Document the staging recipe in APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md** — README-DEPLOY covers the web deploy, but a TestFlight staging build widening the window needs the `eas secret:create` line; adding it (or an explicit "web-only tunable" note) keeps the iOS path from silently missing the knob.

- **Fire a `signup_window_widened` diagnostic trait** — when the resolved window differs from the default, attaching `signupWindowMs` as a super-property (or an identify trait) would let analysts exclude staging-widened sessions from the production signup funnel instead of discovering the skew after the fact.

- **Reuse the window for the `login_completed` counterpart** — the suggested returning-user login event (OAuth follow-ups above) needs the same "fresh vs returning" boundary; deriving both from `SIGNUP_FRESHNESS_WINDOW_MS` keeps the funnel arms mutually exclusive by construction.

## time-helpers follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Adopt `isWithinDuration` in `premium-helpers.ts`** — `lib/premium-helpers.ts` rolls its own `Date.parse(stamp)` / `Date.parse(expiresAt) <= now` arithmetic for trial/expiry checks; the expiry comparison is the inverse predicate, so adding an `isExpired(iso, now?)` sibling (or `hasElapsed`) to `lib/time-helpers.ts` and migrating both call sites would finish the consolidation the task started.

- **Add a `clampDurationMs` guard** — a negative `durationMs` silently returns false for everything; validating (or clamping to 0) with a dev-mode warning would surface caller bugs like a ms/seconds mixup at the source instead of as "the event never fires".

- **Promote the ISO-parse-or-null shape too** — `analytics-mirror-payload.ts`, `subscriptions.ts`, and `sync-cursors.ts` each re-roll `Date.parse` + `Number.isFinite`/`isNaN` guards into slightly different fallbacks; a shared `parseIsoMs(iso): number | null` would make those three parsers one-liners and unify the "invalid timestamp" contract.

- **Relative-time formatting counterpart** — `app/settings.tsx` formats "last sent 3 hours ago" via `formatRelativeDate`; documenting (or re-homing) the render-side helper next to the predicate side in `lib/time-helpers.ts` would give future "X minutes ago" features one obvious module to look in.

- **Property-style boundary tests** — the suite pins the inclusive boundaries by example; a small loop over window sizes (0, 1ms, 1s, 5min, 24h) asserting `isWithinDuration(new Date(now - w).toISOString(), w, now) === true` and `w+1` false would harden the off-by-ms contract the task called out, for a few lines of test code.

## __simulateSignupEvent devtools follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Extend the simulator to every taxonomy event** — `__simulateSignupEvent()` covers one event; a `__simulateAnalyticsEvent(name)` sibling that validates `name` against `getAnalyticsEventCatalog()` and fires `{ method: "manual_test" }`-style marker props would let a developer smoke-test any funnel arm (listing_created, chat_opened) from the console without driving the UI.

- **Filter `manual_test` events out of Power BI** — the synthetic event lands in the production PostHog project when fired from a dev build pointed at real keys; documenting a `properties.method != 'manual_test'` filter in `docs/powerbi-connection.md` (or a saved PostHog cohort) keeps the signup funnel numerator honest.

- **Surface the returned status in the dev menu** — tapping "Simulate signup event" in expo-dev-menu discards the `AnalyticsStatus` return; routing it through a toast (`useToast` is available at the layout) would give on-device testers the same which-gate-blocked-it feedback console callers get.

- **Pin the gate-order parity with a shared test** — the fixed `getAnalyticsStatus`/`getSentryStatus` now both walk `user-opted-out` before `ready`, but the two reason-walks are hand-mirrored; a structural test that diffs the two functions' gate order (or a shared `walkTelemetryGates` helper both consume) would stop the next stack (Clarity status?) from reintroducing the opted-out-but-ready lie.

- **Reset the rate limiter from the dev menu** — a burst of simulator calls can exhaust the 200/min `trackEvent` window and make subsequent real-interaction testing silently drop events; a "Reset analytics rate limit" dev-menu action wrapping `__resetAnalyticsRateLimitForTests` (renamed for dual use) would un-wedge a testing session without an app restart.

## useTransitionEvent follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Adopt the hook for `friend_request_accepted`** — the pending social-funnel task ("fire when `incoming && outgoing` flips to friend") is exactly the render-derived false→true edge `useTransitionEvent` was built for; wiring `useTransitionEvent(relationship === "friend", () => trackEvent(...))` in the profile screen would be its first real consumer and prove the mount-baseline contract.

- **Falling-edge sibling** — churn events (`last_photo_removed`, `listing_unpublished`) need the true→false direction; an `isFallingEdge(prev, next)` + optional `direction` param on the hook keeps both edges in one module instead of a future `use-falling-edge.ts` twin.

- **Debounced variant for flappy sources** — a realtime-driven boolean (peer online, sync status) can flap across renders and spam fire(); composing the hook with the planned `useDwellTimeEffect` primitive (fire only if the state holds for ≥ms) would make it safe for connection-state funnels.

- **Count-threshold generalisation** — "first photo" is `count > 0`, but "power user" funnels ("added 10th item", "5th collection") are the same shape with a different threshold; a `useCountThresholdEvent(count, threshold, fire)` wrapper delegating to `isRisingEdge(prevCount >= t, count >= t)` would cover them without new edge logic.

- **Structural adoption lint** — once 2-3 call sites exist, a grep-based test asserting no `app/**` file re-rolls `!hadXBefore &&`-style inline edge gates (the pattern `/!\w+Before\s*&&/` outside lib/) would keep future funnels on the shared predicate the same way the design-token and env-inlining lints enforce their conventions.

## item_photos_replaced follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Track the removal edge too** — `hasReplacedPhotoSet` deliberately excludes some→none, so photo removals are still invisible; an `item_photos_removed` sibling (fired when `previousPhotos.length > 0 && finalPhotos.length === 0`) would complete the attach/replace/remove triple and let Power BI separate curation from abandonment.

- **Carry a `delta` prop** — `photoCount` alone can't distinguish "swapped one of five" from "replaced the whole gallery"; adding `added`/`removed` counts (cheap to derive from the two sets inside the helper) would let analysts size rotation depth without raw photo data.

- **Move the create-flow `hasPhoto` derivation into analytics-helpers** — `app/create.tsx` still hand-rolls `uploadedPhotos.length > 0` for `item_added.hasPhoto`; now that `lib/analytics-helpers.ts` exists, the planned `summarisePayload(item)` booleans have an obvious home and the first migration is one line.

- **Dedupe URIs inside the helper** — a photo array with duplicate URIs (possible after a re-upload race) makes the length comparison overcount; normalising both sides to `new Set(...)` sizes first would make the predicate immune to duplicates for two extra lines.

- **Cross-event funnel test** — a structural test asserting the attach and replace events share the same `itemId`/`collectionId` prop names (registry-level parity) would keep the two arms joinable in Power BI if either payload is ever renamed.

## buildCollectionAnalyticsProps follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Adopt the builder for the edit path** — `app/collection/[id].tsx`'s edit gate fires `premium_upsell_shown` but a successful visibility/cover edit emits nothing; a `collection_updated` event built with the same helper would show whether users curate collections post-create, with zero new payload logic.

- **Backfill hasCover into item_added** — `item_added.hasPhoto` and `collection_created.hasCover` are the same "media attached at create" concept with two names; documenting the pairing in the registry descriptions (or renaming one at the next taxonomy version bump) keeps Power BI slices consistent across the two funnels.

- **Type the builder's return against the registry** — the new lock-step test catches drift at runtime; typing the return as `Record<AnalyticsEventProps<"collection_created">, string | boolean>` would catch it at compile time instead, using the literal-union machinery already exported by analytics-events.

- **Visibility source-of-truth guard** — the create screen clamps `visibility` → `finalVisibility` for free users before both save and event; lifting that clamp into a pure `resolveCollectionVisibility(requested, isPremium)` helper beside the builder would let the event, the save, and future server-side validation share one rule.

- **Cover-upload failure telemetry** — `uploadImage(coverPhoto)` failures currently surface only as a thrown save error; catching specifically the cover-upload step and firing an `image_upload_failed` event (provider, byte size bucket) would explain "created without cover" rates in the dashboard.

## analytics-imports lint follow-ups (2026-07-11)

- **Generalise into a module-boundary lint** — the scanner hard-codes one specifier; a config array of `{ module, allowedImporters, hint }` rules (analytics-events today, `@/lib/supabase-admin` or `posthog-react-native` tomorrow) would turn it into a general "screens must go through the wrapper" boundary enforcement with one more rule being one line.

- **Promote stripComments to a shared lib/source-scan.ts** — three lint modules now import it from `lib/env-inlining.ts`, which is an odd home for a generic tokenizer; moving it (with a re-export shim for the old path) would make the next scanner's provenance obvious.

- **Scan lib/ for reverse leaks** — the gate covers UI→taxonomy, but a future `lib/analytics-events.ts` importing a React Native module would break the node-pure contract the docs tooling relies on; a companion assertion (no react/react-native imports inside the taxonomy) closes the other direction.

- **Wire the CLI into a pre-commit hook** — the scan takes ~100ms; running it from a husky/pre-commit config alongside lint:peer-dep-free would surface the violation before the push instead of at CI time.

- **Report the byte cost** — when the gate fails, printing the taxonomy module's current source size ("this import drags ~6KB of descriptions into the bundle") would make the failure self-justifying to a contributor who hits it cold.

## marketplace purchase-funnel integration follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Promote the stub marketplace into a shared test harness** — `createStubMarketplace` in the funnel test re-implements `addListing`/`markListingSold` on the real pure helpers; extracting it to `__tests__/helpers/stub-marketplace.ts` would let future integration tests (listing_dropped funnel, seller-notification flow) reuse the same node-side provider stand-in instead of re-rolling it.

- **Extract the provider's addListing/markListingSold cores into marketplace-helpers** — the stub mirrors the provider's inline logic (trade-mode price clamp, already-sold guard); lifting `buildDraftListing(input, userId, now)` and `applyListingSale(listings, id, buyerId, soldAt)` into `lib/marketplace-helpers.ts` would let the provider AND the stub call one implementation, so the integration test exercises the literal production transitions.

- **Walk the abandon arm in the same harness** — a companion `listing_created` vs `listing_dropped` integration (publish one draft, abandon another) would pin that one sheet session emits exactly one of the two events, the mutual-exclusion property the structural tests only check per call site.

- **Assert funnel joinability in the Power BI doc** — the schema doc lists both events but nothing verifies the shared `mode` column is documented as the join key; a doc test asserting both event sections name `mode` with identical value domains would keep the report join stable.

- **Cover the realtime seller-notification arm** — `isListingClaimedFromOwner` is unit-tested, but no integration walks publish → remote claim echo → seller prompt queue; the stub harness plus a simulated realtime UPDATE payload would cover the cross-device half of the funnel.

## listing_view + use-dwell-time follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Adopt useDwellTimeEffect for profile_view / collection_view** — the two remaining surfaces the hook's doc comment names; each is now a ~6-line addition (registry entry + one hook call) and together they complete the engagement-funnel triple (view → follow/friend, view → item browse).

- **Thread the actual dwell duration into the payload** — a `dwellBucket` prop ("0.5-2s" / "2-10s" / "10s+") captured by firing a second timer would separate glance-views from deep reads; conversion analysis on listing_view currently treats both identically.

- **listing_view → listing_claimed session join** — PostHog auto-captures session ids, but a doc note (or a Power BI SQL equivalent in `docs/bi-sql-equivalents.md`) showing the view-to-buy conversion query would make the new denominator immediately usable by whoever builds the dashboard.

- **Guard against double-fire on remote fetch** — `listing?.id` flips undefined → id when `fetchListingById` resolves, re-arming the dwell timer once; if a future refactor makes the listing object identity unstable (e.g. re-normalising on every realtime echo), keying on a stable string id keeps it safe — a structural test pinning the deps array shape would catch a regression to `[listing]`.

- **Migrate the typing-indicator debounce onto a shared timer primitive** — `app/chat/[id].tsx` still hand-rolls `typingTimerRef` (`TYPING_DEBOUNCE_MS`); it's throttle-shaped rather than dwell-shaped, so a sibling `useThrottledCallback` in the same `lib/use-dwell-time.ts` module would centralise the remaining raw setTimeout usage in screens.

## friend_request_accepted funnel follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Add the `friend_request_cancelled` arm from the same diff effect** — the sibling task already queued in `.tasks.md` can reuse `diffAcceptedFriendships`'s shape: a `diffWithdrawnRequests(prev, next, userId)` (outgoing-only in prev, absent in next, never mutual in between) fired from the same baseline-ref effect completes the sent → accepted | cancelled funnel with one more pure helper.

- **Carry a `pendingForMs` latency bucket on friend_request_accepted** — time-to-accept ("<1h" / "1-24h" / ">24h") is the classic social-graph health metric; it needs a `createdAt` on the request edge (today `FriendRequest` is direction-only), so the cloud `friend_requests` table's existing timestamp would have to survive the `RemoteFriendRequest` mapping — a small coercer extension plus one bucket helper.

- **Fire a `first_friend_added` transition via useTransitionEvent** — `useTransitionEvent` (built for exactly this) can watch `friends.length > 0` in social-context and fire once per account when the graph goes 0 → 1, the activation milestone Power BI needs for the social-onboarding funnel; the per-account baseline concern is already solved by the pattern shipped in this task.

- **Dedupe accepted events across devices in reports** — the diff effect fires on whichever of the accepter's devices observes the transition first; if the user runs two devices, both may see the half→mutual flip and double-report `accepted_by_me`. PostHog-side dedupe on (distinct_id, targetUserId) is enough today, but a doc note in `docs/powerbi-connection.md` (or an insert-id-style event key) would keep the funnel counts honest.

- **Promote the baseline-ref transition pattern into a `usePrevious`-style hook** — `friendRequestsBaselineRef` in social-context and `prevIsPremium` in bottom-nav both hand-roll "compare against the last committed snapshot, keyed to an owner id"; a `useAccountScopedPrevious(value, accountId)` hook in `lib/use-transition-event.ts` would make the next diff-driven event (collection shares, follower counts) a two-liner.

## friend_request_cancelled follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Surface the decline arm as `friend_request_declined`** — `classifyRequestRemoval` already returns `declined_request` when the user dismisses an incoming request; registering the sibling event is now a three-line change (union + registry + one gate branch) and completes the receiver-side funnel: received → accepted | declined.

- **Track `friend_removed` for mutual unfriends** — the `unfriended` classification is silent today, but graph-shrinkage is the strongest churn predictor; a `friend_removed` event with a `friendshipAgeDays` bucket (needs a `createdAt` on the request edge) would let Power BI cohort "friendships that dissolve within a week".

- **Detect remote declines via the diff effect** — when the counterpart declines MY request on their device, the realtime refetch silently drops my outgoing edge; a `diffWithdrawnHandshakes(prev, next, userId)` sibling to `diffAcceptedFriendships` could classify outgoing-only → absent transitions as `request_declined_remotely`, closing the last invisible funnel exit (the "expired" arm).

- **Assert funnel completeness in a structural test** — a taxonomy test asserting the three `friend_request_*` events keep prop-schema parity (same `targetUserId` join key, no accidental extra props on one arm) would keep the funnel joinable as arms get added; today the pin lives in the cancelled test only.

- **Move the two hasRequest snapshot reads into social-helpers** — `addFriend` (alreadyRequested/isAccept) and `removeFriend` (hadOutgoing/hadIncoming) both read the same pair of directions; a `handshakeStateWith(requests, userId, profileId): { outgoing, incoming }` helper would collapse four `hasRequest` calls into two call sites and give the classifier a single canonical input shape.

## premium_activated.source intent-ref follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Tag the collection-edit upsell path** — `app/collection/[id].tsx` fires `premium_upsell_shown` with `source: "collection_edit"` but still refuses with a toast instead of surfacing `PremiumUpsellSheet`; swapping the toast for the sheet with `source="collection_edit"` (added to `PremiumIntentSource`) would both lift conversion and complete the funnel join on that surface.

- **Compute upsell→activation conversion per source in the Power BI doc** — both events now share source vocabularies; a documented DAX/SQL snippet joining `premium_upsell_shown.source` to `premium_activated.source` within a session would turn the new tagging into the ranking the task wanted.

- **Assert source-vocabulary parity structurally** — a test walking every `premium_upsell_shown` call site's `source` literal and asserting it is (or maps to) a `PremiumIntentSource` member would stop the two vocabularies drifting as new gated surfaces appear.

- **Persist the intent across the OAuth/paywall detour** — if a future real-payment flow redirects out of the app, the in-memory ref dies with the session; parking the intent in AsyncStorage (`premium-intent-v1`, TTL ~1h) before hand-off and consuming it in the post-payment `server_sync` merge would keep attribution through Stripe/RevenueCat round-trips.

- **Fire `premium_cancelled` with the same intent pattern** — `cancelPremium()` is untracked today; mirroring the source ref (`settings` is currently the only cancel surface) plus a `daysActive` bucket derived from `activatedAt` would give churn dashboards the retention arm.

## RADIUS_PILL migration follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Fold the remaining batches' counts into the adoption registry as they land** — `__tests__/radius-pill-adoption.test.ts`'s `MIGRATED_FILES` list is the running ledger; batches 2-5 should append their files in the same commit as the swap so the guard and the migration can never be a commit apart.

- **Sweep `borderRadius: 9999` and `borderRadius: 100` look-alikes** — a quick grep shows only 999 is idiomatic today, but RN codebases commonly grow 9999/100 pill variants; the future lint:radius matcher should flag any literal ≥100 in a borderRadius, not just exactly 999.

- **Consider `RADIUS_PILL` adoption in JSX inline styles** — the batches target StyleSheet blocks; a follow-up grep for `style={{...borderRadius: 999...}}` inline objects (rare but possible in chips rendered conditionally) would close the same backdoor the hex scanner closed for JSX color literals.

- **Extend dev tokens-preview with the geometry family** — `app/dev/tokens-preview` (if present per the suggestions backlog) shows the palette; adding a row of pill/card/input radius samples would give designers the same one-glance audit for geometry that colors already have.

- **Batch the gap-token migration with the same registry pattern** — the `gap: 10/12/8` → `SPACING_LIST/CARD/INLINE` parent task (138 occurrences) can copy the exact per-batch + adoption-registry shape proven here, incl. shipping its scanner last.

## RADIUS_PILL batch 2 follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Dedupe the pill-button style recipe in `app/wishlist.tsx`** — several of the swapped styles (`addButton`, sheet action chips, promote-target rows) share the same `borderRadius: RADIUS_PILL` + horizontal-padding + row-center shape; a local `pillButton` base style spread into each variant would shrink the StyleSheet and make future geometry tweaks single-point.

- **Unify the avatar-circle radius in `app/profile/[id].tsx`** — the avatar and its edit-badge both use pill radii on square boxes to make circles; a `RADIUS_CIRCLE` alias (same 999 value, different intent) would let the future lint:radius scanner distinguish "pill on a rectangle" from "circle on a square" and document the two idioms in `lib/design-tokens.ts`.

- **Pin per-file occurrence counts in the adoption registry** — `MIGRATED_FILES` asserts zero leftovers but not how many `RADIUS_PILL` usages exist; recording the expected count per file (`{ rel, count }`) would catch a refactor that silently deletes a pill style while keeping the import alive.

- **Migrate `borderRadius: RADIUS_PILL` on `overflow: "hidden"` image wrappers to a shared `circleImage(size)` helper** — profile avatar / wishlist thumbnails hand-roll width+height+radius trios; a 5-line helper returning the trio from one `size` argument removes the drift risk between width and height that breaks the circle.

- **Run batches 3-5 back-to-back in one session if token budget allows** — the recipe is now mechanical (import + sed swap + registry append); merging the three remaining batches into one commit each but a single PR would cut merge/CI overhead by ~3× and let the lint:radius scanner land the same day the tree greps clean.

## lint:radius scanner follow-ups (2026-07-12)

- **Generalize the trio into a `lint:geometry` multi-literal gate** — the scanner currently guards only `borderRadius: 999`; once the RADIUS_CARD (22) / RADIUS_CARD_LG (24) and gap-token migrations land, extend `INLINE_RADIUS_PATTERN` into a table of `{pattern, token}` pairs so one scanner (and one CI step) covers the whole geometry family.

- **Share the directory walker between the three scanner CLIs** — `check-inline-hex.ts`, `check-analytics-imports.ts`, and `check-inline-radius.ts` each carry a private ~15-line recursive walker; a `lib/walk-sources.ts` helper would deduplicate them and give future scanners one import.

- **Emit GitHub annotations from the radius scanner too** — the `::error file=…,line=…::` upgrade already suggested for lint:hex applies verbatim here; doing both in one pass would make all geometry/palette findings click-through on PR diffs.

- **Fold the `radius-pill-adoption` registry's tree-clean role into the scanner test** — the adoption test pins 22 files' history; now that lint:radius owns the tree-wide guard, a comment cross-linking the two (scanner = future, registry = provenance + dead-import guard) prevents someone deleting one thinking it duplicates the other.

- **Add `lint:radius` to the pre-push husky hook if one ever lands** — the repo relies on CI to catch violations; a local git hook running the fast scanners (hex, radius, analytics-imports — all <1s) would shorten the feedback loop without the full lint:ci cost.
